## [assistant 414]
I treated file 1’s unique Part 2 as the only payload to turn into recommendations. I used the shared preamble only to understand naming and cross-cutting context, then checked the concrete Part‑2 claims against the uploaded code snapshot where possible. The file identifies itself as “file 1 of 6” and says the unique payload is the 14 subagent outputs after the divider, which is the scope I kept to. fileciteturn2file5

One caveat: I could verify many file/path claims against the uploaded `polylogue-all` code snapshot, but I did not have the live `/realm/project/polylogue` tree or the original `/tasks/*.output` files. For anything that depends on the current branch after July 5, the code should be re-opened before patching.

## Executive verdict

The strongest parts of this file are real and important: honesty-audit completeness, recursive-safety, FTS coherence, query/finding objects, and the idea of Polylogue becoming a producer of external standards rather than only a consumer of exports. Those should survive.

The weakest parts are where the designs talk as if a content hash, Merkle root, `AssertionKind`, or generated variant magically solves more than it does. Merkle roots do not give membership queries. New assertion kinds are schema-free at SQLite level but not free at surface/schema/audit level. Mechanical variants are not necessarily faithful. Query canonicalization must be conservative because ranking, lanes, time, macros, and implicit defaults can make superficially equivalent expressions non-equivalent.

My prioritized take: land safety and honesty first, then query/finding objects, then FTS/ingest invariants, then interop/export surfaces. Do not build the large measure catalog or evidence cockpit before the substrate produces one or two citable, regenerated findings.

## Confirmed hard problems

The honesty-audit incompleteness is real. The current registry has more number-bearing insight products than the rigor matrix covers, and the audit path iterates the contracts rather than reconciling against the registry. That means an insight product with no contract can disappear from the audit instead of showing `coverage_status=uncovered`. The payload’s proposed fix is right: iterate the product registry, emit explicit uncovered rows, and make number-over-empty and text-derived provenance checks executable rather than prose. The unique file-1 material names the uncovered cost/coverage/tool/debt cluster and the contract iteration failure directly. fileciteturn2file17

The temporal provenance bug is also real. The aggregate high-water mark classifier collapses input provenance toward `provider_ts` instead of propagating the weakest contributing source. The correction should be stronger than “fix one helper”: the leaf classifier also needs audit because any aggregate fix built over already-laundered leaf values is only half a fix. The file-1 material itself calls out that risk. fileciteturn2file2

The forensic transform honesty problem is real. The code distinguishes tool-result exit status from prose-derived artifacts for some axes, but commit SHAs, decisions, caveats, and similar fields can still be mined from prose without being carried as `text_derived` or unverified. The design direction is correct: payload models, not just bundle prose, must expose which fields are structural evidence and which are text-derived inference. fileciteturn2file17

The recursive-safety diagnosis is confirmed and should be treated as a top-tier safety bug, not a nice-to-have. The durable `assertions` table already has `author_kind`, `status`, `evidence_refs_json`, and `context_policy_json`; candidate promotion already flips judged rows to `author_kind='user'`; but the injection gate does not require `author_kind='user'`, does not resolve material-origin grounding, and can therefore let agent-authored active rows become future context if any write path stamps them incorrectly. The payload identifies this as the self-ingesting archive’s laundering failure mode: auto-captured R&D can become assertions, then future context, without a human or external grounding break. fileciteturn2file0

The `blackboard_post` class of bug is particularly plausible: if any path calls `upsert_assertion` with `author_kind=agent`, `status=ACTIVE`, and `inject:true`, the current central write layer will accept it unless guarded upstream. The right fix is a single `upsert_assertion` chokepoint coercing every non-user author to `CANDIDATE` plus `inject:false`, while preserving terminal judged rows. This exact invariant is also surfaced in the shared later-wave bug list, but it belongs here because the recursive-safety Part‑2 payload makes it operational. fileciteturn2file1

The FTS coherence design is grounded. The rowid identity `messages_fts.rowid == blocks.rowid == messages_fts_docsize.id` is the keystone, and the current ledger/repair path is a real substrate to build on. The proposed metamorphic testing strategy is unusually good: generate block insert/update/delete sequences through the real write path, assert no missing/excess rows, test empty-text transitions, repair convergence, and ledger-vs-exact agreement. fileciteturn2file13

The FTS risk section is also correct and sharper than the average design note. Rowid reuse means a ghost FTS row can accidentally bind to a different block; count agreement alone is insufficient. The coherence check must join on rowid and confirm `block_id`. Ledger-only O(1) checks are acceptable for startup and Prometheus, but periodic exact reconciliation remains necessary because the ledger can be the thing that drifted. fileciteturn2file10

The query/finding-object gap is real. The current object-ref vocabulary has saved views, recall packs, assertions, transforms, runs, context snapshots, observed events, and similar objects, but no first-class `query`, `result_set`, or `finding`. Saved queries are still mutable names / saved-view assertions, not stable query identities. The file-1 model—`query:<hash>`, result-set snapshots, query DAG, `FINDING` lifecycle, findings-as-tests—is the right architecture. fileciteturn2file4

The standing-query design is pointed in the right direction. A standing query should be a saved query with notification/delta semantics and should write candidate findings or query-delta assertions rather than directly notifying as truth. The payload is correct that dedup should be by stable identity sets, not raw events, because re-ingest storms should not generate repeated notifications for the same underlying finding. fileciteturn2file13

The triage frontier is a plausible and useful read-model. The proposed score uses existing `session_profiles`, terminal/workflow weights, logical-session collapse, gates, and read-time staleness. The key correction in the payload is right: hard-zero only truly disposable sessions; in-flight and superseded branches should be visible demotions, not hidden drops. fileciteturn2file12

## Refuted or corrected points

“Add `AssertionKind.FINDING` with no migration” is true only at the SQLite-table level. The durable table stores `kind` as text, so a new kind does not require a user-tier DDL migration. But the project embeds assertion kinds into OpenAPI, CLI output schemas, user-audit surfaces, and tests. The file itself notes those gotchas, and the bead work must include them; otherwise the change will pass storage and fail surfaces. fileciteturn2file12

The query-hash canonicalization rule is too broad if read literally. `auth and test` can commute only inside a pure Boolean predicate fragment. A full Polylogue query can include ranking, retrieval lanes, semantic/FTS/hybrid policy, limits, time-relative predicates, projection/render defaults, macros, set-algebra operand order, and future stage metadata. The safe canonicalization rule is: normalize pure predicate ASTs conservatively, but do not commute operations that affect rank, cost, scope, or time semantics.

The Merkle-root recommendation is half right. A Merkle root over sorted member keys is excellent for change detection and cheap equality testing. It is not sufficient for “cheap intersect/except membership.” To compute intersections, diffs, or example rows, Polylogue needs either `result_set_members`, a compressed membership structure, or a re-executable query. The right storage split is metadata + Merkle root for every snapshot, and exact member rows only for capped/saved/promoted snapshots that need dereference, citation, or set operations.

“Result sets belong in derived index.db” is right for ordinary snapshots, but not for every user-facing result. A result set referenced by a promoted finding must either be reproducible from durable query+corpus hash or have a durable citation manifest sufficient to explain what was cited after a derived reset. The durable object is not the whole member table; it is the decision/finding plus its evidence anchors and the query/result fingerprint.

The standing-query substrate should not ship before query identity and finding identity exist. Saved-view plus `notify_on` JSON is a good migration path, but stable no-storm semantics depend on stable query IDs, stable result-set/finding IDs, and content-hash anchors. Without those, a standing query can still be an event replay notifier dressed as a finding detector.

The CIF/polylogue-export direction is correct, but `polylogue-export` must preserve two identities at once: the embedded original origin and the fact that the transport envelope itself came from Polylogue. Re-ingesting `export(A)` should be idempotent relative to the original content, but the archive must not lose provenance that the bytes came through a Polylogue export package. The package needs an envelope identity, source manifest, origin-specific parser fingerprint, content hash algorithm, and collision policy.

The mechanical-vs-generative variant axis is useful, but “mechanical” cannot mean “trusted 100%.” OCR can be wrong; transliteration can be lossy; language detection can be ambiguous; captions can omit critical content. Mechanical should mean “deterministic or non-generative transform with measurable coverage/confidence,” not “truth-equivalent.”

The RL/eval export lane is good, but it must stay conservative. The action stream gives strong structural labels for tool outcomes, but reward modeling over corrections is weak if corrections remain session-scoped. Any AUC/accuracy report must include base rate, `n`, correction granularity, and coverage. The file’s warning to verify the live Atropos schema first is necessary: Atropos is a moving RL trajectory/evaluation framework, and recent releases reference format fixes around nested messages and `jsonl2html.py`, so a pinned round-trip test is mandatory. citeturn194146search1turn194146search0

The measure catalog should not be allowed to become a museum. The 5-tuple algebra is the right product shape, but the first implementation should be a registry and single aggregate path for a small number of live measures: count, cost-per-outcome, tool-error recovery latency, retry storm, and maybe delegation yield. The full 16-measure catalog should be backfilled only after the registry proves it prevents lies and reduces duplicate implementation.

## External context and missing prior art

For query/findings-as-objects, the closest product analogues are semantic metric layers and data-quality checks, not just saved searches. dbt’s Semantic Layer centralizes metric definitions so metrics are consistently interpreted across tools, and MetricFlow generates SQL for metrics over dimensions; Cube likewise models measures as aggregate definitions such as sum/count/average/rolling windows. Polylogue’s measure registry should steal that split: metric definition is centralized, query execution is generated, and surfaces are not allowed to invent their own denominator. citeturn117276search4turn117276search0turn117276search1

For construct-validity gates, Dagster asset checks and Great Expectations checkpoints are relevant patterns: they turn quality expectations into executable checks attached to data assets. Polylogue’s twist is stronger evidence semantics: a number is invalid not merely because a check fails, but because its backing rows are missing, text-derived, stale, or using the wrong unit frame. citeturn117276search3turn117276search2

For citation anchors and report baskets, the W3C Web Annotation Data Model is directly relevant. It is designed to share and reuse annotations across systems, including linking arbitrary content and selected segments. Polylogue should not copy the model wholesale, but the `target/body/selector/state` vocabulary is useful when designing evidence baskets, content anchors, variant alignments, and external report exports. citeturn493599search2turn493599search6

For interop outputs, SARIF is the obvious standard for exporting pathologies or agent-behavior defects into GitHub/code-scanning style surfaces. SARIF is an OASIS standard format for static-analysis results; a Polylogue “agent pathology as SARIF” export is a low-cost way to make its findings visible in existing developer workflows. citeturn493599search1turn493599search13

For MCP, the Part‑2 idea that sessions/messages/blocks should become resources and recall packs/saved views should become prompts is aligned with the protocol’s own primitive split. MCP resources are application-controlled contextual data identified by URIs, with optional subscriptions/list-changed support; prompts are reusable prompt templates/instructions exposed by servers. That maps neatly to Polylogue: sessions and evidence packs are resources, recall packs and saved analysis recipes are prompts, and mutations/search remain tools. citeturn799248search0turn493599search4

For OpenTelemetry interop, the right lesson is not “export everything as OTel.” OpenTelemetry semantic conventions define shared meanings for attributes, metric instruments, units, and spans; the GenAI conventions already include provider/model/tool/evaluation-oriented attributes. Polylogue should import/export selected spans/events where useful, while preserving its richer archive-specific evidence model internally. citeturn493599search3turn493599search15

## Strategic synthesis

The file’s real center of gravity is not “more features.” It is a transition from archive search to evidence-bearing analytical objects.

The correct product ladder is:

raw sessions and artifacts → typed units → query objects → result relations → findings/assertions → standing rechecks → evidence reports.

Honesty-audit, recursive-safety, FTS coherence, ingestion fidelity, CIF/export, variants, evidence cockpit, RL export, and the measure catalog all fit that ladder. Anything that does not fit should be treated as optional interop or demo polish.

The first thing to land is the safety/honesty substrate. Agent-authored assertions must not self-inject. Every number-bearing insight product must either have a rigor contract or emit `uncovered`. Text-derived fields must be typed as text-derived. Weakest temporal provenance must propagate. FTS drift must become a measured, tested invariant rather than a boolean readiness hope.

The second thing is query/finding identity. Without `query:<hash>` and result/finding objects, standing queries, evidence reports, findings-as-tests, live recall packs, and analysis recipes all lack stable handles.

The third thing is ingestion and citation stability. `polylogue-export`, CIF, block content hashes, parser fingerprints, raw fidelity, and content variants are not side quests; they make later claims reproducible. But they should be staged so the initial proof artifact can ship.

The fourth thing is external surfaces: SARIF, git notes, MCP resources/prompts, `.well-known/ai-sessions`, Datasette/SQLite publication. These are useful because they make Polylogue’s results legible outside Polylogue. They are not a substitute for the internal proof path.

## Prioritized take

Priority 0: safety and lies. Harden `upsert_assertion`, the inject gate, generated-context-pack exclusion, rigor coverage, text-derived fields, weakest-source propagation, and FTS exact-vs-ledger drift. These are credibility issues.

Priority 1: object identity. Add `query`, `result_set`, and `finding` refs; conservative canonical query hashing; result-set metadata/member storage; content-hash evidence qualifiers; re-runnable findings.

Priority 2: standing analysis. Saved queries with `notify_on`, delta findings, finding drift, triage frontier, and analysis/evidence packs should all build on the object identity layer.

Priority 3: standards and interop. CIF/polylogue-export, SARIF, MCP resources/prompts, git notes, and web evidence cockpit are valuable after stable evidence refs exist.

Priority 4: broad measure catalog, variants, RL export, and “champion the standard” campaigns. These are high upside but should not displace the first citable finding and proof loop.

## [user 307]
You are a senior engineer + technical strategist reviewing R&D for Polylogue, a local, single-writer, cross-provider archive for AI coding/chat sessions (split-tier SQLite: durable source/user, rebuildable index/embeddings, disposable ops; query-first CLI + MCP + daemon). The attached file has two parts: Part 1 is a master synthesis (shared context, identical across 6 sibling files — do not base deliverables on it, use it only to understand the whole); Part 2 is this file's unique slice of ~15 subagent design specs. Five sibling files hold the rest; your outputs must stay disjoint from theirs, so anchor everything you produce to Part 2.

Do three things.

1. Vet, hard. Adversarially verify the Part-2 specs — especially the conclusions: bug diagnoses (are the file:line claims and failure modes
real and correctly characterized?), the tier/regime/schsments, and any strategic or prioritization verdicts.Separate what you confirm, refute, and extend/correct, with reasoning. Then research around it: use your own knowledge and web search for
prior art, competing approaches, relevant standards/libure patterns, and anything the specs assume but don'tjustify. Bring in what's missing; challenge what's overconfident. Note where you'd need to read live source to be sure.
2. Write a self-contained analysis. Produce one coherenontains all the value in this file's material plus yourvetting and research — written so a reader who never se Restate and own the substance; never say "the specclaims" or reference the attachment. Organize it well (themes, confirmed problems, design decisions and their tradeoffs, your corrections, external context, open questions, a prioritized take). Be opinionated and concrete; preserve the sharp specifics (numbers, file paths,       mechanisms, risks) rather than abstracting them away.

      "acceptance_criteria": ["observable, checkable ...", ...],
      "dependencies": ["polylogue-<extant>", "p<N>-0X"],   // extant bead ids and/or sibling proposed ids
      "parent": "polylogue-<epic>|p<N>-0X|null",
      "risks": ["top 1-3"],
      "confidence": "high|med|low",             // after your vetting
      "provenance": "one line: which finding/recommendaacts"
    }
  ]
}

Rules for the bead set: use real extant Polylogue bead es them (for target_bead, dependencies, parent); everyproposed bead must trace to something in your analysis (provenance); prefer update/supersede on an existing bead over a duplicate new one; size them as landable units with genuine acceptance criand keep them scoped to this file's payload so the sixJSON blocks concatenate into one non-overlapping backlog.

    # Print lines with key section labels + bead titles + bugs risks

## [assistant 424]
According to the file 2 bundle from 2026-07-05, I treated Part 1 only as orientation and anchored the deliverable to Part 2’s unique payload. I also checked the uploaded working-tree snapshot where the payload made concrete file/path claims. That means “confirmed” below means confirmed against the attached source snapshot, not necessarily the live repo if it has moved since this bundle was packed. fileciteturn2file4

## Executive verdict

File 2 is one of the stronger slices. Most of its tier/regime reasoning is correct: new analytical units mostly belong in rebuildable `index.db`; cross-tier assertion joins must remain runtime query methods rather than stored views; user-authored and agent-authored overlay state should stay in `user.db.assertions`; and proof/demo/relevance work should be made executable rather than prose-only. The best parts are the `turn-pair` / `artifact` / `correction-edge` unit design, the annotation-recipe substrate, the measure-registry discipline, Polish recall, search relevance, and demo/finding proof loop. fileciteturn1file16 fileciteturn2file12 fileciteturn1file0 fileciteturn1file13

The main corrections are important. The `turn-pair` pairing law as written can duplicate one assistant answer across multiple preceding prompts. The assertion “query-back” gap in annotation recipes is stale for the uploaded source: assertions are already a registered query unit with `query_assertions`. The observability write-path diagnosis is also partially stale: `daemon_events` already has writer/query infrastructure in the snapshot, so the real gap is SLO sampling and stall/idle verdicts, not basic event recording. The artifact design is directionally right but overconfident about “strictly richer than files” until shell redirections, bash commands, relative paths, and path identity are handled honestly. The measure-registry is conceptually excellent but should not ship as a 16-measure “museum” before the registry/count/coverage gate proves itself.

My strongest strategic correction: **make file 2’s payload cohere around three platform moves** rather than many parallel feature tracks:

1. **Typed analysis units**: turn-pair, artifact, correction-edge, spec-card, TQI, SLO sample, relevance judgment.
2. **Safe external judgment loop**: annotation recipes, assertion batches, query-back, recursive-safety at `upsert_assertion`, evidence/provenance refs.
3. **Executable proof and evaluation**: `.polydemo`, finding provenance, search-eval, measure-registry, replay/spec-card/RL export.

That is the non-overlapping contribution of file 2.

## Hard vet: confirmed

### `turn-pair`, `artifact`, and `correction-edge` are the right missing units

The design correctly identifies `actions` as the model pattern: a read relation pairing tool-use blocks with tool-result blocks. A `turn-pair` view over message adjacency is a natural analogue, and it belongs in the rebuildable index tier as a view plus a covering index. The query-unit machinery is indeed descriptor-driven: new units require a closed `QueryUnitName` update, descriptor, payload model, query method, structural registry entry, generated output schemas, OpenAPI, and topology projection regeneration. The payload’s “miss any one and discovery/render tests fail” warning is accurate. fileciteturn1file16

The `artifact` distinction is also correct. Polylogue already has `files` as a path aggregation over actions, while `raw_artifacts` in the source tier is an ingest taxonomy concept. A session-created/edited/read artifact relation should not reuse `raw_artifacts` terminology, and a real artifact unit needs operation provenance and later lineage, not only “this path appeared in the session.” The proposed Phase A `artifact_touches` view and Phase B `session_artifacts` / `artifact_lineage` materialization are a sound staged design. fileciteturn2file12

The `correction-edge` tiering is exactly right. It must join durable `user.db.assertions` to index-tier blocks/messages, but not as a persistent cross-database SQLite view. SQLite does not allow a view in one attached database/schema to reference objects in another attached database, so the runtime-query-method decision is not taste; it is a platform constraint. The uploaded payload calls this out, and external SQLite guidance confirms the constraint. fileciteturn1file1 citeturn717370search20

### The annotation substrate is real, but the missing product layer is batch/schema/agent ergonomics

The `assertions` table already has the right raw shape: target/scope, kind/key/value/body, author metadata, evidence refs, lifecycle status, confidence, staleness, context policy, supersession. New assertion kinds are schema-free text, so annotation recipes do not need a durable schema migration just to add vocabulary. fileciteturn1file0

The missing layer is not storage. It is: schema registry, JSONL batch import, evidence-ref validation, recursive-safety coercion, review/acceptance surface, query-back examples, and agent-friendly CLI/MCP verbs. External annotators should write candidate assertions in batches, not bespoke JSON files whose only consumer is a report script.

### The recursive-safety write chokepoint is a real bug surface

I verified the uploaded source snapshot’s `upsert_assertion` path: it normalizes status, visibility, author, and refs, but it does not centrally coerce non-user authors into candidate/non-injecting state. `post_blackboard_note` accepts `author_kind`, and the blackboard path can reach assertion insertion. That matches the payload’s diagnosis that agent-authored claims can become authoritative unless the safety gate is enforced in the assertion write chokepoint. The bundle explicitly frames this as the invariant recall/recipe/distillery/goal/decision all assume. fileciteturn1file2

This should be treated as P0/P1 correctness, not “nice safety.” Once Polylogue auto-captures its own R&D and agents can write annotations, self-laundering is the failure mode.

### The measure-registry concept is correct and strategically important

The measure algebra is the right antidote to bespoke `analyze` modes. A measure should declare construct, formula, denominator, unit frame, evidence tier, coverage preconditions, confounds, uncertainty, and output schema. The design’s insistence that `count` route through the same measure path is especially important: otherwise `group by … | count` becomes the bypass through which unfootnoted, construct-invalid numbers leak. fileciteturn1file9 fileciteturn1file10

The default `LOGICAL_SESSION` frame is also right. Physical fork/resume/compaction duplicates are not iid observations. Treating physical sessions as independent shrinks confidence intervals dishonestly and double-counts sums. The bundle’s risk section names this clearly. fileciteturn1file13

### Polish search recall is a real defect class

The payload’s FTS diagnosis is grounded. Current `messages_fts` uses SQLite FTS5 `unicode61`; the payload says both canonical DDL sites need to stay in sync, and that query-side normalization currently relies on the tokenizer rather than doing Polish-specific folding. The specific Polish issue is also real: `ł/Ł` is not handled by ordinary combining-mark removal, so relying on `remove_diacritics` alone leaves a recall hole. The staged plan—shared `pl_fold`, write-side folding into contentless FTS, query-side symmetry tests, then `block_prose_lang`—is sound. fileciteturn2file6 fileciteturn2file2

SQLite’s FTS5 `unicode61` tokenizer is the relevant built-in baseline, and using a Python/SQL folding function avoids writing a custom native FTS tokenizer, which would violate Polylogue’s current “no native deps” posture. citeturn717370search1

### Search relevance needs durable judgments before tuning

The search-relevance slice is strong. It correctly separates “ranking feels off” from the substrate needed to improve it: `RELEVANCE` assertions keyed by query fingerprint and target ref, an eval harness reporting nDCG/MRR/recall, explainability over existing `score_components`, lineage-aware collapse, and ranking-policy versioning. fileciteturn2file11 fileciteturn2file15

Do not tune RRF weights by intuition. First build judgments and an eval harness. Only then add weighted fusion, MMR, weak-evidence tags, or cross-query calibration.

### Demo proof engine and finding provenance are high-leverage

The `.polydemo` / finding-id / evidence-ref resolver / budget telemetry / privacy gate direction is exactly aligned with Polylogue’s credibility story. The important move is that a demo becomes an executable proof object, not a screenshot or README claim. The payload’s proposal for `.polydemo` frontmatter, declared constructs, failure taxonomy, artifact-hash drift, and CI integration should survive. fileciteturn2file0

The “finding provenance as table, not prose” idea is also right. A finding needs a queryable provenance stanza: measurement cursor, measure/DSL/code version, git SHA, sample-frame predicate, run date, and staleness state. That aligns with W3C PROV’s entity/activity/agent framing and RO-Crate’s approach of describing research objects and their contents with machine-readable metadata. fileciteturn1file17 citeturn272480search0turn272480search1

## Hard vet: refuted or corrected

### The `turn-pair` property test is wrong as stated

The proposed SQL pairs each prompt with the next later assistant message. If two human/operator messages occur before the next assistant answer, both prompts can pair to the same assistant. Therefore the proposed property “no assistant message is claimed by two prompts” is not guaranteed by the SQL. fileciteturn1file6

Correct design options:

- If a “turn” means “prompt burst answered by one assistant,” group consecutive human/operator prompts before the assistant into one prompt-set.
- If a “turn” means “one prompt row,” pair only the last prompt before an assistant and mark earlier prompt rows as superseded/unanswered-within-burst.
- If preserving every prompt row matters, expose `answer_claim_count` or `prompt_burst_id` so downstream rates do not assume one-to-one.

I recommend **prompt-burst turn pairs** for analytics and a lower-level message adjacency relation for forensic inspection.

### `artifact_touches` is not yet strictly richer than `files`

It is richer for structured tool-path operations. It is not richer for bash redirections, `tee`, `sed -i`, `cat > file`, generated files without `tool_path`, absolute/relative path aliases, renamed paths, or provider-specific tools that do not map to `Read/Edit/Write`. The payload acknowledges open-ended tool vocabulary risk, but the “strictly richer” statement should be weakened until a tool-operation classifier and shell-path parser exist. fileciteturn2file12

The first landing should call itself “structured artifact touches,” not “all artifacts a session touched.”

### Annotation “query-back” is stale for this source snapshot

The payload/meta-summary says annotation recipes have a “query-back” completeness gap because assertions are MCP-list-only and not in the `find` DSL. That is not true in the uploaded working tree. `assertion` is already a terminal/structural query unit, and `query_assertions` exists as a runtime method over `user_tier.assertions`. The real gap is not queryability; it is batch import, schema validation, review ergonomics, and recursive-safety coercion. fileciteturn2file17 fileciteturn1file0

So: do not create a bead for “make assertions queryable” as if absent. Create one for “make external assertion batches easy and safe.”

### Observability should reuse existing event infrastructure

The steady-state observability design is mostly right: SLO samples, reducers, idle-vs-stalled verdict, live-tail scoping, disposable ops-tier retention. But the current snapshot already has daemon event infrastructure; the missing work is not “create event writing from nothing.” The landing should reuse the existing daemon-events and cursor-lag patterns and add `slo_samples`/reducers/retention. OpenTelemetry and Prometheus both make a useful distinction between raw events, histograms/distributions, and derived time-series; Polylogue should follow that separation. fileciteturn2file18 citeturn272480search2turn272480search3

There is also an unresolved ops-tier policy conflict. Some file-2 designs assume an `ops.db` version bump; others assume self-healing optional telemetry tables. Pick one rule: I recommend **self-heal optional telemetry tables, but version/bump only when a table becomes a required contract validated by doctor/CI**.

### Measure registry is over-scoped if shipped all at once

The 16 named measures are useful, but shipping all 16 before the registry/count/coverage core is a classic “analytics museum” failure. The critical-path material in the bundle itself warns that broad behavioral analytics can be orthogonal until a live query demands them. fileciteturn2file14

First PR should be: `MeasureSpec`, `count`, coverage refusal, tier footnotes, Wilson/bootstrap primitives, and rigor audit. The named measures should land in small batches only when a proof/demo/report uses them.

### TQI must stay reward-shaping, not truth

The spec-card/TQI slice is valuable, but TQI is a composite score over partially heuristic subscores. It should be emitted only with component tiers, NULL/insufficient-coverage gates, base rates, and a Goodhart warning. The file already says this, and I agree. fileciteturn2file1

The stronger design is to make TQI a `MeasureSpec`-backed projection with visible components, not a single ranking number that surfaces by default.

### Trigram fallback and “Polish recall” need measurement before default enablement

Trigram fallback can improve substring/typo/inflection recall, but it can also expand index size and hurt precision. The payload estimates roughly 1.5–2× FTS size and recommends fallback/recall-booster behavior rather than replacing primary FTS. That is the right posture. It should be behind a measured benchmark and an explicit routing rule, not silently enabled for all queries. fileciteturn2file9

### Performance recommendations need sharper “prove then build” gates

The performance slice correctly identifies exact vector scans, repeated per-seed fanout, no query-plan regression lane, no preview cache, and exact counts on interactive paths. fileciteturn2file8

External context shifts the ANN story. `sqlite-vec` now documents binary quantization as a way to reduce vector size, but it still describes the current search path as brute-force; SQLite’s separate Vec1 extension now offers ANN via IVFADC/OPQ. citeturn422173search0turn422173search3

That means the right bead is not “migrate to ANN.” It is: benchmark exact f32, int8/binary quantization + rerank, sqlite-vec metadata partitioning, and Vec1 as an experimental sidecar candidate. Keep “SQLite as sole store” as a constraint until numbers prove otherwise.

## External context and design implications

The local protocol/composer work should borrow from LSP without becoming LSP. LSP’s cancellation mechanism is a useful precedent for keystroke-driven completion/preview: superseded requests should be cancellable by id, not merely ignored client-side. citeturn717370search3

The proof engine should borrow from reproducible research packaging rather than ordinary demos. W3C PROV gives the right conceptual triad—entities, activities, agents—and RO-Crate gives the “research object with machine-readable metadata” pattern. For Polylogue, the minimal adaptation is: finding entity, query/measure activity, archive/corpus entity, agent/operator, evidence refs, generated artifact, and verification status. citeturn272480search0turn272480search1

The MCP-facing parts should use MCP resources and prompts deliberately. Resources are the natural way to expose evidence packs, schemas, query result refs, and report artifacts; prompts are the natural way to publish reusable analysis recipes without hiding them inside a bespoke daemon command. citeturn272480search4turn272480search15

For RL/eval export, Atropos is relevant but must be verified live before locking schema. It is an open-source environment framework for collecting/evaluating LLM rollouts, but file 2’s own caution is correct: the export should be a pure read projection first, not a training system. fileciteturn2file1 citeturn272480search5

## Prioritized take

**Do immediately.** Enforce recursive-safety in `upsert_assertion`; ship annotation batch import; create `turn-pair` corrected to prompt-burst semantics; add `correction-edge` runtime query; build demo/finding proof loop; add search relevance judgments and eval harness; add query-plan regression/perf gates.

**Do next.** Land structured artifact touches; Polish `pl_fold` and FTS symmetry; measure-registry core with `count`; SLO samples and idle-vs-stalled verdict; finding provenance table; spec-card export.

**Do after proof.** TQI as reward-shaping, RL/eval export, trigram fallback, MMR/diversity, vector quantization/ANN, incident/compaction lifecycle analytics.

**Need live source before final implementation.** Re-check current repo HEAD for line drift; confirm whether `s7ae` shipped after the bundle; verify current Atropos schema; measure live archive performance for vector scans, counts, and artifact materialization; sample real provider tool vocab before hardcoding artifact operation classes.

## [assistant 403]
According to a document from 2026-07-05, I treated `rnd-bundle-3-of-6.md` as **file 3 of 6** and used only its Part 2 payload as the scope anchor; Part 1 was useful only for confidence caveats and global context. The package/code snapshot let me verify many of the “greenfield vs existing seam” claims, but I could not verify live Git tags, current release state, or the original `tasks/*.output` line anchors because those task-output files and live repo metadata were not included. The payload itself also warns that some synthesis-level file:line claims were summary-derived after compaction and should be re-opened before coding. fileciteturn2file1turn3file3

## Executive verdict

File 3 is the “analysis substrate” slice. Its strongest coherent direction is: make Polylogue able to turn archive evidence into **durable query objects, reproducible findings, citable evidence packs, compressed corpus digests, provenance-aware reports, and validity-gated analytics**. This is the right frontier for Polylogue because it reinforces the product identity as a local system of record / flight recorder for AI work rather than a generic chat viewer or memory toy. The strongest parts are query/findings-as-objects, content-hash citation anchors, corpus compaction, source/blob tiering discipline, vector retrieval evaluation, and meta-quality tests. The weaker parts are where the payload overstates “no schema break,” under-specifies canonicalization and staleness, or treats derived result sets as more durable than they really are.

My highest-confidence correction is that **query objects need to be split into at least four concepts**: `query_definition`, `query_run`, `result_relation`, and `render_artifact`. The Part-2 design’s `query_defs/result_sets/result_set_members` is a strong start, but a single `query:<hash>` plus index-tier snapshots is not enough to support citations, findings-as-tests, analysis replay, and agent loops cleanly. `query:<hash>` should identify the canonical definition; executions and result relations need separate refs.

My second-highest-confidence correction is that **provenance is the common abstraction behind almost everything in this file**. Findings, reports, annotations, query runs, context packs, model-drift observations, citation anchors, and corpus compaction all need the same pattern: structured object, evidence refs, source freshness, derived-vs-raw tier, and revalidation behavior. This aligns well with W3C PROV’s entity/activity/agent model and OpenLineage’s run/job/dataset/facet model: both treat provenance as structured event metadata rather than prose attached after the fact. citeturn346437search2turn346437search6turn346437search3turn346437search7

## Hard vetting: confirmed

The query/findings object work is genuinely greenfield on real seams. In the code snapshot, there is no `query_defs`, `result_sets`, `query_edges`, `StandingQueryStage`, `query` ObjectRef kind, or `AssertionKind.FINDING`. `index.db` is still v24; `user.db.assertions.kind` is plain `TEXT`, so adding a new assertion kind is a code/schema-surface change rather than a durable DDL migration. The existing assertion candidate → judge → promote lifecycle is real and can be reused. The Part-2 design’s placement of query registry/result snapshots in derived `index.db`, durable standing-query intent in `user.db`, and standing-run bookkeeping in `ops.db` is directionally correct. fileciteturn1file4turn1file5turn1file11turn1file16

The main correction is canonicalization. “Equivalent queries collapse” is right only where equivalence laws are explicit. Boolean `A and B` can commute. Pipeline stages, ranking, `limit`, `sort`, semantic/hybrid retrieval, sequence, and set-op rank policies usually cannot. The query identity layer needs an operator-law table: commutative, associative, order-sensitive, rank-bearing, stochastic/model-dependent, and macro-expanded. Without that, the exact risk the payload names—canonical-form drift orphaning result sets and findings—will happen. fileciteturn2file2

The archive-economics/tiering design is grounded. The current blob store stores raw sharded blobs addressed by SHA-256 of the uncompressed payload; verification currently hashes raw file bytes; there is no zstd placement/dictionary/tombstone/frozen-segment layer in the snapshot. So the safe beachhead is exactly right: update read/verify to sniff/decompress before compressing a single blob. Source-tier durable placement/dictionary/tombstone metadata is justified because losing a zstd dictionary can make compressed evidence unreadable; RFC 8878 describes a dictionary ID field, but decompression still depends on having the dictionary bytes, so the dictionary registry must be backed up and append-only. fileciteturn1file6turn1file10turn3file16 citeturn346437search4turn346437search16turn346437search20

The “address is SHA(uncompressed)” principle is exactly the right invariant. It preserves deduplication, re-ingest idempotency, and evidence identity while allowing compression, cold movement, frozen pack files, or citable tombstones underneath. The correction is that `last_read_at_ms` is not really source-tier durability; it is access-temperature telemetry. It can be co-located for performance, but the design should either tolerate losing it or mirror it in ops. Physical placement and decompression dependencies are durable; access heat is not.

Corpus compaction is correctly placed in the read algebra. It should not be a separate report generator. The payload frames `find <query> | compact` as `Selection × CompactionProjection × COMPACT render`, distinct from the existing context compiler that builds handoff/context images around seed sessions. That distinction is important: context compiler is for continuation; corpus compaction is for feeding an external model a bounded, decision-dense digest of many sessions, with a drop manifest. fileciteturn3file16

The context scheduler direction is real but less implemented. The assertions schema already supports author, evidence refs, confidence, staleness, and `context_policy_json`, but the scheduler/ContextSource/ledger behavior is not present in the snapshot as a real subsystem. The payload’s ops-ledger design is a good first cut, especially its explicit exclusion of `context_inject` from attention signals so the scheduler cannot reinforce its own injections. The correction is retention: if a context compile or injection ledger becomes evidence in an uplift experiment, report, or finding, it must be snapshotted/exported/promoted, because pure ops retention is disposable by design. fileciteturn3file10turn1file17

The blue-green index rebuild design is well-founded. The current code is still built around `index.db`, so generation pointer files, `index.gN.db`, atomic swap, reader leases, and ops mirrors are new work. The pointer file should be authoritative; an ops table can mirror state but cannot be the thing you need before opening the index. The test strategy is strong: pointer atomicity, held-reader generation stability, zero failed queries during swap, and lease-safe reaping. fileciteturn1file7turn1file8

The provider→origin aggregate honesty issue is real, but one phrasing needs tightening. The code already has some source-family concepts, so the problem is not “there is no source-family anywhere”; the problem is that physical session identity and headline rollups are still keyed in ways that can collapse distinct runtime families. Adding `source_family` and lossy markers can fix aggregate honesty; it cannot fix a physical row collision caused by `session_id = origin || ':' || native_id`. The payload correctly isolates that residual as a separate durable/identity problem. fileciteturn2file13turn2file6

The vector-search plan is plausible and properly skeptical. The snapshot has two live vec0 DDL definitions with incompatible metadata naming (`+origin` versus legacy `+source_name`), no int8/bit lane, and no quantization/eval gate. The payload’s insistence on f32 baseline, int8 rerank, recall@k from lineage-labeled pairs, and “do not default until live eval passes” is exactly the right posture. The correction is prior-art freshness: sqlite-vec has binary quantization support, and SQLite’s official `vec1` extension has recently documented ANN support with IVF/PQ-style compression. Before building a homegrown centroid/IVF layer, Polylogue should run a short decision spike comparing sqlite-vec int8/binary, SQLite `vec1`, and an external ANN option. fileciteturn2file12turn3file9 citeturn346437search1turn346437search9

The evidence-cockpit anchor diagnosis is confirmed. Current block refs are position-based; message content hashes exist, but block content hashes do not. A stable citation system needs block hashes, but block hash alone is not enough because compaction/replay can duplicate identical blocks. Anchors need captured position, parent message/session hash, lineage segment, and ambiguity states. The payload’s exact/drift/deleted/quarantined framing is correct; I would add “ambiguous” as a first-class resolution state rather than treating multi-hit as degraded exactness. fileciteturn2file8turn3file17

The missing-unit and ontology work is valuable only if kept disciplined. Several “units” should be views or runtime methods, not tables. The SQLite rule is real: a persistent view in one attached database cannot reference objects in another attached database, so correction-edge / assertion-over-block joins must be runtime queries, TEMP views, or materialized derived tables built without cross-tier DDL. SQLite’s own forum guidance aligns with this constraint. fileciteturn3file1 citeturn437157search0turn437157search6

The meta-quality suite is one of the highest-leverage parts of this file. Identity round-trip, content-hash idempotency, lineage no-double-count, FTS trigger coherence, daemon-vs-direct differential, convergence idempotency, blob-GC state machine, parser fuzz, and scale-shaped synthetic corpus are exactly the tests that make the “system of record” claim credible. They should outrank a lot of UI polish. fileciteturn3file11turn3file2

## Hard vetting: refuted or corrected

The “no break” phrasing in archive compression is too optimistic. The address layer can remain stable, but the read layer changes semantically: every reader, verifier, backup checker, evidence resolver, and GC path must understand codec sniffing, dictionaries, frozen ranges, tombstones, and logical-vs-stored bytes. That is not an identity break, but it is a wide behavioral migration. The bead must land read/verify decompression first and block compression writes until every path is proven codec-aware. fileciteturn1file12

The query-object design underplays query-run durability. It says ad-hoc snapshots are disposable, which is correct for index-tier caches, but any promoted finding, published report, or analysis recipe cannot cite a disposable result set. Promotion must require a saved/standing query or a durable evidence pack. A finding can cite `query:<hash>` and durable evidence refs; it should not depend on `result_set_id` surviving `ops reset --index`. fileciteturn3file7

`corpus_version = MAX(updated_at_ms)` is not good enough as a general staleness boundary. It is coarse, can thrash every standing query after irrelevant ingest, and may not be stable across rebuilds. The staleness dependency should be a vector: source high-water marks by origin/family, materialization generation, query lanes used, and maybe relevant filter constraints. The Part-2 risk section already names thrash/staleness; I would make dependency vectors part of the design rather than an optimization. fileciteturn2file2

The model-drift observatory is correct to avoid causal claims, but it should not become another analytics “museum.” Drift measures need to be tied to a measure registry and to actual launch/use questions. Existing systems like Evidently and NannyML distinguish data drift, performance estimation, and label-free monitoring, while changepoint libraries like `ruptures` can find structural changes but do not identify causes by themselves. Polylogue should render “candidate + nearby events + confounds,” never “model X regressed because…”. fileciteturn3file0 citeturn231898search0turn231898search1turn231898search2

The release/distribution analysis is only partially verifiable from the package. I confirmed that the tree carries release workflows and docs that still describe packaged installation as unavailable, and that the version appears frozen at `0.1.0` in local files. I could not verify the “zero git tags” claim from the tarball because `.git` metadata is absent. The actionable conclusion remains: release is mostly a decision and smoke-matrix issue, but the exact current public tag/release state needs live GitHub verification before bead closure. The right release baseline should use PyPI trusted publishing/OIDC, Sigstore attestations, CycloneDX SBOMs, and `uvx`/`uv tool` smoke tests rather than manual tokens or clone-only docs. fileciteturn3file5 citeturn566573search0turn566573search1turn566573search2turn566573search3

The “pure Python/no native deps” launch phrasing should be retired or narrowed. Even if Polylogue is written in Python, its packaging path can depend on native/Rust-backed wheels or SQLite extensions. The launch claim should be “installable without a compiler on supported platforms” only after wheel smoke tests prove no sdist fallback.

The “finding as AssertionKind” idea is right, but `AssertionKind.FINDING` is not sufficient as a product model. A published finding also needs a manifest: producing query, query run, corpus data sheet, expected value/tolerance, evidence refs, artifact URI, and revalidation status. This is where PROV/OpenLineage-style run metadata becomes more useful than a single row in `assertions`. fileciteturn3file4turn3file13

## What should be designed better than the current payload

The strongest unifying abstraction missing from file 3 is **analysis objects**. The payload has query objects, findings, reports, context ledgers, model-drift cohorts, compaction outputs, and demos, but it does not quite name the general object:

`analysis_run = recipe/prompt + query_runs + result_relations + evidence_packs + annotation_batches + findings + render_artifacts`

This matters because external agents will not only query Polylogue; they will run iterative analyses. They need stable refs for “what I asked,” “what came back,” “which rows I annotated,” “which claims I promoted,” and “which report I rendered.” This is more general than YAML recipes and more durable than CLI stdout.

The second missing abstraction is **value-level evidence refs**. The honesty audit correctly notes that block/message refs are too coarse for a cost, token count, occurrence count, or provenance-derived timestamp. A number should be able to point to `block + json-path/field + reducer + denominator/frame`, or else the product promise must say “every number resolves to evidence at block granularity,” not “every number resolves to bytes.” fileciteturn2file16turn3file12

The third missing abstraction is **identity-policy on every relation**. Query results, cohorts, result sets, episodes, drift cohorts, set algebra, and saved snapshots all depend on identity: physical session, logical session, message row, composed message, block hash, artifact hash, or source-family-qualified native id. This should not be implicit in each feature. It should be part of `result_relation`.

The fourth missing abstraction is **promotion gates**. Agent-written assertions, findings, prompt templates, drift observations, text-derived facts, and context-injected memories all need one chokepoint for author_kind/trust_class/status/inject policy. The payload’s recursive-safety note is right: if this is per-feature, one path will bypass it. fileciteturn3file8

## Prioritized take

First, land the honesty substrate before the gallery features: query/run/result refs, finding lifecycle, value-level evidence, text-derived provenance contracts, and meta-quality tests.

Second, land blue-green before the v25/v3/v5 pile. File 3 repeatedly needs index v25 and source v3; rebuilding a 38 GB archive one feature at a time is operationally wrong. The payload’s own cross-cutting note says schema bumps must be batched and blue-green removes the downtime cost. fileciteturn3file8

Third, do the compression beachhead early but slowly. Read/verify codec support first; placement/dictionaries second; compression writes third; frozen/drop later. Compression is high leverage, but only if evidence integrity is never put at risk.

Fourth, do not build the model-drift/analytics observatory before its validity gates. Embed coverage, cohort anchors, denominator rules, and uncertainty should block output. Otherwise it becomes exactly the “insight museum” the red-team warned about.

Fifth, preserve the launch lesson: Polylogue’s public story should be flight recorder/system-of-record plus one hard finding, not a giant feature catalog. The demo proof engine should force every public number through query/finding/evidence refs.

## Executive verdict

This slice is unusually strong. The best specs are not “ideas”; they are close to implementation briefs with correct tier placement, realistic tests, and good construct-validity instincts. I would trust four clusters enough to turn directly into work: attachment referenced-vs-stored honesty, secret/forget + reset dry-run contract, blob-GC state-machine hardening, and ingest fidelity/fingerprint tracking. Those are credibility work: they prevent Polylogue from lying about bytes, mutating the wrong target, losing parse coverage silently, or deleting data during GC.

The largest correction is that several specs are overconfident about “already 90% built.” The substrate is often 60–80% present, but the missing 20% is usually the product boundary: queryability, object refs, import/review ergonomics, generated contracts, and recursive-safety chokepoints. That difference matters. It is the difference between “we have rows that could support this” and “agents can reliably use this as an analysis substrate.”

The highest-leverage strategic improvement is to make **query/result/annotation/analysis objects** first-class sooner. That makes many Part-2 ideas compose: delegation demo, Fable analysis, standing queries, ambient notifications, external annotation batches, context packs, triage, and self-referential Polylogue analysis.

## Hard vetting

### Confirmed

The ingest fidelity design has the right tier split. `raw_fidelity` is derived from blob plus parser and belongs in `index.db`; `parser_fingerprint` is the durable parse-identity switch that belongs with `raw_sessions`. The spec’s `detect_all()` addition is also directionally right because today detection is first-match, and the dispatch blind-spot around sampling only the first 32 JSONL records is a real class of loss signal to record. The file explicitly calls out the same tier rationale: derived ratios should not be durable, and only the decision input needs to survive rebuilds. fileciteturn1file11 The proposed F1–F7 breakdown is landable: `detect_all`, source v3 fingerprint/decode class, `raw_fidelity`, ambiguity/tripwires, drop accounting, parser-drift convergence, and golden/property tests. fileciteturn1file10

The attachment honesty diagnosis is real and important. The archive already has the load-bearing truth: `byte_count`, nullable `blob_hash`, and `acquisition_status`. The bug is projection: read surfaces expose a bare `size_bytes`/declared byte number without saying whether bytes were actually acquired. The spec is correct that this is not a schema migration; it is a projection, payload, accounting, and lint problem. fileciteturn1file0 The two-sum invariant is the right product contract: `referenced_bytes` must be separated from `stored_bytes`, with `unfetched` and `unavailable` kept explicit; a citation to a non-stored attachment must never render as a confident retrievable hit. fileciteturn1file4

The secret/forget spec identifies a real mutation safety failure. The reset path can resolve an unknown token into a suppression target instead of failing closed, and mutation is behind confirmation rather than behind a typed resolved-target dry-run. The content-hash resurrection vector is also real: if excised content is re-ingested from the original source, idempotency needs a tombstone guard or the content can reappear. The spec’s split into dry-run mutation contract, source tombstones, excision engine, idempotency guard, secret candidate queue, read overlay, and reconciliation stage is coherent. fileciteturn2file1 fileciteturn2file5

The delegation unit is well-framed. A delegation should not mean “any child session.” It should mean a parent-dispatched subagent edge with a structural parent-side task/action, returned artifact, and outcome fields; Codex-style sidechains without parent task result data should stay visible as `unknown` and excluded from ROI/yield denominators. That is exactly the construct-validity line the demo needs. fileciteturn2file9 The DSL/unit/card/yield breakdown is also right: the demo should be built over a generic `delegation` relation, not as Fable-specific logic. fileciteturn2file14

The blob-GC hardening spec correctly says the implementation is not absent. The current system already has leases, generation gates, GC history, failure-path cleanup, and nontrivial tests. The missing work is a stronger state-machine model, SIGKILL/fault coverage, and reconciliation between divergent orphan-detection surfaces. That is a high-quality correction: do not rewrite GC; prove its invariants. fileciteturn1file18 Hypothesis’s stateful testing model is a good fit for this exact class of interleaving invariant, because it defines operations and checks invariants across generated state transitions rather than only checking fixed examples. citeturn603773search0

The non-English/accessibility slice surfaces real gaps. The SQLite FTS5 `unicode61` issue around Polish `ł/Ł` is not imaginary; SQLite maintainers have explained that the relevant characters lack decomposition data, so `remove_diacritics` does not fold them the way users expect. citeturn222185search0 The Part-2 text’s proposed split between natural-language detection, query/index normalization symmetry, trigram/Polish expansion fallback, reply-language preference, TTS/STT, and a true screen-reader/plain mode is useful. fileciteturn2file6 fileciteturn2file3

The query-objects/annotation direction is exactly right. The assertions table already has the right bones: scope, target, evidence refs, staleness, supersession, confidence, author kind, and assertion kinds such as saved query, recall pack, workspace note, decision, blocker, lesson, and judgment. The spec correctly identifies the missing frontier: saved queries are currently inert blobs/strings, not referenceable query objects with result-set memory and query→query dependency edges. fileciteturn1file17

### Corrected or narrowed

The temporal bug is real, but one diagnosis should be narrowed. The file family says `RELATIVE_BASE = datetime.now()` behaves as an import/process-start anchor; in the code snapshot I inspected, the visible direct `datetime.now()` base is not a global import-time constant but a wall-clock call inside date parsing. That still needs a `core/clock.py` seam and hermetic `frozen_clock` tests, but the precise failure mode should be described as “uncontrolled wall-clock in relative-date parsing,” not necessarily “process-start-stale relative base.” The temporal design’s acceptance tests remain right: hermetic relative windows, half-open `[since, until)`, explicit timeless handling, comparator properties, and backfill invariants. fileciteturn2file10

The `sort_key_ms=COALESCE(...,0)` issue is real but not uniform across all read paths. Some ordering paths already bucket NULLs explicitly; others do coalesce to zero or otherwise risk synthetic 1970 behavior. The bead should start with a targeted ordering/window audit and then replace bad sites, not assume every sort path is equally broken. The design’s deeper move is still correct: `sort_key_ms` needs provenance/confidence, NULL/timeless rows need explicit semantics, and cursor stability must be protected by a backfill invariant. fileciteturn2file13

Delegation should not be implemented as “just a VIEW” without an audit pass. The proposed view is plausible, but the join `actions.message_id = branch_point_message_id` may miss cases where the parent Task dispatch is “near” the branch point rather than exactly equal, or where the provider emits subagent relationships differently. The right first bead is an audit/backfill over a seed/live sample that computes match rate: subagent links, parent dispatch action found, returned artifact found, `unknown` rate by origin. Only after that should the public yield measure ship. The Part-2 risk section already anticipates `unknown` dominating non-Claude; the backlog should encode that as a gating metric, not a footnote. fileciteturn2file4

The ingest unparsed-key census via a read-tracking proxy is promising, but overconfident. A proxy catches `.get`/`__getitem__` reads, but parsers may copy dicts, hand payloads to Pydantic, iterate keys, destructure, or consume nested objects in ways that the proxy does not faithfully attribute. Treat the census as a best-effort coverage detector until each parser opts into an explicit consumed-key contract or golden corpus comparison. The golden “key-set only shrinks” test is the stronger guard.

The notification specs need a stricter anti-feedback rule. Recording a filtered/unsafe signal into an ops ledger is fine; emitting it as a user-facing content notice or injecting it into a context preamble is not. Alerting prior art strongly favors actionable, user-relevant alerts and warns against alert noise; Polylogue should additionally require citation anchors and recursive-safety provenance checks before surfacing content notices. citeturn216365search1 The Part-2 notification spec already gestures at recursive gates and suppression assertions; I would make them first-class acceptance criteria, not optional polish. fileciteturn1file5

“Verifiable forget” should be named carefully. The design can provide **logical archive forget** and **reingest resurrection prevention**. It should not imply cryptographic or physical erasure from filesystem slack, WAL history, backups, copied exports, external provider logs, or old bundles unless those scopes are explicitly included. NIST media-sanitization guidance frames sanitization as making access to target data infeasible on the relevant media; Polylogue’s default scope is narrower than whole-media sanitization, so the product language must say so. citeturn222185search3

Archive economics is useful but must be measurement-gated. Zstd dictionaries, cold shards, embedding pruning, and content-defined chunking are credible directions, but the first bead should be “measure dedup/rebuild/storage dividend,” not “implement FastCDC.” FastCDC is real prior art for efficient content-defined chunking, but whether Polylogue benefits depends on the distribution of large near-duplicate blobs and rebuild cost. citeturn646079search14

The replay/reproduction design is appropriately cautious. It should stay a two-phase feature: dry reconstruction plan first, sandboxed execution second, and no deterministic replay claims by default. ReproZip, rr, and Nix show the design space: capture execution environments, record/replay deterministic executions, or rebuild in declarative isolated environments. Polylogue’s session logs are weaker than those systems’ full execution capture, so “reconstruct/reproduce plan” is the honest baseline. citeturn646079search0turn646079search1turn646079search20

### Extended recommendations

The file’s most important missing unifier is an explicit **analysis object model**. Query objects, result sets, annotation batches, standing queries, context packs, delegation cards, triage frontiers, ambient notices, and reports are currently described in separate specs. They should share one object vocabulary:

`query_definition`, `query_run`, `result_relation`, `cohort`, `annotation_batch`, `analysis_run`, `evidence_pack`, `report_artifact`.

This avoids building “delegation demo,” “triage inbox,” “ambient notifications,” and “query history” as separate systems. A query run can feed a result relation; a result relation can become a snapshot cohort; an annotation batch can target that cohort; an analysis run can link the query runs, evidence pack, imported judgments, and final report. That is the substrate needed for the Fable/delegation demo, external annotations, and Polylogue tracking its own use.

OpenTelemetry’s GenAI semantic conventions are relevant here: model names, token counts, prompts, completions, tool calls, and tool results are becoming a shared telemetry vocabulary. Polylogue should not simply clone OTel, because it has stronger archive/evidence needs, but the replay/delegation/observability work should map outward to OTel concepts where possible. citeturn603773search1

The entity graph is valuable but should be staged conservatively. Structural entity extraction from URLs, issue refs, commits, repo paths, and action evidence is high value. Candidate prose mining is dangerous in a self-archiving system; the Part-2 risk around recursive fabrication is correct. fileciteturn1file2 Ship structural mentions and query surfaces first. Treat prose-mined mentions as candidate assertions requiring the same recursive-safety gate as external annotations.

The accessibility slice should be split between **machine mode** and **human accessibility**. `--json` is not screen-reader UX. A true `--plain` or `--a11y` mode should avoid Rich tables/box glyphs and render linear labeled text. WCAG’s “color is not the only visual means” principle is a useful baseline for terminal/web cockpit output, even though Polylogue is not a conventional website. citeturn216365search6

## Prioritized take

Tier 0, credibility and safety: attachment two-sum honesty, reset/excision dry-run, tombstone resurrection guard, temporal clock/window fixes, and blob-GC state-machine tests. These prevent data lies and destructive mistakes.

Tier 1, analysis substrate: query objects, result relations/cohorts, annotation batches, assertion query-back, delegation unit, and evidence packs. These turn Polylogue from a search surface into an analysis workbench.

Tier 2, ambient/context: semantic notifications, triage frontier, attention/read-access logs, context preambles, and standing queries. These are powerful only after recursive-safety and object refs are in place.

Tier 3, breadth/frontier: entity graph, replay execution, archive economics, non-English recall, TTS/STT/accessibility, and public positioning. These matter, but several should be measurement-gated or proof-artifact-gated.

The bead set below is deliberately scoped to file 4. I used existing bead ids where they were clearly available from the current bundle/bead context; where a file-4 spec implies new work rather than an existing child, I used `new` and linked it to the nearest extant epic.
