## [assistant 448]
I treated file 5 as its own slice. I used the master synthesis only to understand vocabulary and extant bead IDs; the substance below is anchored to Part 2’s sixteen outputs. I also checked the uploaded Polylogue code snapshot where possible. I did not run the daemon, the live archive, or heavy tests, and I could not verify cross-repo claims about Lynchpin without Lynchpin’s source tree.

## Executive verdict

File 5’s unique payload is not one topic; it is a coherent “make Polylogue useful to itself and to agents” slice. It covers: intent units (`phase-segment`, `goal`, `decision`), migration/scale correctness, executable demos, content variants, SDK/public boundary, activation/adoption, cross-machine sync, prompt distillation, missing insight units, MCP collapse, cost correctness, daily workflow verbs, release/schema discipline, config doctrine, and self-observability.

The good news: most of the strongest diagnoses are real. The code already has the primitives the designs want to expose: work events distinct from phases, a unified assertions table with candidate/accepted/superseded lifecycle, split-tier storage discipline, sync/async API surfaces, rich MCP tooling, and cost code whose exact-cost and provider-lane problems are concrete. The file is strongest when it says “wire what exists, expose it through the algebra, and gate derived claims.”

The bad news: several designs are overconfident about naming, tiering, or scope. The recurring correction is that Polylogue needs fewer new nouns and more typed provenance objects. “Goal,” “decision,” “prompt template,” “demo finding,” “variant,” and “saved query” should all converge on the same model: durable assertion/judgment/recipe objects, derived candidates, explicit evidence refs, candidate-by-default agent output, and queryable result/analysis objects. The file often gets the storage regime right, but under-specifies the object model that would make these analyses composable.

## Hard vetting: confirmed

The `phase-segment` correction is right. In the code snapshot, `SessionPhase` is explicitly time-gap segmented and its docstring says the intent `kind` field was removed because phases represent when activity happened, not what kind of activity it was. The intent-classified substrate is `session_work_events`, with labels such as planning, implementation, debugging, review, testing, research, configuration, documentation, refactoring, data_analysis, and session; the index DDL has `session_work_events` rows with `work_event_type`, confidence, duration, file paths, tools, and evidence. Exposing `phase-segment` as a query/projection over work events, not as a new `session_phases.kind`, is the correct construct-validity choice. The proposed confidence gate and “unlabeled” bucket are also right: low-confidence inferred work type must not become a crisp workflow shape. fileciteturn1file4turn1file14

The `goal` and `decision-object` direction is mostly right: mined intent must go through the existing assertion lifecycle. I verified `AssertionKind` already includes `DECISION`, `JUDGMENT`, `RUN_STATE`, `PROMPT_EVAL`, `TRANSFORM_CANDIDATE`, and `PATHOLOGY`, and `AssertionStatus` includes `ACTIVE`, `CANDIDATE`, `ACCEPTED`, `REJECTED`, `DEFERRED`, `SUPERSEDED`, `DELETED`, and `INACTIVE`. The assertion table is schema-free enough for new kinds, with `evidence_refs_json`, `context_policy_json`, `supersedes_json`, author fields, status, visibility, and confidence. The design’s “mined claim never ACTIVE/injectable until judged” rule is exactly the right invariant. fileciteturn2file4

The migration-fuzz and scale-regression line is strategically right even though I would size it as an infrastructure bead, not product work. The code has a durable migration runner with backup-manifest checks, per-tier migrations for source/user, and rebuild rather than in-place migration for derived tiers. That means fuzzing start versions, sparse migration chains, backup gating, and durable-versus-derived policy is not theoretical; it directly protects the split-tier archive. The correction is that fuzz tests must model the real sparse historical chains, not assume contiguous `001..N`.

The `.polydemo` proof-engine design is strong. Its best idea is not “demo runner”; it is that a demo finding should be content-addressed over claim, metric, evidence anchor, sorted refs, and corpus datasheet hash, then recomputed in CI so drift breaks the build. That turns public demos into reproducible findings rather than screenshots. The parser/runner/resolver/refusal/construct-validity tests are the right failure gates. fileciteturn1file2turn1file17

The content-variant design is directionally correct: variants must not overwrite original evidence, must carry alignment edges, coverage status, source-content hashes, staleness state, and explicit “dark matter” for unaccounted source children. The design is also correct that generated variants must never be auto-repainted in place when source evidence drifts; recovery should be a new variant that supersedes the old one. fileciteturn1file13

The SDK diagnosis is partly confirmed from Polylogue’s side. The code snapshot has `polylogue.api.sync`, but no stable `polylogue.models` package. Public models are scattered across archive/session/message/insight modules. A curated SDK boundary would be valuable. I could not verify the Lynchpin raw `SELECT ... FROM conversations` claim because Lynchpin source was not in the uploaded Polylogue package; treat that specific cross-repo diagnosis as plausible but unconfirmed until the Lynchpin tree is read. fileciteturn2file6

The cross-machine sync tiering is broadly right: sync durable source/user data, never derived index/embeddings/ops files. I verified `deterministic_raw_session_id` includes `source_path`, so the file’s warning about machine-local raw IDs is real. Same logical capture can become two physical raw sessions across machines if paths differ. That must be surfaced as physical-union behavior, not hidden as “deduped sync.” fileciteturn1file6

The MCP collapse target is right, but the count is approximate. The uploaded code snapshot’s static `EXPECTED_TOOL_NAMES` count is 96, not 95; dynamic insight registration plausibly brings the live server into the ~110–130 range. The conclusion still stands: the MCP surface is too wide and should collapse around algebraic verbs like `query`, `get`, `explain`, `context`, `correlate`, `coordinate`, `assert`, `retract`, and `maintenance`, with resources/prompts used for non-tool affordances. The migration must be golden-tested, not big-bang deleted. fileciteturn1file3turn1file9

The cost-correctness issues are real and urgent. I verified `_session_level_estimate` returns `None`; subscription pricing lacks the newer Opus keys named in the file; `cost_compute.py` hardcodes a Pro-tier `$20 / 21,700,000 credits` conversion; `cost_enrichment.py` can replace a stored exact estimate with a re-derived priced estimate; day/week summaries aggregate physical profiles while logical counts are tracked separately. The file’s provider-lane warnings are exactly the kind of bug that invalidates public findings if left unresolved. fileciteturn2file12turn2file8

The daily workflow section is valuable because it shifts from substrate nouns to operator journeys: resume work, postmortem failures, bundle external context, cite motivating sessions, compare attempts, recall exact errors, save/run queries, and check freshness. These are not “nice UX.” They are the practical surfaces that make the archive worth using every day. fileciteturn2file18

The observability/SLO ideas are good: Polylogue needs to distinguish idle-healthy from stalled, keep ingest/convergence success rates, detect poison rows stuck under retry/`false_means_pending`, and retain ops-history for regression baselining. This fits the disposable `ops.db` tier and should not pollute user evidence. fileciteturn2file9

## Hard vetting: refuted or corrected

`Goal` should not introduce `author_kind="operator"` casually if the recursive-safety rule elsewhere requires `author_kind='user'` for injection. The actual invariant should be trust-class based: agent/miner/authored-by-model rows are candidate and `inject:false`; human/operator-promoted rows may become active/injectable. If the enum uses `operator`, then the injection gate must know `operator` is the trusted human class. If it uses `user`, the goal spec should say `user`, not `operator`. This mismatch is small but load-bearing.

`GOAL` as a new `AssertionKind` is reasonable, but I would first ask whether it should be `kind=RUN_STATE` or `kind=JUDGMENT` with `key=goal`. New kinds are cheap at the database layer, but not free at the product layer: generated schemas, audit surfaces, OpenAPI, CLI schemas, MCP contracts, and UI filters all need updates. The file knows this trap; the correction is to require a “new kind justification” checklist before adding `GOAL`, `PROMPT_TEMPLATE`, or any new assertion vocabulary.

`decision-object` should not store supersession only as `value.superseded_by` long-term. That is acceptable as phase one, but read performance, auditing, and graph queries will want a normalized edge view or runtime edge extractor with cycle checks. Since SQLite persistent views cannot cross attached tiers, the right boundary is a runtime query method over user assertions, not a persistent cross-tier view.

`.polydemo` finding IDs should not hash mutable human phrasing as the only identity. Hashing `claim` catches drift, which is good for CI, but it also makes harmless wording changes look like new findings. I would split this into two IDs: a stable `finding_semantic_id` over metric, corpus datasheet, construct, evidence refs, and anchor; and a `finding_render_id` or artifact hash over the human claim text. CI can decide which drift is fatal.

Content variants should not be only a user-tier table if variant bodies can be large. Durable metadata belongs in `user.db`, but generated text bodies and alignment payloads may need blob storage or a body table with content hashes. Otherwise translations/summaries of long transcripts will bloat user.db and complicate backup/merge semantics. The design should explicitly split metadata from variant payload storage.

Cross-machine sync should not keep both `user_settings` and “settings as assertions.” The file’s sync design includes user settings merge, while the broader config direction says the `user_settings` table is dead and settings should unify into assertions. Pick one. My recommendation: new settings use assertions; legacy `user_settings` gets a copy-forward/deprecation path and is excluded from new sync semantics except for migration compatibility.

The prompt/meta-workflow distillery is high-risk and should be later than the file’s implementation detail implies. The design is honest about candidate-only birth, A/B evaluator floors, and recursive contamination. But observational prompt induction is a causal minefield; treat it as hypothesis mining, not as “distillation” until controlled treatment data exists. Candidate templates must be excluded from their own evidence loops. fileciteturn2file2turn2file15

The missing insight units need stricter priority. `project` is likely useful soon because it helps scope everything else. `topic-cluster` and `cross-origin-thread` are riskier: embeddings, hub-merge, candidate explosion, and label stability will make them expensive. The file already names hard-signal floors and blocking; the correction is to ship them as insight-registry candidates before DSL units, unless a live query demands them. fileciteturn1file12turn1file3

MCP collapse should not be treated as purely a tool-count cleanup. It is an agent-attention and compatibility migration. The current MCP standard separates tools, resources, and prompts; resources are for data/context, prompts are reusable templates/workflows, and tools are executable functions. That supports moving many current read affordances away from tools, but only with compatibility shims and usage telemetry. citeturn837479search0turn837479search1

The release/versioning section’s “decision, not build” stance is only partly true. Local files confirm version `0.1.0` and docs that say PyPI/Homebrew/container/browser-store are not user install paths yet. I did not verify “zero git tags” against a live remote. Even if distribution machinery exists, cold-machine install verification, docs reconciliation, generated metadata, and release artifact provenance are real work.

## External context that should change the designs

Polylogue’s analysis objects should borrow from W3C PROV: entities, activities, agents, usage, generation, derivation, and association. That maps almost perfectly to sessions, queries, query runs, agents, evidence packs, generated reports, content variants, and prompt templates. This is stronger than inventing isolated “demo finding,” “analysis run,” “variant,” and “prompt eval” graphs separately. citeturn643610search0turn643610search4

RO-Crate is relevant for portable evidence bundles: it packages research objects with metadata about files, workflows, people/organizations, provenance, and context entities. A Polylogue evidence pack or `.polydemo` artifact should be able to export into an RO-Crate-like shape later, even if the first implementation is internal JSON/Markdown. citeturn643610search1turn643610search17

The Web Annotation Data Model supports motivations such as classifying, commenting, describing, editing, highlighting, and questioning. That argues for a structured `motivation`/`kind`/`purpose` axis on external annotations and assertions rather than stuffing everything into prose notes. citeturn643610search2turn643610search14

SQLite’s own documentation reinforces the single-writer rule: multiple processes can read, but only one writer can commit at a time; WAL also uses a shared-memory wal-index, so readers and writers need same-machine assumptions. This matters for cross-machine sync: do not rsync live WAL-era SQLite files and do not allow peer merge paths that bypass the daemon/single-writer boundary. citeturn643610search7turn643610search3

Litestream and LiteFS are useful comparisons but not direct substitutes. Litestream continuously copies WAL pages for async disaster recovery; LiteFS replicates SQLite through a distributed filesystem model. Polylogue’s desired sync is not block/WAL replication; it is semantic durable-tier merge with source idempotency and user assertion conflict rules. citeturn779583search1turn779583search0

Hypothesis-style property and stateful testing is the right tool for migration fuzz, sync merge commutativity, and state-machine candidate lifecycles. The important point is to model operation sequences, not only generate values. citeturn837479search7turn837479search3

OpenTelemetry’s semantic conventions are a useful prior for naming observability measurements, but Polylogue should not blindly adopt unstable conventions. Use the pattern—standardized names, units, attributes, and status semantics—not necessarily every metric name. citeturn837479search4turn837479search8

Provider pricing and token semantics must be treated as live external facts, not as static internal doctrine. Anthropic’s official pricing docs distinguish cache writes and cache reads; OpenAI’s pricing exposes input, cached input, and output; Gemini’s docs say output price includes thinking tokens and context caching has separate pricing/storage. That supports the file’s disjoint-lane cost model, but also means rates and inclusions need a live-source update path and tests. citeturn754182search0turn754182search1turn754182search2

## Design synthesis

The missing unifier is an **analysis/provenance object model**. File 5 independently proposes `.polydemo`, prompt evals, adoption experiments, query recall, saved views, content variants, sync manifests, and daily workflow commands. These should not become separate silos.

The shared model should be:

`query_definition → query_run → result_relation/cohort → evidence_pack → annotation_batch/assertions → analysis_run → report/demo artifact`

A query definition is the reusable dynamic object. A query run is a specific execution against an archive epoch. A result relation has grain, identity policy, exactness, and member refs. A cohort is a named dynamic or snapshot relation. An annotation batch imports external/agent judgments as assertions under a schema. An analysis run ties queries, cohorts, annotation batches, evidence packs, reports, and artifacts into a provenance DAG. This single model makes `.polydemo`, prompt distillery, activation A/B tests, Fable-style delegation analysis, and daily saved queries all composable.

The second unifier is **candidate-by-default for derived human-meaning claims**. Goals, decisions, prompt templates, topic clusters, cross-origin threads, and mined findings should all begin as candidate/private/non-injectable unless they come from a structured human/operator command or are explicitly judged. This is not just safety. It preserves construct validity.

The third unifier is **tier discipline**. Source and user data are durable and mergeable only through explicit migration/single-writer paths. Index/embeddings are rebuilt or blue-green swapped. Ops is disposable and ideal for query runs, context compile runs, SLO samples, adoption telemetry, and daemon state. The file mostly respects this, but some designs blur user.db into a general blob/artifact store and blur sync into settings/config.

## Prioritized take

Tier 0: fix cost truth and assertion safety first. The cost issues are concrete and public-finding-breaking. The assertion safety chokepoint is a recursive-contamination risk now that Polylogue captures its own R&D.

Tier 1: land `.polydemo`/finding reproducibility and adoption/install/doctor. These turn the system into an externally inspectable proof engine and make agent use measurable.

Tier 2: thin the API/MCP/SDK boundary. MCP collapse, SDK boundary, and daily CLI workflows should route through the same query/read/action contract. Do not build more surfaces that duplicate substrate logic.

Tier 3: add query/result/cohort/analysis objects. This is the general substrate behind saved queries, demos, annotation batches, prompt evals, and evidence reports.

Tier 4: content variants and project unit. These are useful, but must respect payload storage and provenance boundaries.

Tier 5: cross-machine sync, topic clustering, cross-origin threads, and prompt distillery. These are promising but higher-risk, and should be gated by evidence, small pilots, and clear false-merge/causal-validity floors.

import json, textwrap
issues={}
for l in open('polylogue-beads-export.jsonl'):
    d=json.loads(l)
    if d.get('_type')=='issue': issues[d['id']]=d
for id in ['polylogue-7xv','polylogue-f2qv','polylogue-w8db','polylogue-mhx','polylogue-mhx.4','polylogue-kwsb','polylogue-37t','polylogue-37t.11','polylogue-3tl','polylogue-3tl.4','polylogue-jnj','polylogue-cpf','polylogue-4ts','polylogue-83u','polylogue-fnm','polylogue-t46','polylogue-9l5','polylogue-gjg','polylogue-4p1','polylogue-bby','polylogue-20d','polylogue-s7ae']:
    b=issues.get(id)
    print('\n',id, 'exists', bool(b))
    if b:
        print('P',b.get('priority'),'type',b.get('issue_type'),'status',b.get('status'),'title',b.get('title'))
        print('desc', textwrap.shorten((b.get('description') or '').replace('\n',' | '), 250))
        print('design', textwrap.shorten((b.get('design') or '').replace('\n',' | '), 300))
        print('acc', textwrap.shorten((b.get('acceptance_criteria') or '').replace('\n',' | '), 250))

import json, re, textwrap
issues=[]
for l in open('polylogue-beads-export.jsonl'):
 d=json.loads(l)
 if d.get('_type')=='issue': issues.append(d)
terms=['episode','compaction','cost','provider usage','config','runtime','search relevance','ranking','security','recall','MCP','docs onboarding','temporal','time','SDK','python api','launch','entity mention','verification','world effect','setting','f2qv','gjg','w8db','y4c','9l5','mcp','3tl','cpf','mhx','37t','bby','a5e']
for term in terms:
    matches=[i for i in issues if term.lower() in (' '.join(str(i.get(k,'')) for k in ['id','title','description','design','labels'])).lower()]
    if matches:
        print('\nTERM',term, len(matches))
        for i in matches[:15]: print(i['id'],i.get('priority'),i.get('status'),i.get('issue_type'),i.get('title')[:100])
PY

## [assistant 431]
According to a document from 2026-07-05, I treated `rnd-bundle-6-of-6.md` as **file 6 of 6** and anchored this review to its Part 2 payload, not to the shared master synthesis. The file itself says the unique payload begins after the divider and contains this file’s subagent outputs; I used the preamble only for orientation and collision avoidance. fileciteturn2file10

## Executive verdict

File 6 is one of the stronger slices. Its center of gravity is not “more analytics.” It is the infrastructure that makes Polylogue useful as a real substrate: episode stitching, compaction forensics, cost truth, runtime preferences, search relevance, security hardening, recall, MCP ergonomics, docs/onboarding, temporal doctrine, and public SDK shape.

The strongest conclusions survive adversarial review:

The **cost-accounting defects** are real and urgent. Physical-session rollups, dead provider-reported cost reads, missing current-model credit rates, and hardcoded Pro-tier subscription math are all concrete correctness failures, not speculative design debt. fileciteturn3file3

The **daemon/browser-capture security concerns** are real. DNS rebinding and forged local browser captures are credible attack classes for a loopback daemon that trusts missing `Origin` or lacks `Host` gating; the receiver token and Host/Origin middleware direction is correct, but must not overclaim protection against hostile same-user processes. fileciteturn3file17turn3file18

The **episode unit** is conceptually right but must be more conservative than the initial design. Cross-session “same task” inference is useful only if false merges are prevented by hard corroborators, durable reject/confirm/split judgments, and a visible candidate tier. The file’s false-merge tests are exactly the kind of construct-validity guard this feature needs. fileciteturn2file7turn2file8

The **MCP surface redesign** is directionally correct. Polylogue should not present dozens of near-duplicate tools to agents when the read DSL, resources, and prompts can carry most of the surface. The MCP spec distinguishes resources as URI-addressed contextual data, tools as model-invoked actions, and prompts as reusable interaction templates; it also has capabilities for resource subscription and list-change notifications, which directly support the “continuity API” direction. fileciteturn3file12 citeturn129470search1turn129470search5turn129470search19

The most important correction is prioritization: **do not ship all of this as one frontier wave.** Cost truth, security, config-state cleanup, temporal correctness, and MCP/recall ergonomics are high-leverage. Episodes, ranking-learning, broad entity graphs, SDK/Arrow polish, and launch/docs are valuable, but should be gated behind the credibility fixes and the first external artifact.

## What I confirmed

### Cost accounting is the clearest Tier-0 file-6 item

The cost slice is unusually well grounded. It identifies two rollup paths that sum physical sessions instead of logical sessions, the dead `session_reported_costs` read path, missing current-model credit rates, Pro-tier hardcoding, and the absence of a strict strength lattice for cost provenance. The strongest file-local evidence is the defect table: day/week summaries sum physical profiles; cost rollups sum `total_usd` over physical session insights; `_session_level_estimate` returns `None`; `session_reported_costs` is written but not read; current Opus/Sonnet model rates are absent; and subscription USD uses `credit_cost / 21_700_000 * 20.0`. fileciteturn3file3

My verification against the code snapshot confirmed the core defects. The only nuance: the phrase “every subscription-cost figure is silently $0” is too broad if read literally. Catalog-priced/token-derived paths can still produce numbers. The narrower and correct statement is: **provider-reported session-level exact costs are dead, and current-model subscription-credit costs can collapse to zero because the current model credit rates are missing.** That is enough to block external cost claims.

The design should land as one `f2qv` correctness lane, not scattered fixes. It needs one shared cost provenance lattice:

`provider_reported > subscription_credit > catalog_api_equivalent > heuristic > unavailable`

No path should demote within the lattice unless explicitly marked as a fallback. Every output should carry `cost_view = api_equivalent | subscription_credit | provider_reported`, subscription tier assumptions, and an “unconfigured tier” warning rather than silently defaulting to Pro.

### Security hardening is not optional

The security slice correctly distinguishes real risks from residuals. Host/Origin validation before dispatch is the right fix for browser-mediated attacks against loopback services. The browser-capture receiver needs an always-on token or HMAC-like authorization, constant-time comparison, and spool quotas. Query-string bearer tokens should be scoped to routes that actually need EventSource compatibility, not accepted globally. The threat model must keep saying that a hostile same-user process can still read local token files and SQLite databases unless OS/disk protections prevent it. fileciteturn3file17turn3file18

External context strengthens this. GitHub’s DNS-rebinding writeup shows local web apps remain attackable when they trust loopback without robust host/origin validation, and Chrome’s Private Network Access work adds browser preflights but does not remove the server’s obligation to reject bad requests itself. citeturn129470search3turn129470search4

My correction: **do not frame this as “authenticated browser capture” without a threat-class qualifier.** It is “authenticated against confused-deputy browser pages and unauthenticated local POSTs.” It is not “secure against malicious same-user local code.”

### Episodes are useful, but only with candidate-first semantics

The episode unit is a good abstraction: a logical task spanning sessions, providers, cwd roots, time, artifacts, and commits. It should sit above provider lineage/threads, not replace them. The proposed placement is mostly right: derived episode tables in `index.db`, session-level embeddings in `embeddings.db`, and durable human/operator stitch judgments in `user.db.assertions`. The file correctly notes that `session_embeddings` do not exist yet and proposes `message_centroid` as the cheap default over existing message vectors. fileciteturn2file7

The hard false-merge floor is the most important part. Same title, same day, high embedding similarity, or same theme must never be enough to merge sessions. Shared SHA, shared error fingerprint, strong same-repo+time evidence, or explicit user confirmation should be required for corroborated+ edges. The test suite proposed in the file is the right bar: high-embed/different-repo pairs must remain candidates; shared-SHA cross-provider pairs should link; reject/split/confirm judgments must survive rebuild. fileciteturn2file8

My correction: connected components over corroborated edges can still create **transitive over-merge**. If A↔B and B↔C are strong but A and C have negative evidence, naïve connected components merge all three. Episode materialization needs cut constraints and maybe component-level consistency checks, not only pairwise scoring. The file includes split constraints, but acceptance should explicitly test this chain case.

### Compaction lifecycle belongs in durable source/provenance, not only index summaries

The compaction lifecycle design is right in spirit: Polylogue should record compaction boundaries, what was retained/lost/transformed, and how later sessions re-ground lost facts. The file correctly reuses existing concepts: `context-snapshot` refs already exist, content-addressed blobs can deduplicate large snapshots, `session_events(event_type='compaction')` marks boundaries, and `AssertionKind` can grow schema-free. fileciteturn3file0

The risk analysis is also good. PreCompact hooks may not actually carry the assembled context, so capture tier must be honest. “Loss” cannot mean “model forgot,” because summaries may semantically preserve a fact in transformed form. Durable records should store refs, not giant injected prose in `user.db`, and snapshot blobs need retention/purge policy. fileciteturn3file0

My correction: this subsystem should align with a general provenance model. W3C PROV describes provenance as entities, activities, and agents involved in producing data, and OpenTelemetry traces model operations with spans, attributes, events, links, and parent-child relationships. Polylogue does not need to implement either standard wholesale, but compaction events, query runs, analysis runs, and replay plans should all look like provenance DAG nodes, not bespoke one-off tables. citeturn844460search5turn844460search4

### The missing-units slice is mostly correct

The three missing units are valuable because they turn implicit evidence into queryable relations.

`entity-mention` should start as a table, but only structural mentions should be trusted by default. Prose-regex candidates should be candidate-tier, recursive-safety-gated, and capped for confidence. The file itself flags the high false-positive risk for hex IDs, code symbols, and broad regex extraction. fileciteturn3file10

`world-effect` is a good view if the cause comes from explicit observed-event evidence refs to producing actions. It should not infer causality from time adjacency except as a lower-trust optional branch. The file’s proposed `session_observed_events → evidence_refs_json[0] → blocks → actions` path is the right structural spine. fileciteturn3file10

`verification-run` is useful, but the first version should not rely on broad string matching like `LIKE '%test%'` unless it is clearly confidence-tiered. It should reuse or introduce a central command classifier so the same classification feeds claim-vs-evidence, replay, and analytics.

### Config/runtime preferences should not revive `user_settings`

The config slice is correct that deployment config and runtime preferences are different things. `config.py` already handles deployment-layer config; the dead `user_settings` table should not become a second, half-wired state store. The file notes that `user_settings` exists but has no read/write helpers, while assertions already have scope, target, key, value, author, staleness, context policy, status, and supersession fields. fileciteturn2file11

The proposed settings-as-assertions direction is pragmatic, but semantically delicate. A preference is not always an epistemic assertion. I would still use `AssertionKind.SETTING` or an assertion-compatible row shape, but enforce a registry that separates deployment secrets from runtime preferences. The file’s risk list correctly calls out deployment/runtime bleed and secret leakage as the top issue. fileciteturn1file5

The design should require:

A closed registry for runtime keys.

A deployment-only partition for secrets.

Batched scope resolution, not one DB query per setting.

`author_kind=agent` settings must default to candidate and never auto-apply.

A migration that either proves `user_settings` empty or copy-forwards it into assertions with a backup manifest.

### Search relevance needs eval-first discipline

The search relevance slice points in the right direction: collapse duplicate search paths, add `why` explanations, collect relevance judgments, and use `AssertionKind.RELEVANCE` / labels for evaluation. The broader bundle says search resolution currently lives in two paths and should collapse into one shared helper; it also calls out `variant_count`/lineage sibling duplication as a real class of bug. fileciteturn1file13

The external context matters here. Reciprocal Rank Fusion is a well-known IR method for combining multiple result rankings and is scale-insensitive across different scoring systems, which fits Polylogue’s lexical/vector/hybrid setup. citeturn844460search3

My correction: do not add MMR, learning-to-rank, model-weight tuning, or ranker knobs before there is an evaluation corpus. Phase one should be “one resolution path + explainable score decomposition + relevance labels + nDCG/MRR gate.” Only after enough labeled queries exist should Polylogue tune RRF constants, recency weights, or diversity reranking. Also, session-level diversity reranking depends on session embeddings, so it should either depend on the episode/session-embeddings work or stay message-level.

### Recall is a strong near-term agent affordance

The `recall(task_hint)` MCP tool is one of the best file-6 ideas. The load-bearing primitive exists: `VectorProvider.query(text, limit)` embeds arbitrary text and KNN-searches stored message embeddings, whereas existing similar-session flows are session-seeded rather than free-text-seeded. The file’s proposed MCP tool contract makes recall cross-repo by default, attaches lessons/blockers/corrections/pathologies, carries token budget, and uses `min_similarity` instead of padding weak hits. fileciteturn2file2turn2file9

The risk analysis is exactly right: query embedding needs a live provider key, so FTS fallback must be explicit; and trust-class laundering is the main danger. Recall can become a prompt-injection amplifier if an agent-authored lesson is surfaced as operator doctrine. fileciteturn2file9

My correction: the first recall payload should be structured JSON plus a rendered Markdown view, not only a string. Agents need stable refs, trust class, retrieval lane, score, evidence refs, and “why included.” The human-readable report can be a renderer over the payload.

### MCP should become resource/prompt-first, not tool-heavy

The MCP slice’s thesis is correct: Polylogue should not expose a flat wall of tools when it has a DSL, resources, and saved views. The file says Polylogue already has static resources, hardcoded prompts, many tools, and read/write/admin gating; the gaps are resource subscriptions/list-changed and user-authored prompts from saved recall packs/views. fileciteturn2file1

I refute the precise tool count in the file for the code snapshot I inspected. I found fewer than “~130” concrete `@mcp.tool()` definitions and a lower `EXPECTED_TOOL_NAMES` count than that. But the strategic conclusion survives: there are too many overlapping tools, and read operations should move toward `query(expression)` and resource fetches.

The MCP spec supports this directly: resources are URI-addressed context, tools are invocable actions, prompts are reusable templates, and the schema includes resource `subscribe` and `listChanged` capabilities. citeturn129470search1turn129470search5turn129470search19

### Python SDK / library consumer surface is real, but the “async-only” diagnosis is overstated

The file’s SDK slice identifies the right consumer problem: external code reaches into internals, reimplements models, or reads SQLite because there is no small, stable, versioned public surface. That is a real issue. The proposed `polylogue.sdk` / `polylogue.models`, query objects, and columnar bridges are appropriate.

But I would not state “the facade is async-only” as an absolute for the current package snapshot. I saw a sync API namespace in the code tree. The stronger, safer conclusion is: **the public SDK boundary is not stable or attractive enough, so consumers still bypass it.** Build the narrow SDK and model namespace; do not over-index on sync-wrapper as if nothing exists.

### Docs and launch are execution, not more invention

The docs/onboarding slice is practical and should land. A demo-corpus golden path, doc commands that actually execute, “How do I…?” recipes, a query ladder above the grammar, `polylogue explain "<query>"`, and a narrated tour are exactly the missing bridge between powerful substrate and first value. fileciteturn3file13

The product/launch and red-team slices are also correct in the uncomfortable way. The 80/20 minimal core is not enough to be Polylogue, but it is a useful adversarial baseline. The file’s own counter is the right one: keep the cheap differentiators that grep cannot reproduce — `material_origin`, real continuity tools, content-hash idempotency, and split-tier durability — and defer museum-like analytics until live use demands them. fileciteturn3file5turn2file15

## What I refute or downgrade

The tool count in the MCP slice is probably stale or rounded up. The exact number should be regenerated from the current `EXPECTED_TOOL_NAMES` and decorators before any deletion plan. The conclusion “collapse the surface” is right; the claim “~130” should not be used as a cited fact without live regeneration.

The cost slice should not say all costs are zero or every cost path is dead. Provider-reported exact session totals are dead; current-model credit rates are missing; subscription-tier math is hardcoded; rollups double-count lineage. These are severe enough without overstatement.

The SDK slice should not say “async-only” without qualification. The gap is stable public SDK/DTO/columnar ergonomics, not necessarily total absence of sync access.

The security slice should not imply loopback auth solves same-user compromise. It solves browser/network confused deputy and forged local receiver traffic. Same-user residual remains.

The episode slice should not trust connected components alone. Add component consistency tests for transitive false merges.

The entity-mention slice should not ship broad prose/code-symbol mining as fact. Start structural-first, candidate-second.

The launch slice should not create another docs/product iceberg. It should cut to: release tag, cold install proof, one demo-corpus first-value path, one reproducible finding, one short screencast.

## External prior art and design pressure

There are four external anchors worth importing into the design.

First, provenance should be a first-class mental model. W3C PROV’s entity/activity/agent framing and OpenTelemetry’s span/event/link model both support a general “what produced this?” graph. This argues for representing compaction events, recall runs, query runs, evidence packs, replay plans, and reports as linked provenance objects rather than isolated feature tables. citeturn844460search5turn844460search4

Second, replay/reproduction should be conservative. ReproZip is strong prior art for tracing command executions and dependencies into reproducible packages; it shows the right ambition, but also why Polylogue should start with **dry reconstruction and replay plans**, not promises of exact deterministic replay. citeturn844460search2turn844460search18

Third, MCP should use its three primitives properly. Official MCP resources, tools, and prompts map neatly onto Polylogue’s needs: resources for session/query/result state, tools for side effects, prompts for saved workflows/recall packs. Resource subscription/list-change support is especially relevant to live continuity. citeturn129470search1turn129470search5turn129470search19

Fourth, hybrid search should respect IR practice. RRF is a defensible default for fusing rankings, but learning/reranking should be evaluation-gated. The RRF paper’s value is that it fuses rankings simply; it is not a license to add a pile of ranker knobs without labels. citeturn844460search3

## Prioritized take

Tier 0: fix credibility and safety. Land cost correctness, browser/daemon security hardening, config-state cleanup, and temporal clock/doctrine. These directly protect the “honest system of record” claim.

Tier 1: make agents happier immediately. Land `recall(task_hint)` with trust classes and FTS fallback, collapse MCP reads toward `query`/resources, make saved views/recall packs discoverable prompts, and add docs/onboarding that executes against demo data.

Tier 2: enrich the relational substrate. Add missing units where they are structurally grounded: `entity-mention`, `world-effect`, `verification-run`. Add compaction snapshots and loss records, but keep them provenance-linked and retention-aware.

Tier 3: build frontier analytics only after evidence exists. Episode stitching is worthwhile but should be candidate-first and false-merge-gated. Search ranking improvements should wait on relevance labels and eval. SDK/Arrow outputs should follow the service contract, not precede it.

Tier 4: launch discipline. Publish one finding and one working install/demo route before adding more surfaces.

## [assistant 360]
I take A11 as the brief: design `find <query> | compact` as a token-budgeted, decision-dense corpus digest for external LLM handoff, with block scoring, lineage dedup, budget fitting, and an honest drop manifest. The snapshot is dated 2026-07-05, so code-line claims below should be verified locally before turning this into Beads or implementation work. fileciteturn1file0

## Defended recommendation

[proposal] Implement `compact` as a **new projection/render preset over the existing read algebra**, not as a new context subsystem and not as a mutation/action. Concretely:

```text
find <query> | compact --budget 60000 --audience external-llm --manifest full
```

should lower to:

```text
SelectionSpec(query)
→ CompactProjectionSpec(scoring_policy, lineage_policy, budget_policy, manifest_policy)
→ RenderSpec(format=markdown|json, layout=corpus-compaction-pack)
```

The output should be a `CorpusCompactionPack` envelope with two renderable parts: a human/LLM-facing digest and a machine/auditor-facing manifest. The digest is what you paste into GPT-pro/Gemini; the manifest is what lets a later Polylogue run, or a skeptical auditor, reconstruct what was included, summarized, deduplicated, clipped, or dropped.

[evidence] This fits the current architectural direction better than a new subsystem because the swarm brief already defines the read surface as `Query × Projection × Render`, with Query selecting sessions/units, Projection choosing evidence families/body policy/exclusions, and Render deciding format/destination/layout. It also explicitly says named views are currently a closed preset vocabulary and should move toward composable projection algebra and user-defined views/macros. fileciteturn1file4

Runner-up rejected: extend `build_context_image` / `compile_context` with a `detail_level="corpus_compact"` mode. That is tempting because those already have token-budgeted context images and omission accounting. I reject it because `compile_context` is a seed/ref handoff compiler; `compact` is a **cohort optimizer**. It needs cross-session ranking, lineage-family dedup, block-level material-origin filtering, fairness constraints, external-LLM manifests, and decision-density scoring. If we shove this into `ContextImage`, `ContextImage` becomes a second read algebra.

## Layer 1 — today’s substrate

[evidence] Polylogue is already surprisingly close on the primitives. `messages.material_origin` exists precisely because role is not enough: Claude Code can carry command wrappers, provider context bundles, and tool-result envelopes through `role=user`, so `material_origin` is the authoredness/material axis for projections and accounting (`docs/data-model.md:72-85`; `polylogue/core/enums.py:176-192`). That directly supports A11’s instruction to drop `runtime_protocol`, `runtime_context`, and most `tool_result` material. fileciteturn1file0

[evidence] The tool-result side is also not merely prose. `blocks` has `tool_result_is_error` and `tool_result_exit_code`, and the `actions` view exposes paired tool-use/tool-result rows with `is_error` and `exit_code` (`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/index.py:182-224`, `324-343`; `docs/internals.md:175-185`). This matters because `compact` should keep error→fix pairs and terminal outcomes based on structure, not regex vibes.

[evidence] Lineage dedup is also partially there. The lineage model says fork/resume/subagent/auto-compaction copies physically replay parent context, and index schema v12 stores only the divergent tail plus `session_links.branch_point_message_id` and `inheritance`, while reads compose parent prefix + child tail (`docs/internals.md:214-224`). The design doc’s decision is “default reporting unit: logical,” with physical artifacts still recoverable (`docs/design/session-lineage-model.md:171-176`). The earlier session also confirmed prefix-dedup and logical composition are load-bearing parts of the live direction. fileciteturn1file2

[evidence] `compile_context` / `build_context_image` already prove the product has the right “bounded context image with omissions” instinct. `compile_context` is documented as reusing query/read primitives and recording unsupported or missing inputs as omissions, not creating a parallel memory store (`polylogue/api/archive.py:2271-2277`). `ContextImage` already carries `segments`, `object_refs`, `evidence_refs`, `assertion_refs`, `omitted`, `caveats`, and `token_estimate` (`polylogue/context/compiler.py:103-117`). The MCP `build_context_image` tool is explicitly a thin lens over the same shared compiler and mentions token-budgeted accumulation and omission accounting (`polylogue/mcp/server_context_tools.py:1-8`, `48-67`).

[evidence] But today’s context image is not enough. It picks seed sessions, compiles `messages`, `temporal`, `chronicle`, query-unit rows, and injectable assertions; it uses bounded message windows and a tail-biased token fit (`polylogue/api/archive.py:301-365`, `368-415`, `2356-2495`). `context_image_payload` clamps `max_sessions` to 20 and defaults to message windows (`polylogue/api/archive.py:2518-2575`). That is useful for handoff, but it is not a corpus compactor.

[evidence] The single-client contract is also not ready yet. B8 says the projection algebra exists as `QueryProjectionSpec = SelectionSpec × ProjectionSpec × RenderSpec`, but live `read` still executes named views and `projection_spec.py` is “a contract builder, not an executor.” B8 also says there is no single wire request DTO and `preview` does not yet exist. fileciteturn1file12

So: today, Polylogue can fake this by `find <query>`, `read --view context-image`, and maybe external summarization. It cannot yet do the thing A11 wants honestly and repeatably.

## Layer 2 — near-term substrate change

[proposal] Add `compact` as a **projection preset first**, not a whole analysis framework. The near-term target is a deterministic, non-LLM compactor that produces an evidence pack good enough for a GPT/Gemini handoff.

The syntax should be something like:

```text
polylogue find 'repo:polylogue semantic:"hot daemon composer"' \
  | compact --budget 60000 --layout external-llm --manifest full
```

and later, in the composer:

```text
find repo:polylogue semantic:"delegation rhetoric"
  | compact budget:60k audience:gemini
```

The output envelope:

```json
{
  "kind": "CorpusCompactionPack",
  "pack_ref": "compact:...",
  "query_ref": "query-run:...",
  "result_relation_ref": "result:...",
  "budget": {"target_tokens": 60000, "estimated_tokens": 58740},
  "digest_markdown": "...",
  "manifest": {...},
  "evidence_refs": [...]
}
```

### Block-selection scoring

[proposal] The scorer should operate on candidate blocks/windows, not whole sessions. The selected query gives a cohort of logical sessions; each logical session yields candidate units:

`message`, `block`, `action`, `assertion`, `session_event`, `session_summary`, `terminal_outcome`, and eventually `artifact`.

The first pass is hard filtering:

```text
drop by default:
  material_origin in {runtime_protocol, runtime_context}
  material_origin == generated_context_pack unless explicitly requested
  block_type == tool_result if success, long, and unreferenced
  low-signal context boilerplate, provider wrappers, repeated tool stdout

keep by default:
  material_origin in {human_authored, operator_command}
  assistant_authored messages with decisions, plans, results, contradictions
  tool_result blocks with is_error=1 or nonzero exit_code
  tool_use/tool_result pairs that form error→fix→verify chains
  final summaries, terminal outcomes, merged PR/commit/verification summaries
  assertions/judgments attached to selected sessions
  compaction summaries and continuation boundaries
```

[evidence] This filter is grounded in the data model: `material_origin` exists to distinguish human-authored prose from provider/runtime material, and structured tool-result outcomes exist specifically to avoid regex-guessing failures (`docs/data-model.md:76-85`; `docs/internals.md:175-185`). The situation brief also identifies structured tool outcomes, error flags, and exit codes as Polylogue’s sharpest defensible wedge. fileciteturn1file13

[proposal] After filtering, score each candidate with an additive score vector:

```text
score =
  + query_relevance                 # lexical/semantic hit score
  + authoredness_weight             # human/operator > assistant > generated
  + decision_signal                 # "decided", "we will", "root cause", "recommendation"
  + outcome_signal                  # "merged", "verified", "tests pass", terminal status
  + error_fix_signal                # failed action + subsequent fix + later success
  + contradiction_signal            # claim vs tool outcome mismatch, if present
  + novelty_within_lineage_family   # not already represented by ancestor/sibling
  + artifact_link_signal            # commit/report/file/link attached
  + recency_or_terminal_position    # late-session summaries/outcomes
  + diversity_bonus                 # covers another session/model/task
  - spam_penalty                    # runtime/tool/protocol bulk
  - redundancy_penalty              # duplicate text/prefix/repeated stdout
  - length_penalty                  # huge block with low density
```

Use named reasons in the manifest, not just a number. A block should say:

```json
"score_reasons": ["human_authored", "query_hit", "decision", "terminal_outcome"]
```

This matters because an external LLM should see why something is present, and an auditor should be able to tell whether the scorer quietly overfit to recency or query relevance.

### Error→fix pair detection

[proposal] Treat a failed action as a small narrative unit, not an isolated block.

A retained error window should include:

1. the command/tool-use summary,
2. the structured failure outcome,
3. the assistant/user interpretation immediately after,
4. the next material fix attempt,
5. the verifying success or terminal unresolved status.

For example:

```text
[ERROR-FIX PAIR ref=action:...]
- failed: pytest tests/foo.py, exit=1
- diagnosis: assistant says fixture path was wrong
- fix: edited tests/foo.py
- verify: pytest tests/foo.py, exit=0
```

This is better than including long stdout or dropping the failure entirely. It directly supports external analysis of agent behavior: “what happened, what did the agent claim, what did the tools say?”

### Lineage dedup

[proposal] `compact` should deduplicate at **logical lineage-family grain**, not by raw text.

Algorithm:

First, group selected physical sessions by logical root / lineage family. Use the existing `session_links` and logical session identity. Within each family, sort by lineage topology and time.

Second, build a composed logical transcript for each selected leaf: inherited parent prefix + divergent tail. But for the compaction pack, emit inherited material **once** per lineage family.

Third, when both parent and child sessions are in the cohort, include:

```text
<<<LINEAGE-FAMILY root=... logical=... selected_physical=N>>>
shared prefix: included once / summarized / dropped
child A tail: included selected blocks
child B tail: included selected blocks
```

Fourth, if the branch point is unresolved or dangling, do not dedup silently. Mark:

```json
"lineage_status": "unresolved",
"dedup_policy": "physical_fallback",
"degraded_reason": "missing branch_point_message_id"
```

[evidence] This follows the existing lineage doctrine: dedup is by lineage, not content hash; default reporting unit is logical; raw physical artifacts remain recoverable (`docs/design/session-lineage-model.md:158-176`). It also avoids the known silent-failure class from earlier lineage bugs, where incomplete composition was dangerous precisely because the user could not tell what was missing. fileciteturn1file6

### Budget fitting

[proposal] Use a **stratified greedy water-fill**, not pure knapsack and not LLM summarization as the first pass.

Pure knapsack maximizes score/token but tends to starve smaller sessions, late-stage outcomes, and minority providers. LLM summarization first is worse: it destroys auditability before the deterministic manifest exists. The compactor should be deterministic first; LLM summarization can be a later optional transform with its own assertion/provenance record.

Budget plan for `B = target_tokens`:

```text
Reserve:
  3%  pack header, methodology, query spec, caveats
  7%  corpus map and per-session skeletal summaries
  10% manifest-visible drop summary / citation table
  80% evidence blocks and dense extracted windows
```

For a 60k pack, that leaves roughly 48k tokens for evidence. For a 200k pack, roughly 160k.

Packing phases:

Phase 0: build candidate inventory with token estimates and score reasons.

Phase 1: include mandatory skeletons for every selected logical session: title, origin/model, date range, query match reason, terminal status, lineage role, and counts by material origin. These are tiny, but prevent the external LLM from thinking omitted sessions do not exist.

Phase 2: include mandatory high-value anchors: human-authored turns, explicit decisions, error→fix pairs, terminal outcomes, and active assertions/judgments.

Phase 3: fill remaining budget using stratified score/token density. The strata should be lineage family, session, task type, provider/model family, and evidence kind. This prevents one massive session from eating the pack.

Phase 4: degrade in this order:
1. clip long retained blocks;
2. collapse contiguous low-value runs into deterministic summaries like “17 successful tool results omitted”;
3. replace low-score sessions with skeleton only;
4. drop whole low-score sessions only if the user asked for hard budget and skeletons exceed budget;
5. if even skeletons exceed budget, emit an index-only pack with explicit failure state.

Never silently trim the tail. The current context compiler is tail-biased because it is for handoff continuity (`polylogue/api/archive.py:368-415`). Corpus compaction should be **decision-density-biased**.

### Fidelity drop-manifest

[proposal] The drop manifest is not optional. It is the feature.

Minimum manifest:

```json
{
  "source": {
    "query_text": "...",
    "lowered_selection": "...",
    "archive_epoch": "...",
    "created_at": "...",
    "projection": "compact:v1"
  },
  "budget": {
    "target_tokens": 60000,
    "estimated_tokens": 58740,
    "estimator": "polylogue_words_v1",
    "hard_budget": true
  },
  "corpus": {
    "logical_sessions_total": 37,
    "physical_sessions_total": 54,
    "lineage_families_total": 12,
    "blocks_considered": 18492,
    "blocks_included": 412,
    "blocks_summarized": 260,
    "blocks_dropped": 17820
  },
  "drop_by_reason": {
    "runtime_protocol": 5021,
    "runtime_context": 817,
    "tool_result_success_spam": 9102,
    "lineage_duplicate_prefix": 2110,
    "budget_low_score": 770,
    "redacted": 0
  },
  "sessions": [
    {
      "logical_session_ref": "...",
      "physical_session_refs": ["..."],
      "included_tokens": 1800,
      "dropped_tokens_estimate": 9200,
      "included_blocks": 21,
      "summarized_blocks": 4,
      "dropped_blocks": 310,
      "lineage_policy": "shared_prefix_once",
      "boundary_markers": ["S001"]
    }
  ],
  "anchors": {
    "S001.M004.B002": "session:.../message:.../block:2"
  }
}
```

Digest markers should be terse but machine-stable:

```text
<<<PACK query_run=qrun:... result=result:... budget=60000>>>

<<<SESSION S001 logical=logical:... physical=session:... origin=claude-code-session tokens=1840>>>
[ANCHOR S001.M012.B000 score=91 reasons=human_authored,query_hit,decision]
User: ...

[ANCHOR S001.A003 score=88 reasons=tool_error,fix_pair]
Tool failed: pytest ..., exit=1
Fix/verify: ...

<<<OMITTED S001 reason=tool_result_success_spam count=87 est_tokens=9400>>>
<<<END SESSION S001>>>
```

The receiving LLM can reason over the digest, but every factual claim can be traced back by anchor. That is what makes this an analysis substrate, not a prompt hack.

## Layer 3 — full direction

[proposal] In the full design, `compact` should become one member of a larger family of **external-analysis projections**:

```text
find <query> | compact
find <query> | evidence-pack
find <query> | specimen-gallery
find <query> | report-pack
find <query> | annotate-with <schema>
```

But `compact` comes first because it unlocks the parallel-R&D flywheel: package the archive’s own prior work, send it to another frontier model, import the returned analysis as assertions, then query those assertions and run the next loop.

[evidence] This aligns with the strategic brief’s binding constraint: the missing gate is demonstrated use that an outsider can see, and the finished demos so far prove honesty/machinery more than agent/operator uplift. fileciteturn1file13 It also matches the raw-log idea of composing long, impactful prompts from filtered AI conversations, raw logs, and dynamic queries instead of dumping everything possibly relevant into context. fileciteturn1file7

[proposal] The full object model should be:

```text
query_definition
query_run
result_relation
compact_pack
external_llm_run
annotation_batch
assertions/judgments
followup_query_run
report_artifact
```

This is where your earlier query-object idea matters. `find <query> | compact` should not just print Markdown. It should optionally record:

```text
query_run_ref
result_relation_ref
compact_pack_ref
render_artifact_ref
```

Then an external LLM’s output can attach to `compact_pack_ref` or `result_relation_ref` as an assertion batch. Later:

```text
assertions where scope:compact_pack:<id> and key:directive_intensity
```

or:

```text
from result:<id> | compact --budget 200k
```

[evidence] C10 already proposed that committed composer runs write recall entries to `user.db` with query text, resolved spec, result fingerprint, and timestamp; named recall entries become macros. fileciteturn0file5 My improvement is to split that into query definition / query run / result relation / render artifact, because a compact pack is not just “history”; it is a reusable analysis object.

## Why this is distinct from `build_context_image` / `compile_context`

[evidence] `build_context_image` is an MCP-facing context assembly tool: select sessions through query algebra, then compile bounded context image payloads with token accumulation and omission accounting (`polylogue/mcp/server_context_tools.py:1-8`, `48-67`). `compile_context` is the shared engine, deliberately not a new memory store or handoff ontology (`polylogue/context/compiler.py:1-6`; `polylogue/api/archive.py:2271-2277`).

[proposal] `compact` should reuse that discipline but not that shape.

`compile_context` answers: “What context should I hand to an agent so it can continue/review/debug?”

`compact` answers: “Given a cohort of sessions, what is the highest-value, lowest-spam, lineage-deduplicated evidence digest for an external model to analyze?”

That difference changes everything: scoring, lineage grouping, retained evidence kinds, budget allocation, and the manifest.

So the implementation should probably share lower-level helpers: token estimation, `ContextSegment`-like sections, evidence refs, omission objects. But the top-level DTO should be separate:

```text
ContextImage              # handoff / continuation
CorpusCompactionPack      # external analysis / R&D flywheel
```

Both are projections over read algebra. Neither should become a silo.

## Browser-auto-capture interaction

[proposal] The browser-auto-capture flywheel should treat external LLM work as first-class evidence.

Flow:

```text
1. Polylogue captures prior local AI sessions and browser R&D.
2. Operator/agent runs: find <query> | compact --budget 200k.
3. Pack is fed to GPT-pro/Gemini/DeepResearch/Fable/whatever.
4. Browser auto-capture imports the external run/result.
5. External output is linked back to compact_pack_ref.
6. Agent imports structured annotations/assertions from the external output.
7. Polylogue queries those annotations for the next compact pack.
```

This is not “browser capture as another ingestion source.” It is “browser capture closes the loop on outsourced cognition.” The digest packages Polylogue’s own past R&D for the next lane, and the captured external lane becomes new archive evidence.

[evidence] The broader project framing is already “local-first archive and analysis layer for AI/agent sessions” across providers, with daemon, browser capture, cost, lineage, and analysis ambitions. fileciteturn1file13 The raw log also repeatedly points at using LLMs to process large prior chat/log corpora into more useful higher-order forms rather than hand-carrying everything. fileciteturn1file15

## Concrete Beads I would add

[proposal] I would add one P1/P2 bead under the query/read-algebra + external-legibility axis:

**`find <query> | compact`: token-budgeted corpus compaction projection**

Description: Build a deterministic corpus-compaction projection over selected AI-session cohorts for external LLM handoff. It scores blocks by authoredness/material origin, query relevance, decision/outcome/error-fix value, and redundancy; deduplicates lineage prefixes; fits a hard token budget; emits an explicit drop manifest with source anchors.

Design:
- Add `CompactProjectionSpec` and `CorpusCompactionPack` payload.
- Add block/window candidate builder over logical sessions.
- Implement material-origin filtering and structured tool-outcome retention.
- Implement lineage-family grouping and shared-prefix dedup.
- Implement stratified greedy budget fitting.
- Render Markdown + JSON manifest.
- Add CLI terminal/projection `| compact`.
- Reuse existing query/read/ref payloads; do not fork `compile_context`.

Acceptance:
- A fixture with runtime protocol/context/tool-result spam compacts to a digest that excludes those blocks by default and reports counts by `material_origin`.
- A fixture with failed tool result → fix → verify keeps the pair and cites all source refs.
- A fork/resume fixture selected with both parent and child includes inherited prefix once and reports duplicate-prefix omissions.
- A 60k-token budget test proves deterministic degradation order: full blocks → clipped blocks → summarized runs → skeleton-only sessions → explicit budget failure.
- Manifest round-trip test: every digest anchor resolves to source session/message/block/action.
- Comparison test proves `read --view context-image` and `| compact` remain separate projections sharing helpers but not payload shape.

Related beads: `4p1`/read algebra, `fnm` pipeline/projection roadmap, `fnm.13` set algebra, `t46` contract-thin surfaces, `20d` interactive performance, `37t` context/memory loop, `4ts` lineage truth, `3tl` external legibility.

## Open questions for the operator

Should `compact` produce only deterministic extraction, or may it optionally call a local/external LLM to summarize low-score runs? My recommendation: deterministic v1 only; LLM summaries become generated analysis packs/assertions in v2.

Should the manifest be included inside the pasted digest, or emitted as a sidecar JSON artifact? My recommendation: both. The pasted digest needs a compact drop summary; the full manifest should be sidecar JSON.

Should `compact` default to logical-session grain even if the query selected physical sessions? My recommendation: yes, with `--physical` as an explicit opt-out.

Should browser-auto-captured external outputs automatically link back to the compact pack that prompted them? My recommendation: yes if the pack ref is present in the prompt header; otherwise offer a manual `polylogue link artifact --derived-from compact:<id>` affordance.

I did not design the full annotation-import loop here; I only connected `compact` to the earlier assertion/annotation/query-object direction.

The exact block-scoring weights should be calibrated on a real corpus slice. The important design claim is the score vector + manifest, not the first constants.
