**[evidence] I did not verify whether `session_profiles` convergence is currently complete on the live archive.** The previous chatlog mentions `w79` session-profile convergence as an unaudited/open thread, so any design relying heavily on `session_profiles` should verify freshness locally before launch. fileciteturn1file15

**[evidence] I did not inspect a live `embeddings.db` for coverage.** The schema exists, but session-summary embedding quality and coverage are unverified.

**[evidence] I did not inspect Sinex/Lynchpin telemetry schemas.** A27 asks to anchor to lynchpin cross-source telemetry, but the uploaded task only names the need; the current bundle snippets do not provide a concrete telemetry schema. fileciteturn0file0

**[evidence] I did not produce a migration PR or bead mutations.** This is a design answer only.

**[proposal] The first implementation should deliberately under-stitch, then use operator-confirm/reject assertions to calibrate.** The product wins by avoiding embarrassing false merges first; better recall can come later.
## [assistant 367]
According to a document from 2026-07-05, the target for `bby.11` is specifically **Webui-v2 evidence cockpit: result-list → linked evidence-graph → citable report**, centered on content-hash citation anchors rather than position-based refs. fileciteturn0file0 fileciteturn1file0 I’m treating the code snapshot as dated; live code may have moved and should be verified locally before implementation.

My recommendation: **keep the `bby.11` stack decision of TypeScript + Preact + Vite, but make Python/Jinja server-rendered HTML the canonical fallback for every route, with Preact as progressive enhancement rather than SPA-or-nothing.** [evidence] `polylogue-bby.11` already chooses Preact/Vite/TypeScript, generated API types, committed built assets, no-CDN/offline posture, and reader/export parity as the architecture direction. [proposal] Tighten that decision: the cockpit is not “a Preact app with some HTML fallback”; it is “the daemon serves semantic HTML and typed JSON; Preact hydrates graph/basket/report interactions when available.”

Runner-up rejected: **pure Jinja/HTMX-style server UI.** [proposal] It is tempting because A09 explicitly requires phone/curl/pandoc usability and progressive enhancement. But the force-directed graph, live evidence basket, report editor, drag/refocus, citation verification overlays, and typed API-client work are much better served by a small typed client. Pure server UI would likely recreate the current JS-in-Python-strings ceiling under a different name. The compromise is SSR-first routes plus typed Preact islands.

## Layer 1 — today’s substrate

[evidence] Polylogue already has the right strategic shape for this: it is described as a local-first system of record for AI work, with durable `source.db` / `user.db`, derived `index.db` / `embeddings.db`, and disposable `ops.db`. The orientation excerpt also says adjacent P2 vision already includes “web workbench v2 (result list → evidence cockpit)” and construct-validity metadata. fileciteturn1file1

[evidence] The current daemon already exposes the raw ingredients of an evidence cockpit. In the snapshot, `polylogue/daemon/http.py` registers `/api/sessions`, `/api/query-units`, `/api/refs/resolve`, `/api/read-view-profiles`, `/api/assertions`, `/api/sessions/:id`, `/api/sessions/:id/messages`, `/api/sessions/:id/read`, `/api/sessions/:id/raw`, `/api/sessions/:id/provenance`, `/api/sessions/:id/topology`, `/api/sessions/:id/topology/parent-chain`, `/api/sessions/:id/similar`, and `/api/sessions/:id/attachments` (`polylogue/daemon/http.py:257-305`). That is already result-list, reader, provenance, lineage, assertions, and attachments.

[evidence] The current web shell is a single Python-assembled HTML document, with JS modules embedded through string substitution. `polylogue/daemon/web_shell.py` calls itself the “MK2 web reader — single-page interactive archive cockpit” and assembles `WEB_SHELL_HTML` from imported CSS/JS modules (`web_shell.py:1-22`). That is exactly the foundation `bby.11` says is no longer enough.

[evidence] The current reader already has message anchors and permalink actions, but these anchors are DOM-safe IDs derived from message IDs, not content-hash citations. `reader_anchor("session"|"message", target_id)` sanitizes the target id into `session-...` or `message-...` (`polylogue/surfaces/payloads.py:551-555`), and the message action rail copies/jumps to those anchors (`polylogue/daemon/web_shell_reader.py:200-219`). Good UI affordance; wrong durability layer for citations.

[evidence] Current public refs are still position-shaped for evidence. `EvidenceRef` is `session_id[::message_id[::block_index]]`, explicitly using `::` because session ids contain colons (`polylogue/core/refs.py:116-171`). `ObjectRef` supports `block:<message_id>:<qualifier>` where the block qualifier is effectively the block index (`core/refs.py:76-114`). User-state target kinds include `block`, but the block identity template is `block:{session_id}:{target_id}` and target id is `message_id:block_index` (`polylogue/core/user_state_targets.py:77-82`; `polylogue/api/user_state_resolver.py:216-247`). This is the key gap: block references exist, but they are still position/index anchored.

[evidence] The `index.db` schema gives sessions and messages `content_hash`, but not blocks. Sessions have `content_hash` at `sessions.content_hash`; messages have `messages.content_hash`; blocks are keyed by `(message_id, position)` and expose `block_id = message_id || ':' || position`, `text`, `tool_name`, `tool_input`, `tool_result_is_error`, `tool_result_exit_code`, etc., but no `content_hash` (`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/index.py:39-75`, `92-126`, `182-209`). The writer computes message content hashes from block content (`write.py:1433-1476`) but writes blocks without a block hash (`write.py:1479-1523`).

[evidence] The current topology layer is useful but insufficient for A09. It models lineage as sessions/nodes/edges, with edge kinds `continuation`, `sidechain`, `fork`, `subagent`, `unknown`, and `unresolved_native`; it reports cycle detection and BFS-ordered nodes (`polylogue/insights/topology.py:1-21`, `34-55`, `126-153`). The HTTP envelope is bounded, returns nodes/edges/readiness/truncation/cycle/unresolved counts, and is consumed by the Lineage tab (`polylogue/daemon/topology_http.py:1-20`, `103-160`). But A09 wants a visual graph keyed by `prefix-sharing` vs `spawned-fresh`, quarantined cycle-break nodes, and branch-point highlighting. Those fields exist lower in `session_links`: `branch_point_message_id`, `inheritance IN ('prefix-sharing','spawned-fresh')`, `status IN ('repaired','quarantined')`, confidence, evidence JSON (`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/index.py:376-400`). The current topology envelope does not surface all of that.

[evidence] User overlays are already first-class enough to reuse. `user.db.assertions` stores `scope_ref`, `target_ref`, `kind`, `value_json`, `body_text`, `author_ref`, `author_kind`, `evidence_refs_json`, `status`, `visibility`, `confidence`, `staleness_json`, `context_policy_json`, and `supersedes_json` (`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/user.py:7-31`). `AssertionClaimPayload` mirrors this into a surface payload with evidence refs and lifecycle fields (`polylogue/surfaces/payloads.py:1465-1505`). The web shell already fetches `/api/user/marks` and `/api/user/annotations` into client state (`web_shell.py:717-735`), and `/api/assertions` lists assertion-backed overlay claims (`http.py:2950-2987`).

[evidence] Recall packs and workspaces are very close to “evidence basket” and “open investigation state.” `upsert_recall_pack` stores a recall-pack assertion with `target_ref=recall_pack:<id>` and `kind=recall_pack` (`user_write.py:591-613`). The API resolves recall-pack items into sessions, messages, annotations, marks, and registered target kinds, recording `resolved_count` and `degraded_count` (`api/archive.py:4834-5066`). The HTTP user-state routes already expose `GET/POST/DELETE /api/user/recall-packs` and `GET/POST/DELETE /api/user/workspaces` (`daemon/user_state_http.py:445-620`). So a crude evidence basket exists in spirit; it just lacks block-hash anchors, report coupling, and citation verification.

## Layer 2 — near-term substrate change

[proposal] The near-term substrate should be **not a rewrite**, but three precise additions: block-hash citation anchors, evidence baskets as user-tier objects, and a citation verifier. This gives `bby.11` enough power without waiting for the full daemon/protocol/composer refactor.

### 1. Anchor format

[proposal] Use this as the canonical textual anchor:

```text
<session_id>::<message_id>::block@sha256:<64-hex>
```

Example shape:

```text
claude-code-session:abc123::claude-code-session:abc123:42.0::block@sha256:7a0f...
```

[evidence] This deliberately reuses the existing `::` separator because Polylogue already notes that session ids are colon-bearing and therefore cannot safely use plain colon segmentation for evidence refs (`polylogue/core/refs.py:116-130`). The A09 mnemonic `session:message:block@<hash>` is the conceptual form; the concrete Polylogue-safe form should use `::`.

[proposal] Store anchors structurally wherever possible:

```json
{
  "anchor_version": 1,
  "kind": "block",
  "session_id_hint": "...",
  "message_id_hint": "...",
  "hash_algo": "sha256",
  "content_hash": "...",
  "position_hint": 3,
  "created_archive_epoch": "...",
  "created_at_ms": 1783210000000
}
```

The Markdown/report form can be compact; the `user.db` form should be structured.

### 2. Block content hash

[proposal] Add `blocks.content_hash BLOB NOT NULL CHECK(length(content_hash)=32)` to the derived `index.db` blocks table, plus indexes:

```sql
CREATE INDEX idx_blocks_content_hash
ON blocks(content_hash);

CREATE INDEX idx_blocks_session_message_hash
ON blocks(session_id, message_id, content_hash);
```

[evidence] `index.db` is derived/rebuildable, so this is an index-tier schema change rather than durable `user.db` migration. The swarm brief distinguishes durable source/user tiers from derived index/embedding tiers and says derived tiers rebuild/blue-green rather than migrate in place. fileciteturn1file10

[proposal] Define `block_content_hash_v1` over canonical block evidence, not identity:

```text
sha256(
  "block-v1\0",
  block_type,
  text or "",
  tool_name or "",
  canonical_json(tool_input) or "",
  semantic_type or "",
  media_type or "",
  language or "",
  tool_result_is_error or "",
  tool_result_exit_code or ""
)
```

Do **not** include `session_id`, `message_id`, `message.position`, `block.position`, or `tool_id`. The whole point is to survive fork-position shifts and re-ingest. Including `tool_id` would make the anchor less robust when providers regenerate tool identifiers; omit it from the hash but keep it in resolver metadata.

### 3. Anchor resolution algorithm

[proposal] Add a resolver, e.g. `resolve_evidence_anchor(anchor) -> CitationResolutionPayload`.

Resolution states:

```text
ok
drifted_position
drifted_message
relocated_lineage
ambiguous
missing
quarantined
hash_mismatch
stale_index
```

Algorithm:

1. Parse `<session_id_hint>::<message_id_hint>::block@sha256:<hash>`. Reject unsupported hash algorithms and malformed hex.

2. Exact scoped lookup:

```sql
SELECT b.*, m.position AS message_position, s.root_session_id
FROM blocks b
JOIN messages m ON m.message_id = b.message_id
JOIN sessions s ON s.session_id = b.session_id
WHERE b.session_id = ?
  AND b.message_id = ?
  AND b.content_hash = ?
```

If one row exists and the current `b.position` equals the stored `position_hint`, return `ok`.

3. If the row exists but the block position differs, return `drifted_position`, with `old_position_hint`, `current_position`, and the current live target ref. This is exactly the case A09 is protecting against: the content survived but position changed.

4. If scoped lookup fails, search the same session by hash. If exactly one row exists, return `drifted_message` if the message id changed, or `drifted_position` if only block position changed.

5. If same-session lookup fails, search the lineage neighborhood: topology root, ancestors, descendants, siblings. Prefer rows whose sessions are connected by `prefix-sharing` before `spawned-fresh`, because prefix-sharing means the evidence may be inherited content rather than merely related session content. The current lower schema has `session_links.inheritance` and `branch_point_message_id`; expose those in the resolver. If exactly one candidate remains, return `relocated_lineage`.

6. If global hash lookup finds multiple rows, return `ambiguous`, not a guessed success. Include candidates with session/message/block refs, titles, edge relation to original hint, and snippets. This is common for boilerplate prompts/tool outputs.

7. If no row exists, return `missing`. If the source session/raw artifact is known deleted/quarantined or the lineage path includes a quarantined edge, return `quarantined` rather than generic missing.

8. On any state except `ok`, preserve the old anchor and produce a new suggested anchor only if the live content hash still matches.

[evidence] This algorithm is aligned with the existing topology and user-state posture: current topology already surfaces `partial` readiness when truncation, unresolved edges, or cycles occur (`topology_http.py:80-100`), and recall packs already distinguish resolved/degraded items (`api/archive.py:5053-5060`). The missing piece is content-hash resolution.

### 4. Evidence basket → report flow

[proposal] Near-term storage can use existing `recall_pack` machinery, but with a new payload schema:

```json
{
  "schema_version": 2,
  "kind": "evidence_basket",
  "label": "Fable delegation rhetoric",
  "source_query_run_ref": "query_run:...",
  "items": [
    {
      "item_id": "basket_item:...",
      "anchor": "...::...::block@sha256:...",
      "selection_span": {"start": 120, "end": 355},
      "quote": "...",
      "note": "example of scope-policing",
      "tags": ["scope-control", "stern"],
      "added_from": {
        "surface": "webui-v2",
        "route": "/api/sessions?...",
        "query_ref": "query_run:..."
      },
      "last_resolution": {
        "state": "ok",
        "resolved_block_ref": "block:...",
        "resolved_at_ms": 1783210000000
      }
    }
  ]
}
```

[evidence] This fits current recall-pack capability because recall packs already normalize an item list, resolve items, and record resolved/degraded counts (`api/archive.py:5031-5066`). [proposal] But do not keep calling it “recall pack” in the UI. The product object is an **evidence basket**; recall pack is merely the initial storage adapter if adding a new `AssertionKind` is too expensive.

[proposal] The cockpit UI should have three panes:

Left: result list / query results.

Center: reader + evidence graph.

Right: evidence basket + live report draft.

Data flow:

```text
Query result row
  → open reader/session/topology
  → select block/message/span
  → Add to basket
  → resolver stores content-hash anchor + quote + provenance
  → report draft inserts Markdown footnote
  → verifier re-resolves anchors
  → export Markdown/HTML + citation manifest
```

[proposal] Report draft storage should be a second user-tier object, initially:

```text
target_ref = report:<report_id>
kind       = annotation or workspace_note initially; later report_draft
scope_ref  = evidence_basket:<basket_id>
value_json = {
  "markdown": "...",
  "basket_id": "...",
  "footnote_order": ["basket_item:1", "basket_item:2"],
  "export_policy": "fail_on_missing_or_quarantined"
}
```

Better full form later: add `AssertionKind.REPORT_DRAFT` and `AssertionKind.EVIDENCE_BASKET`, but that touches render/openapi/user-audit surfaces. The Claude memory excerpt even warns that new `AssertionKind` currently has several downstream schema/render implications, so do it deliberately rather than casually. fileciteturn1file4

### 5. Citation-integrity verifier

[proposal] Add `verify_citations(report_id|basket_id|anchors[]) -> CitationVerificationEnvelope`.

Envelope:

```json
{
  "ok": false,
  "verified_at_ms": 1783210000000,
  "archive_epoch": "...",
  "summary": {
    "ok": 9,
    "drifted": 2,
    "ambiguous": 1,
    "missing": 0,
    "quarantined": 1
  },
  "items": [
    {
      "anchor": "...",
      "state": "drifted_position",
      "severity": "warning",
      "old_ref": "...",
      "live_ref": "...",
      "message": "Content hash resolved in same message at block position 4, position hint was 3."
    }
  ]
}
```

Export policy:

`ok` and `drifted_position`: export allowed; footnote says “position drifted, content hash verified.”

`drifted_message` / `relocated_lineage`: export allowed only with visible warning unless operator explicitly promotes the new anchor.

`ambiguous`: export blocked by default; report can export only with an “unverified candidate” appendix.

`missing`: export blocked by default.

`quarantined`: export blocked by default unless report is explicitly about quarantined evidence.

`hash_mismatch`: hard fail; never silently rewrite.

[evidence] This matches A09’s instruction to use the same honesty doctrine that turned the recovery-digest fabrication into “unverified candidates.” fileciteturn1file0 It also aligns with the situation brief’s claim that the project’s strongest method is checking constructs against what they actually compute rather than accepting convenient regex/inference artifacts. fileciteturn0file11

## Layer 3 — full direction

[proposal] The full direction is not “a better web reader.” It is **publication-grade evidence operations over Polylogue’s read algebra**.

The underlying model should be:

```text
query_definition
  → query_run
  → result_relation
  → evidence_basket
  → annotation_batch/assertions
  → report_draft
  → verified_export
```

[evidence] This extends the C10 composer design, which already says committed runs should write recall entries with query text, resolved spec, result fingerprint, timestamp, and promotion to macros. fileciteturn1file6 [proposal] For the evidence cockpit, split that into explicit query-definition/query-run/result-relation objects, because report citations need to know which result set produced the basket.

[proposal] The “evidence graph” should not be just session lineage. It should combine four edge families:

1. **Lineage edges**: parent/fork/continuation/subagent, with inheritance `prefix-sharing` vs `spawned-fresh`, branch point, status, confidence, evidence.

2. **Evidence containment edges**: session → message → block → attachment/paste/tool call.

3. **User overlay edges**: assertion/annotation/mark/correction → target ref, and assertion → evidence refs.

4. **Analysis/report edges**: query_run → result_relation → evidence_basket → report_draft → export artifact.

That makes the graph useful for investigation rather than merely pretty. The user can click a report footnote, see the block, see the message/session, see the lineage edge that explains why the block moved, see assertions attached to it, and see which query originally surfaced it.

[proposal] The Webui-v2 cockpit should become the canonical UI for the “search/analyze/audit/remember” loop:

Search: query/composer/result list.

Analyze: graph + projections + aggregates.

Audit: citation verifier + assertion overlay + drift/quarantine state.

Remember: basket/report/annotation/cohort save.

[evidence] The current strategic language already frames Polylogue as “search / analyze / audit / remember,” not a chat viewer. fileciteturn1file3

## Visual design

[proposal] Replace the current BFS lineage list with a force-directed graph, but keep the BFS tree as the SSR fallback.

Graph behavior:

Nodes:

session nodes, with title/provider/model/date chips.

message/block nodes only when expanded.

assertion nodes as overlay badges or side nodes.

basket/report nodes in investigation mode.

quarantined nodes visibly red/striped.

cycle-break nodes diamond-shaped or warning-marked.

Edges:

`prefix-sharing`: solid, thick, cool color.

`spawned-fresh`: dashed.

`subagent`: arrowed child edge with “subagent” label.

`fork`: split/branch style.

`continuation`: simple forward edge.

`unresolved_native`: dotted, ghost node.

`quarantined`: red/striped edge, never hidden.

Interactions:

Click node: refocus reader/result list to that session/message/block.

Click edge: show branch point, inheritance, confidence, evidence JSON.

Hover branch point: highlight the inherited prefix up to `branch_point_message_id`.

Toggle overlays: assertions, marks, annotations, baskets, query-run provenance.

Lasso/select graph nodes: add all visible evidence blocks/messages to basket.

Keyboard: `g` graph focus, `b` add to basket, `r` report pane, `v` verify citations.

[proposal] Use `d3-force` rendered with Canvas/SVG inside a Preact component, not a huge graph framework at first. D3-force gives enough layout control, small enough dependency surface, and agent familiarity. If graph editing/large-topology performance becomes hard, reconsider Cytoscape.js later.

## Progressive enhancement

[evidence] The current daemon already has `_send_html` and serves the web shell HTML from Python (`daemon/http.py:1168-1175`, `1465-1468`). [proposal] Webui-v2 should formalize this instead of returning only the SPA shell.

Every reader/cockpit route should support three representations:

```text
Accept: text/html       → server-rendered semantic HTML
Accept: application/json → DTO JSON
Accept: text/markdown  → report/evidence-pack Markdown where meaningful
```

Routes:

`/s/<session>` returns server-rendered session reader with message/block anchors.

`/e/<anchor>` returns server-rendered evidence card.

`/g/<session>` returns server-rendered topology as nested tree/table, plus JSON script island for Preact graph hydration.

`/basket/<id>` returns server-rendered basket with verification chips and forms.

`/report/<id>` returns server-rendered Markdown preview with footnotes.

`/report/<id>.md` returns raw Markdown.

`/report/<id>/manifest.json` returns citation manifest.

A phone or `curl | pandoc` gets clean HTML. Preact upgrades the same HTML into the graph/basket/editor cockpit. No CDN. Built assets committed as `bby.11` already says.

## Minimal daemon API

[proposal] Keep the daemon API small and contract-shaped. B8’s core contract recommends `query`, `read`, `preview`, `complete`, `act`, `status`, plus facets as a separate method; the evidence cockpit should ride on that rather than invent a parallel substrate. fileciteturn0file3

Near-term HTTP API additions:

```text
GET  /api/evidence/resolve?anchor=...
POST /api/evidence/resolve-batch
POST /api/evidence/verify
```

```text
GET  /api/evidence-baskets
POST /api/evidence-baskets
GET  /api/evidence-baskets/:id
PATCH /api/evidence-baskets/:id
POST /api/evidence-baskets/:id/items
PATCH /api/evidence-baskets/:id/items/:item_id
DELETE /api/evidence-baskets/:id/items/:item_id
POST /api/evidence-baskets/:id/verify
```

```text
GET  /api/reports
POST /api/reports
GET  /api/reports/:id
PATCH /api/reports/:id
POST /api/reports/:id/render
POST /api/reports/:id/verify
POST /api/reports/:id/export
GET  /api/reports/:id/manifest
```

Extend existing topology:

```text
GET /api/sessions/:id/topology?include=inheritance,status,branch_point,evidence
```

Add overlay batch endpoint:

```text
POST /api/overlays/for-refs
```

Request:

```json
{"refs": ["...anchor...", "session:...", "message:..."], "include": ["assertions", "marks", "annotations"]}
```

Response: overlays grouped by normalized target ref and evidence refs.

For the UDS/thin-client future, these become service verbs rather than URL sprawl:

```text
evidence.resolve
evidence.verify
basket.get/save/add/remove/reorder
report.get/save/render/verify/export
topology.read
overlay.batch
```

[evidence] This matches the A2/A4/A3 direction: a warm daemon with one execution core, UDS fast path, and in-process break-glass rather than duplicate client substrate logic. fileciteturn0file7 fileciteturn0file6 fileciteturn0file4

## Implementation sequence

[proposal] I would land it in this order:

First PR: **block hash substrate.** Add block content hash to index DDL/writer/payloads, extend public-ref parser with `block@sha256`, add resolver and tests over re-ingest/position drift.

Second PR: **citation verifier.** Batch resolver, verification envelope, CLI smoke command, and report-manifest schema. No UI dependency.

Third PR: **basket as recall-pack v2.** Use existing recall-pack/user-state routes, but add evidence-basket payload schema and block-hash item resolver. Add web forms in SSR.

Fourth PR: **SSR evidence routes.** Add Jinja templates for session, evidence card, topology fallback, basket, report. Use existing `jinja2` dependency and HTML sanitizer stack (`pyproject.toml:32`; `rendering/renderers/html_template.py:8-34`).

Fifth PR: **Preact cockpit scaffold.** Typed API client, tokens, router, result list, reader parity, basket pane.

Sixth PR: **force graph.** Extend topology envelope to include inheritance/status/branch point, then add D3-force graph with fallback.

Seventh PR: **report editor/export.** Live Markdown report pane, footnotes, verifier gate, Markdown/HTML/manifest export.

Eighth PR: **assertion overlay.** Batch overlay endpoint, assertion badges on reader/graph/basket/report footnotes.

This sequence gives value early: block-hash verifier and baskets are useful even before the new graph is pretty.

## What I would change in the current design

[proposal] `bby.11` currently frames the stack as the foundation. I would sharpen the bead around **evidence integrity as the first acceptance gate**. The scaffold is not done when Preact renders list+reader parity; it is done when a selected block can survive re-ingest and export through a verifier.

Revised `bby.11` acceptance core:

1. A block content-hash anchor can be created from the reader.

2. Re-ingest or lineage recomposition that changes block position still resolves the anchor as drifted-but-verified.

3. A basket persists selected evidence blocks/messages with structured anchors.

4. A report draft renders those items as Markdown footnotes.

5. Export re-resolves every citation and blocks or flags missing/quarantined/ambiguous anchors.

6. Topology graph surfaces `prefix-sharing` vs `spawned-fresh`, quarantined edges, cycle state, and branch point.

7. The same session/basket/report routes work as server-rendered HTML with JS disabled.

The stack should serve this acceptance, not be the acceptance.

## Open questions for the operator

Should the first implementation store baskets/reports as `recall_pack` / `workspace_note` payloads to avoid new `AssertionKind`, or is it worth paying the schema/render/openapi cost now for `evidence_basket` and `report_draft`?

Should a quarantined citation hard-block export by default, or should it export with a red “quarantined evidence” appendix when the report is explicitly forensic?

Should the block hash include message role? I lean no for the hash itself and yes for resolver metadata. Including role reduces duplicates but makes the hash less purely block-content keyed.

Should report exports be saved back into `user.db` as report objects, written as files under a publication/export directory, or both?

Should the graph render message/block nodes by default, or only on expansion? I lean session graph by default with evidence-node expansion on click.

## What’s missing

I did not run live code or tests. I inspected the uploaded snapshot and extracted package only; live master may have moved.

I did not inspect an actual live archive to verify how often duplicate block-content hashes occur. That matters for ambiguity policy.

I did not inspect current `bd show polylogue-bby.11 --json` from a live repo; I used the uploaded bead export and A09 brief.

I did not prototype the graph or measure bundle size for `d3-force` versus Cytoscape.js.

I did not verify whether current OpenAPI generation can cleanly emit the new DTOs without additional schema-render work.

The most important unverified technical assumption: adding `blocks.content_hash` to derived `index.db` is straightforward. It should be, but the sync/async writer twin path must be checked before claiming it is a small change.

    lines = Path(file).read_text(errors='replace').splitlines()
    print('\n###', Path(file).name, 'lines', len(lines))
    for pat in pats:
        found=[]
        low=pat.lower()
        for i,l in enumerate(lines,1):
            if low in l.lower():
                found.append(i)
                if len(found)>=5: break
        print(pat, found[:5])

## [assistant 340]
## Analytical [A] — Product positioning and the legibility bar, bead `polylogue-3tl`

Snapshot assumption: this is grounded in the uploaded July 5 bundle and the attached swarm outputs. Live code/beads may have moved. In particular, the checked-out README in the bundle already contains much of the 3tl positioning work, while the post-swarm transcript says some legibility beads remain open or newly created. Verify locally with `bd show polylogue-3tl --json`, `bd show polylogue-3tl.4 --json`, current `README.md`, current `docs/proof-artifacts.md`, and the docs site build before acting.

## Recommendation

[proposal] Lead with **claim-vs-evidence**, not “agent memory,” not “chat archive,” and not “better grep.” The defended public category should be:

**Polylogue is the local system of record for AI work: it turns vendor chat logs and coding-agent traces into evidence you can search, analyze, audit, and use to resume work.**

[evidence] This category is already present in the current README snapshot: “Polylogue is the system of record for AI work,” covering ChatGPT, Claude, Codex, Gemini, Antigravity, Hermes, and coding-agent sessions, with the four verbs search/analyze/audit/remember (`README.md:9-12`). The orientation transcript independently says the legibility epic is explicitly not “chat viewer / observability tool / memory store,” but “the system of record for AI work,” fronted by search/analyze/audit/remember. fileciteturn1file5

[proposal] The first public artifact should be a **claim-vs-evidence finding page** plus a **private-data-free reproduction path**. It should show that Polylogue can detect when coding agents proceed after structured tool failures, because that is the cleanest wedge against both “just grep `~/.claude`” and generic memory products.

[evidence] The Situation Brief identifies this as the defensible wedge: Polylogue captures structured tool outcomes, error flags, and exit codes, allowing comparison between assistant claims and tool results; it argues that the moat is structured-outcome capture + multi-provider corpus + construct-validity discipline, not “chat search” alone (`situation-brief(2).md:57-61`). fileciteturn1file15 The proof page says Polylogue reads tool outcomes from provider structure rather than assistant prose and cites `is_error=1` / non-zero `exit_code` as the failure predicate (`docs/proof-artifacts.md:11-13`, `39-53`). The storage DDL backs this: `blocks` has `tool_result_is_error` and `tool_result_exit_code`, and the `actions` view exposes `is_error` and `exit_code` (`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/index.py:195-196`, `328-337`).

[proposal] The runner-up is **browser-captured agent recovery / context-pack uplift**, but I reject it as the first public wedge. It is strategically important, and probably the higher long-run product story, but the current evidence says the earlier uplift experiment was negative/ambiguous and the re-run is still `polylogue-cfk`, not done. Claim-vs-evidence already has a public-safe aggregate and reproduction method; agent recovery should be second-wave after `cfk` closes.

[evidence] The Situation Brief says the closest “useful” demo is agent recovery, but also says claim-vs-evidence travels on its own and either artifact would be sufficient if finished (`situation-brief(2).md:133-137`). The bead `polylogue-cfk` says the prior two-arm experiment recorded “packs lose” due to stale packs and needs an n≥3 re-run, then n=12–20 for a publishable uplift claim. The README also explicitly says memory-benefit claims must stay capability-phrased until measured uplift proves the effect (`README.md:98-100`). fileciteturn1file15

## Layer 1 — With today’s substrate

[evidence] The first-screen README is already close. It has the category sentence (`README.md:9-12`), a 7-minute skim ladder (`README.md:14-25`), five concrete questions ordinary transcript folders cannot answer (`README.md:27-39`), local-first posture (`README.md:41-45`), and a private-data-free demo entrypoint (`README.md:47-61`). The proof artifacts page already maps claims to artifacts and warns that unproven claims must be phrased as capabilities, not facts (`docs/proof-artifacts.md:1-15`). The release gate also says external release must be installable, demoable without private data, and truthful about shipped behavior (`docs/plans/release-readiness-gate.md:5-8`).

[evidence] The one-command demo is not aspirational in the snapshot. `docs/examples/demo-tour/report.md` says `polylogue demo tour` passed, produced first result in 7.956s and full tour in 13.442s, with 11 sessions and user overlays present (`docs/examples/demo-tour/report.md:1-18`). The pre-release install-path proof says the release command is `uvx polylogue demo tour`, with first result in 4.636s and full tour in 10.180s (`docs/examples/demo-tour/uvx-proof.md:1-23`). The demo corpus datasheet reports 11 sessions, 43 indexed messages, five origins, failed tool results, lineage links, subagent links, compaction events, run rows, observed events, context snapshots, and no declared residual construct gaps (`docs/plans/demo-corpus-construct-audit.md:14-89`).

[evidence] The current claim-vs-evidence proof is stronger than a normal demo. It reports a public-safe aggregate generated on 2026-07-04 against schema v24: 5,000 structured failures sampled from 42,033 structured failures, 1,205 silent-proceed next turns, 24.1% silent lower bound, and marker calibration precision/recall values (`docs/proof-artifacts.md:39-53`). It also gives both private local regeneration commands and private-data-free reproduction commands using a seeded archive (`docs/proof-artifacts.md:55-77`).

[proposal] Therefore, with no substrate change, the legibility deliverable can be:

1. README first screen stays category-first, but gets one **finding card** immediately after the five questions: “In a 5,000-row sample of structured tool failures, at least 24.1% were silent-proceed next turns; reproduce the method on the seeded corpus.” Make the private/archive number clearly public-safe aggregate, not demo-corpus result.

2. Add an explicit “Why not `grep ~/.claude`?” box. The answer should be: grep finds text; Polylogue resolves provider structure, tool outcomes, exit codes, costs, lineage, typed units, and evidence-backed derived claims. Ground it in `README.md:27-39`, `README.md:102-120`, `docs/proof-artifacts.md:39-77`, and `index.py:195-223`.

3. Use `uvx polylogue demo tour` as the stranger command once packaging is real; until release, use `uvx --from <repo> polylogue demo tour` because the uvx proof says that is the pre-release equivalent (`docs/examples/demo-tour/uvx-proof.md:3-8`, `20-23`).

4. Publish a static `docs/findings/claim-vs-evidence/index.md` even before the full 3tl.4 renderer, if necessary. It can be hand-generated from the current proof packet, as long as it contains the reproduction commands and a provenance stanza.

[evidence] There is a docs inconsistency to fix before leaning too hard into the current README: the swarm brief says “no bare-query support” and search should be via explicit verb/composer (`SWARM_BRIEF.md:60-62`), but current `docs/getting-started.md` still teaches `polylogue "css refactor"` and says bare tokens are full-text search terms (`docs/getting-started.md:31-35`), and `docs/search.md` says bare tokens are full-text terms (`docs/search.md:5-6`). The public story should not simultaneously say “explicit verb/composer” and teach bare query. fileciteturn2file7

[proposal] Today’s first-screen copy should be more like this:

> **Polylogue is the local system of record for AI work.** It reads the traces your AI tools already leave behind — ChatGPT, Claude, Codex, Gemini, browser chats, and coding-agent tool calls — and turns them into evidence you can search, analyze, audit, and use to resume work.  
>  
> It is not a prettier transcript folder. Grep can find the word “pytest”; Polylogue can show which tool call failed, whether the agent noticed, what it cost, which session it came from, and what raw evidence supports the claim.

That is sharper than “chat archive with FTS and semantic search,” and it directly answers the skeptical “why not grep?” reader.

## Layer 2 — With one near-term substrate change

[proposal] Implement **3tl.4 findings publishing lane** before adding new product demos. Do not build a new interactive surface for legibility first. The missing external object is not another UI; it is a stable, citable finding URL.

[evidence] Bead `polylogue-3tl` defines terminal acceptance as: a stranger can understand from the README first screen, run the one-command demo, and cite a published finding URL, verified by a cold-reader pass. Bead `polylogue-3tl.4` is already scoped as the findings-publishing lane: `docs/findings/<slug>/finding.yaml`, render to `docs/findings/<slug>/index.md`, stable `/findings/<slug>/` URL, provenance gate, changelog, no private rows, seeded-corpus regeneration, and `devtools render findings --check`. The post-swarm transcript says 3tl.4 was raised to P2 because it produces the published finding URL required by the legibility epic. fileciteturn1file8

[proposal] The near-term substrate should be a **Finding object**, not just a Markdown page. It can start as YAML because 3tl.4 already specifies YAML, but the model should anticipate database-backed query objects later. Minimum fields:

`finding_id`, `slug`, `title`, `claim`, `status`, `archive_cursor`, `sample_frame_query`, `measure_version`, `query_dsl_version`, `code_commit`, `run_date`, `source_query_refs`, `evidence_pack_refs`, `seeded_reproduction_command`, `private_archive_aggregate`, `public_demo_result`, `limitations`, `changelog`.

[proposal] The one near-term design improvement over 3tl.4 is this: the `sample_frame_predicate` should be stored as a **query object reference** when available, and as query text only as a fallback. That lines up with the queries-as-objects direction without blocking 3tl.4. In other words: ship YAML now, but design it as a serialized `Finding`, not a bespoke docs format.

[evidence] C10 already proposes that every committed composer run writes a recall entry to `user.db` with query text, resolved spec, result fingerprint, and timestamp, and that naming a recall entry promotes it to a macro (`C10_composer_ux.md`, §3.5–3.6). fileciteturn2file14 The swarm brief says the read surface is `Query × Projection × Render`, and projection/render are already part of the architectural direction (`SWARM_BRIEF.md:9-29`). fileciteturn2file10

[proposal] The near-term “stranger-can-run” artifact should be:

`uvx polylogue demo tour`  
then  
`uvx polylogue finding reproduce claim-vs-evidence`

The second command may initially be a docs/devtools command, but the public copy should look like a product affordance, not a private devtool. If the real command is still `devtools workspace claim-vs-evidence`, the README should say “developer reproduction” and the finding page should expose that honestly.

[evidence] The proof artifacts page currently reproduces the method with `devtools workspace claim-vs-evidence` after seeding/verifying a demo archive (`docs/proof-artifacts.md:65-77`), so the method exists, but the productized verb does not. That is exactly what 3tl.4 should convert into a stable published lane.

## Layer 3 — Full direction

[proposal] The full direction is **not** “better docs” and not “better demo scripts.” It is that Polylogue should make analyses themselves first-class objects:

`raw session evidence → query runs → result relations/cohorts → evidence packs → annotations/assertions → findings → published pages`

[proposal] In the full version, a public finding is not a static page generated at the end. It is the visible projection of an analysis run. The operator or agent asks a question; Polylogue stores the queries; the result sets become cohorts; an agent annotates rows; those annotations become assertions/judgments; a finding renderer produces a page with claims, caveats, reproduction commands, and evidence packs. The docs page is just one render target.

[evidence] This is consistent with the substrate already in the bundle. The read algebra covers query/projection/render and typed units including assertions, files, runs, observed events, and context snapshots (`SWARM_BRIEF.md:9-29`). The hot-daemon/composer direction makes query composition, preview, and commit histories explicit, with recall entries storing resolved specs and result fingerprints (`C10_composer_ux.md`, §3.5–3.6). fileciteturn2file10 fileciteturn2file14 The current proof discipline already says unsupported claims should be phrased as capabilities or caveats, not facts (`docs/proof-artifacts.md:1-15`).

[proposal] In that full direction, the product positioning becomes stronger:

**Polylogue is the local evidence layer for AI work: it records what agents did, lets you investigate it as structured evidence, and turns the investigation itself into citable, reproducible artifacts.**

That sentence is less cute than “flight recorder,” but it lands the unique category: not just storage, not just memory, not just search, but evidence and investigation.

[proposal] The “grep” comparison should become a table only after the claim-vs-evidence page exists. Until then, use prose. A table without a public finding risks sounding like marketing. Once the finding exists:

| Task | `grep ~/.claude` | Polylogue |
|---|---|---|
| Find a word | Yes | Yes |
| Normalize across Claude/Codex/Gemini/ChatGPT | No | Yes |
| Pair tool calls with tool results | No | Yes |
| Detect structured failure via exit code / `is_error` | No | Yes |
| Ask whether the agent acknowledged the failure | Manual | Query + report |
| Reproduce a public-safe method | No | Seeded demo + finding |

[evidence] The bundle supports every row except “reproduce a public-safe method” as a fully productized finding URL. The structured-failure data path is present (`index.py:195-223`, `328-337`); the private-safe proof packet and seeded method exist (`docs/proof-artifacts.md:39-77`); the missing citable URL is exactly `polylogue-3tl.4`.

## The legibility bar, stated operationally

[proposal] Bead `polylogue-3tl` should be considered closed only when all of these are true:

1. **First screen:** A cold reader can say, in one sentence, what Polylogue is and why grep is insufficient. This is not “knows the architecture.” It is “understands the category.”

2. **One command:** A cold reader can run one public command without private data and get a passing report, transcript, and recording/tape. The current demo-tour artifacts suggest this is close or already true, but the public install path must be verified against the current package.

3. **One finding URL:** A cold reader can cite a stable URL with a specific claim, methodology, caveats, reproduction command, and changelog. This is the missing external artifact.

4. **One caveat discipline:** Any measured claim says whether it comes from private archive aggregate, seeded demo reproduction, or capability-only substrate. No blended rhetoric.

5. **One anti-grep answer:** The README must explicitly say grep is useful for text search but cannot audit structured tool outcomes, costs, lineage, or derived claims.

[evidence] The Situation Brief states the bottleneck is “demonstrated use that an outsider can see,” and every strategic path waits on one externalized proof (`situation-brief(2).md:65-81`). It also warns that substrate/scaffold work can substitute indefinitely for the external artifact (`situation-brief(2).md:103-113`). fileciteturn1file15

## Beads / work items I would sharpen

[evidence] Existing relevant beads: `polylogue-3tl`, `polylogue-3tl.1`, `polylogue-3tl.2`, `polylogue-3tl.4`, `polylogue-3tl.11`, `polylogue-3tl.12`, `polylogue-cfk`, `polylogue-sru`, `polylogue-tf2`, `polylogue-jxe`, `polylogue-212`, `polylogue-4bu`. The post-restructure transcript says external legibility/demos are top-of-frame, with `cfk`, `3tl.11`, `3tl.4`, and `3tl.12` as the critical path. fileciteturn1file11 fileciteturn1file12

[proposal] I would add one child under `3tl` only if it does not already exist locally:

**`3tl.x — Anti-grep positioning proof card`**  
Description: The README/docs site must include a concise “why not grep/transcript folder?” proof card grounded in one claim-vs-evidence example.  
Acceptance: A cold reader can correctly distinguish lexical transcript search from Polylogue’s structured evidence model; the card links to one finding URL and one seeded reproduction command; doc-command verify passes.

[proposal] I would not create a broad “marketing site” bead. That would invite the exact substrate/scaffold substitution the Situation Brief warns against. `3tl.4` and `3tl.12` are enough if executed sharply.

## Open questions for the operator

1. Do you want the first public claim to include the private-archive number “24.1% silent lower bound” as a public-safe aggregate, or should the public page lead only with the seeded reproduction method and keep private-archive numbers behind a caveat?

2. Is the public package path ready enough to promise `uvx polylogue demo tour`, or should the README use `uvx --from git+https://... polylogue demo tour` until release?

3. Should the top-line category be “local system of record for AI work” or “local evidence system for AI work”? I prefer “system of record” for category creation, but “evidence system” explains the grep wedge faster.

4. Should “memory” appear in the first screen at all? I would mention it only as “remember,” with a caveat that memory-benefit claims are capability-phrased until `cfk` proves uplift.

5. Which artifact gets the first stable URL: claim-vs-evidence only, or claim-vs-evidence plus v24 agent-forensics? I recommend claim-vs-evidence first, v24 forensics immediately after.

issues={}
for l in open('polylogue-beads-export.jsonl'):

   if n>=25: break

## [assistant 360]
According to the 2026-07-05 bundle snapshot, I would treat 9l5 as **almost ready for a first serious “so what” engine**, but not by building a big dashboard first. My defended recommendation is:

**[proposal] Build `activity_spans_v1` as the next analytic substrate: a derived, queryable relation over time-bounded work spans, backed by existing actions, messages, phases, work-events, observed-events, runs, and subagent projections. Then register measures over it.**

The runner-up I reject is: **start with the full 9l5.7 measure registry/statistics layer first.** It is directionally right and already beaded as the keystone, but if implemented in full before any new analytic relation, it risks becoming another internal substrate artifact. The situation brief explicitly warns that internal scaffold can substitute for the external artifact, and says the missing gate is a finished, inspectable demonstration of real task uplift. `activity_spans_v1` gives immediate publishable numbers; the full measure registry can harden them next. fileciteturn1file6

Snapshot caveat: this is grounded in the uploaded bundle and extracted code snapshot. Live code and Beads may have moved; verify locally with `bd show polylogue-9l5 --json`, `bd show polylogue-9l5.6 --json`, and current `rg` before filing.

## Layer 1 — with today’s substrate

[evidence] Today’s Polylogue already has more than enough raw structure to produce primitive analytics. The read algebra already exposes units including `observed-event`, `context-snapshot`, `message`, `action`, `block`, `assertion`, `file`, and `run`, with pipelines split on `|` and stages such as group/count/terminal actions. That is in the swarm brief at `SWARM_BRIEF.md:9-18`. The same brief says projection is currently still named-view-heavy, not fully composable, at `SWARM_BRIEF.md:19-25`. fileciteturn1file8

[evidence] The action substrate is strong. The SQLite `actions` view pairs `tool_use` blocks with `tool_result` blocks and exposes `tool_name`, `semantic_type`, `tool_command`, `tool_path`, `output_text`, `is_error`, and `exit_code` at `polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/index.py:324-343`. Query rows preserve time ordering via `messages.occurred_at_ms` and expose `is_error`, `exit_code`, and `followup_class` at `archive.py:4960-5002`. The query metadata explicitly exposes action fields `exit_code`, `followup_class`, `is_error`, `output`, `path`, `tool`, and `duration_ms` at `polylogue/archive/query/metadata.py:474-505`.

[evidence] The run/delegation substrate exists but is not yet a first-class “delegation” unit. `session_runs` stores `role` as `main` or `subagent`, plus `parent_run_ref`, `agent_ref`, `provider_origin`, `harness`, status, cwd, branch, lineage refs, and evidence refs at `polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/index.py:913-938`. The run projection builds subagent runs from extracted subagent reports, assigns `role="subagent"`, links parent/child run refs, and emits `subagent_started` / `subagent_finished` observed events at `polylogue/insights/run_projection.py:307-368`. Subagent extraction currently recognizes `Task` tools or `subagent_type` / `agent_type`, prompt/task ids, child session ids, final report previews, PR/issue refs, tests, caveats, and raw refs at `polylogue/insights/transforms.py:1618-1655` and `2072-2138`.

[evidence] Temporal material already exists, but at the wrong granularity for edit/compile/test/idle decomposition. `session_work_events` stores weakly labelled message ranges with start/end/duration, file paths, tools used, evidence, inference, and search text at `polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/index.py:689-708`. `session_phases` stores deterministic time-gap intervals with message ranges, duration, tool counts, word count, and evidence at `index.py:731-748`. The phase extractor explicitly says phases are time-gap segmented intervals, not intent-classified, at `polylogue/archive/phase/extraction.py:27-34`. The work-event labels include planning, implementation, debugging, review, testing, research, configuration, documentation, refactoring, data_analysis, and session at `polylogue/archive/session/extraction.py:89-102`; their classification is heuristic, based on action counts and text signals, at `extraction.py:305-359`.

[evidence] There is also already an honest timing posture. Session profiles store total, engaged, tool-active, wall, thinking, output, and tool duration fields, plus workflow shape, terminal state, cost, token lanes, and timing provenance at `polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/index.py:799-868`. OTLP correlation can enrich work events with exact spans when present, otherwise falling back to message-gap estimates with evidence provenance, at `polylogue/insights/otlp_correlation.py:1-6`, `193-260`, and `274-318`.

[proposal] With no schema change, today’s substrate can already answer weak but useful questions:

`actions where exit_code > 0 | group by tool | count`

`actions where is_error:true | group by followup_class | count`

`observed-events where kind:test_failed | group by session.origin | count`

`runs where role:subagent | group by harness | count`

`actions where session.repo:polylogue | group by action | count`

Those are “so what” adjacent, but not yet the real engine. They tell you which tools fail and where subagents appear. They do **not** yet tell you “this session spent 42% in edit, 18% in test, 31% idle/wait, then delegated twice and only used one result.”

[evidence] Bead `polylogue-9l5` already frames analytics exactly as “the archive answers ‘so what’ questions” and describes Layer 0 as existing substrate: profiles, work events, phases, threads, cost rollups, structural pathologies, followup_class, run projection, topology/logical sessions, tool timing, workflow shapes. Its acceptance criteria require analytics to land as registered measures over the query algebra, not bespoke modes. In the bundled export, `polylogue-beads-export.jsonl:211` is the 9l5 epic. `polylogue-9l5.1` is outcome-conditioned analytics; `polylogue-9l5.6` is tool episodes; `polylogue-9l5.7` is measure registry; `polylogue-9l5.8` is temporal analytics; `polylogue-9l5.10` is process mining; `polylogue-9l5.12` is graph/information-theoretic measures (`polylogue-beads-export.jsonl:156-157`, `207-211`, `293-296`, `357-359`).

## Layer 2 — near-term substrate change

[proposal] Add one derived relation first:

`activity_spans`

This is the missing bridge. It is not a dashboard. It is not a model. It is a materialized, evidence-tiered relation over bounded work intervals.

A row should look roughly like:

```text
span_ref
session_id
run_ref
parent_span_ref
start_message_id
end_message_id
start_action_ref
end_action_ref
started_at_ms
ended_at_ms
duration_ms
turn_start
turn_end
kind
subkind
outcome
confidence
evidence_tier
timing_provenance
classification_provenance
tool_episode_refs_json
action_refs_json
observed_event_refs_json
file_refs_json
commit_refs_json
delegation_refs_json
evidence_refs_json
payload_json
```

[evidence] The needed source fields are already there: action rows carry tool, command/path, timestamp, is_error/exit_code/followup_class (`archive.py:4960-5002`); phases give gap-bounded intervals (`index.py:731-748`; `phase/extraction.py:23-34`); work-events give weak semantic labels and evidence (`index.py:689-708`; `session/extraction.py:505-543`); observed events give structured outcomes including `tool_finished`, `command_failed`, `test_failed`, and subagent start/finish (`run_projection.py:22-33`, `171-192`, `268-305`, `346-368`); session profiles already store active/tool/wall durations and workflow/terminal state (`index.py:799-868`).

[proposal] Span kinds should start coarse and construct-valid:

`read_search`, `edit`, `build_compile`, `test`, `debug`, `review_vcs`, `delegate`, `synthesize`, `idle_gap`, `tool_wait`, `llm_wait`, `unknown`.

The important design choice: **separate “span kind” from “evidence tier.”** A span classified as `test` from a `pytest` command with exit code is stronger than a span classified as `debug` from user text containing “debug.” This follows the 9l5.7.1 gap: existing Layer 0 payloads expose confidence floats but not an explicit evidence-tier distinction, while that bead proposes tagging structural/provider-reported/derived/heuristic confidence (`polylogue-beads-export.jsonl:263`, bead `polylogue-9l5.7.1`).

[proposal] Build `activity_spans_v1` as a materializer over existing tables, not as a new capture source. The algorithm:

First, normalize action rows into atomic events. Use `semantic_type`, `tool_name`, `tool_command`, `tool_path`, `is_error`, `exit_code`, and `occurred_at_ms`. Commands that look like `pytest`, `devtools test`, `devtools verify`, `ruff`, or `mypy` already have related recognition in transforms (`polylogue/insights/transforms.py:2227-2228`); extend that classifier into a versioned alphabet rather than burying it in ad hoc analytics.

Second, split the session timeline at large gaps using the phase threshold. Existing phases use a 5-minute gap threshold at `polylogue/archive/phase/extraction.py:23-24`, and the phase table stores the threshold per row at `index.py:731-748`. A gap larger than threshold should produce an `idle_gap` or `human_absence` span, not disappear into duration math.

Third, merge adjacent atomic events into spans when their kind is stable and no significant gap intervenes. This mirrors the current work-event merge behavior for adjacent same-label events at `polylogue/archive/session/extraction.py:474-502`, but span classification must be stricter and more structural.

Fourth, attach outcome. For edit/test loops, the outcome is often not the edit itself but the following test/build/verify action. The span materializer should attach “next structural outcome” and “next diagnostic outcome” so we can compute recovery and loop metrics.

Fifth, emit caveats. If timestamps are missing, use turn-axis only. If classification comes from text signals, mark `evidence_tier=heuristic`. If a tool has no result, mark outcome unknown. This matches the 9l5.6 tool-episode AC, which explicitly says a tool_use with no paired result must yield an unknown-outcome episode rather than being dropped (`polylogue-beads-export.jsonl:207`, bead `polylogue-9l5.6`).

[proposal] I would slightly revise the current 9l5 design: make `tool_episodes` (`polylogue-9l5.6`) the **atomic episode layer**, and add `activity_spans` as the **temporal composition layer** above it. `tool_episodes` answers “what happened at this call/result boundary?” `activity_spans` answers “how did work unfold over time?”

[proposal] New query units:

`tool-episode` — mostly already specified by bead `polylogue-9l5.6`.

`activity-span` — new. Queryable fields: `kind`, `subkind`, `outcome`, `duration_ms`, `evidence_tier`, `timing_provenance`, `tool`, `path`, `repo`, `run`, `agent`, `session.origin`, `session.repo`.

`delegation` — new or materialized view over run/subagent_report/observed_event. Queryable fields: `parent_run`, `child_run`, `subagent_type`, `model_family`, `instruction_text`, `result_status`, `return_latency_ms`, `used_by_parent`, `outcome`, `evidence_tier`.

[proposal] Minimum DSL surfaces:

```text
activity-spans where session.repo:polylogue
  | group by kind
  | sum duration_ms
```

```text
tool-episodes where outcome:failed
  | group by tool, followup_class
  | count
```

```text
activity-spans where kind:test AND outcome:failed
  | seq(test_failed -> edit -> test_passed)
```

```text
delegations where parent.origin:fable
  | group by child.model_family, result_status
  | count
```

```text
activity-spans where session.repo:polylogue
  | measure active_time_ratio by session.origin window week
```

[evidence] This is aligned with the existing read-algebra direction, because the current design explicitly wants one query grammar and composable projection/render rather than multiplying bespoke verbs (`SWARM_BRIEF.md:9-34`, `63-65`). It also aligns with B8’s diagnosis that `QueryProjectionSpec = Selection × Projection × Render` exists but is not yet the executor, and that read still runs through named views (`B8_contract.md:66-75`). fileciteturn1file8 fileciteturn0file2

## Layer 3 — full direction

[proposal] The full 9l5 direction should be a **measure algebra over typed relations**, not an “analytics page.”

The core objects:

`tool_episode` — one tool call/result pair, including unknown-result cases.

`activity_span` — bounded work span with kind, duration, outcome, evidence tier.

`delegation` — parent agent assigns child/subagent work, with instruction/result/use.

`query_run` — stored Polylogue query execution, so analytics can cite the analysis process itself.

`result_relation` / `cohort` — reusable result set by grain.

`annotation_batch` — agent/human external judgments imported as assertions.

`analysis_run` — provenance DAG tying query runs, cohorts, annotation batches, evidence packs, and reports.

[evidence] Existing object-ref kinds already include `work_event`, `phase`, `file`, `branch`, `commit`, `agent`, `repo`, `run`, `context-snapshot`, `observed-event`, `assertion`, `saved_view`, `recall_pack`, `tool-call`, and `subagent-report` at `polylogue/core/refs.py:8-38`. That means the ref vocabulary is already broad enough for this direction, but it lacks explicit `query_run`, `result_relation`, `activity_span`, `delegation`, and `analysis_run`.

[proposal] Agent-efficiency scoring should **not** be one magic score. It should be a vector of registered measures, with an optional composite view. The composite can exist, but it should never be the source of truth.

Core measures:

`active_time_ratio = active_span_duration / wall_duration`

`idle_gap_ratio = idle_gap_duration / wall_duration`

`edit_test_cycle_count`

`failure_recovery_latency = time from failed test/command to next structural success`

`silent_proceed_after_failure_rate = failed episode followed by non-acknowledging assistant action`

`verification_after_edit_rate = edit spans followed by test/build/verify before final answer`

`cost_per_clean_session`

`cost_per_structural_success`

`tool_failure_rate`

`delegation_fanout`

`delegation_return_latency`

`delegation_used_result_rate`

`delegation_rework_rate`

`subagent_parallelism_width`

`context_churn_ratio`

[evidence] These correspond to existing or beaded analytics. `polylogue-9l5.1` wants cost/duration/retries/tools by structural success; `polylogue-9l5.6` wants tool episodes; `polylogue-9l5.8` wants series/trends/baselines/changepoints; `polylogue-9l5.10` wants process mining over event sequences; `polylogue-9l5.12` wants fan-out/depth distributions and co-occurrence networks (`polylogue-beads-export.jsonl:156`, `207`, `210`, `293`, `295`). The situation brief also says the process story should carry a quantitative spine, but that raw commit volume can mislead because high-commit mechanical sweeps may be low-value compared with architectural collapse days (`situation-brief(2).md:97-107`). fileciteturn1file6

[proposal] Delegation analytics should be its own unit, not just `runs where role:subagent`. The current run projection can count subagent runs and start/finish events, but an analysis like “Fable rules subagents with an iron fist” needs the parent instruction, child identity/model family, output contract, child result, parent use of the result, retry/critique, and return latency. That is a `delegation` relation.

A minimal `delegation` materializer:

```text
delegation_ref
parent_session_id
parent_run_ref
child_run_ref
subagent_report_ref
instruction_block_ref
result_block_ref
subagent_type
child_model
child_model_family
instruction_preview
result_preview
status
started_at_ms
finished_at_ms
return_latency_ms
used_by_parent
parent_use_ref
evidence_tier
evidence_refs_json
payload_json
```

`used_by_parent` is tricky: v1 should be `unknown|mentioned|quoted|synthesized|ignored` with evidence-tier labels. It can be structural when the parent cites the child result by ref; derived/heuristic when inferred from text similarity or temporal adjacency. This should explicitly use assertions/annotation batches for richer qualitative labels instead of pretending the derived label is raw truth.

[proposal] The full scoring layer should be:

`raw evidence → tool episodes → activity spans → delegation edges → measures → series/comparisons → reports`.

A “score” only renders at the last stage. It should decompose into visible components:

```text
agent_efficiency_score
  = structural_success_quality
  + verification_discipline
  + low_idle_ratio
  + low_rework_ratio
  + good_delegation_yield
  - coverage_penalties
```

But the report should show all components, their evidence tiers, and sample frame. This is the construct-valid version of “which model/agent is better.”

## What is one materializer away?

[proposal] The best one-materializer target is:

**`activity_spans_v1` over the existing `actions`, `messages`, `session_phases`, `session_work_events`, `session_observed_events`, `session_runs`, and `session_profiles`.**

Why this one:

[evidence] Existing work events and phases already give time-bounded intervals, but phases are explicitly not intent labels (`polylogue/archive/phase/extraction.py:27-34`) and work-events are weak heuristic labels (`polylogue/archive/session/extraction.py:89-102`, `305-359`). Existing action rows have the stronger structural data: tool call/result pairing, exit code/error flag, path/command, timestamps, followup class (`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/index.py:324-343`; `archive.py:4960-5002`). Existing observed events already include structured command/test outcomes (`polylogue/insights/run_projection.py:22-33`). So the missing materializer is a normalizer/composer, not a new capture pipeline.

[proposal] Once `activity_spans_v1` exists, five immediately useful insights become simple grouped measures:

Edit/test/idle decomposition by model, repo, and harness.

Failure recovery latency after test/build failures.

Wasted-loop detection as a continuous measure, not just a pathology flag.

Delegation overhead: time before/after subagent dispatch and parent integration.

Cost per active minute / cost per structural success.

That is the shortest route from existing substrate to “so what.”

## New or changed beads I would file

[proposal] Add under `polylogue-9l5`:

**`polylogue-9l5.x — Activity spans materializer: edit/test/build/idle/delegate intervals over tool episodes and phases`**

Design: derived `activity_spans` table in `index.db`; builds from action rows, observed events, phases, work-events, run projections; emits span kind, duration, outcome, evidence tier, timing provenance, action/tool/delegation refs; versioned classifier alphabet; no LLM labels.

Acceptance: seeded corpus produces spans; every span has evidence refs; gaps over threshold become idle spans; structural test failures produce `kind=test outcome=failed`; broad query `activity-spans where session.repo:polylogue | group by kind | sum duration_ms` works; no span with heuristic-only classification renders without `evidence_tier=heuristic`.

**`polylogue-9l5.x — Delegation unit: parent instruction → child run/report → parent use`**

Design: derived `delegations` unit over subagent reports/run projections; includes instruction/result refs, subagent type/model family, status, return latency, parent-use classification, evidence tier.

Acceptance: `delegations where role:subagent` equivalent row count matches subagent run count within documented caveats; every row links parent and child evidence; parent-use can be unknown and is not guessed as used.

**`polylogue-9l5.x — Efficiency measure pack v1`**

Design: MeasureSpec registrations over `activity_spans` and `tool_episodes`: active_time_ratio, idle_gap_ratio, test_failure_recovery_latency, verification_after_edit_rate, tool_failure_rate, delegation_return_latency, delegation_used_result_rate.

Acceptance: each measure declares construct, formula, sample frame, evidence tier, confounds; output refuses unlabeled cross-origin comparison if coverage tier missing, matching 9l5.7 doctrine.

**`polylogue-fnm.x — Span/delegation terminal unit DSL`**

Design: add `activity-spans`, `tool-episodes`, `delegations` terminal sources, fields, group keys, and completions. Pipeline remains hand-split outside Lark, so new stages need care but not a full grammar rewrite; the compaction memory also warns that new terminals containing `:` must respect terminal priority relative to `FIELD_CLAUSE` (`Pasted text(35).txt`, query DSL memory). fileciteturn1file4

**`polylogue-bby.x / jnj.x — Analytics evidence-card projection`**

Design: projection preset for span/episode/delegation evidence cards. This is how a group-count cell drills down to actual evidence.

## Rejected runner-up

[proposal] Rejected runner-up: “Implement full 9l5.7 first: stats module, registry, DSL measure/compare, multiple-comparison controls, renderer footnotes, then build analytics.”

Reason: 9l5.7 is correct but over-frontloaded. The bead itself even has a “contract-first split” note saying slice 1 should be small: MeasureSpec dataclass + registry + Wilson interval + one registered measure, because downstream beads depend on the spec shape, not the complete primitive set (`polylogue-beads-export.jsonl:157`, bead `polylogue-9l5.7`). That is the path I’d take: implement the **thin MeasureSpec skeleton** alongside `activity_spans_v1`, not the full statistical edifice first.

[evidence] This also follows the situation brief’s product constraint: the next thing should become a finished artifact proving usefulness, not another internally satisfying scaffold (`situation-brief(2).md:133-137`, `157-161`). fileciteturn1file6

## Open questions for the operator

What should count as “success” for agent-efficiency v1: final structural terminal state, test/verify pass, merged commit, closed bead, or report accepted by parent? My recommendation: v1 uses structural tool/test success and terminal_state; PR/bead outcomes become optional stronger labels.

Should idle mean “no messages/tools for >5 minutes,” “human absence,” “tool wait,” or “agent thinking”? My recommendation: separate `idle_gap`, `tool_wait`, `llm_wait`, and `human_absence` when evidence supports it; do not collapse them into one idle score.

Should delegation “used_by_parent” be structural-only at first, or may it use heuristic text similarity? My recommendation: allow heuristic as candidate assertion, not as raw field. Structural mention/citation gets `evidence_tier=structural`; inferred use gets `derived|heuristic`.

Do you want an explicit composite “agent_efficiency_score,” or only a scorecard of measures? My recommendation: scorecard first; composite only as a named view that decomposes into components.

Should `activity_spans` live under 9l5 as analytics substrate, or under a more general “work-trace” epic that also serves context/replay/delegation? My recommendation: file it under 9l5 now, but design it as a reusable `work-trace` relation.

I did not verify the current Beads state after the later “391 issues” / “370 issues” transcript updates except through uploaded logs. The bundle export I inspected contains 398 issue records; the transcript mentions later applied states. Verify locally.

I did not inspect every raw-log line; I used the relevant retrieved chunks and the uploaded design reports.

I did not run modality-specific checks for Sinex/ActivityWatch/OTLP availability. Exact idle/tool/LLM timing depends heavily on whether OTLP spans or other capture modalities are present; otherwise v1 must use message-gap estimates with caveats.

I did not inspect the live daemon or current HTTP/UDS implementation. The swarm2 daemon/composer documents were treated as design context, not re-derived.
