## [assistant 340]
Assumption: I am treating the bundle as a dated 2026-07-05 snapshot. I did not verify live `master`, live `bd`, or a running daemon. Some attached chat excerpts say the bead set reached 391 issues on master, while the packaged `polylogue-beads-export.jsonl` I inspected contains a later/different snapshot; verify locally with `bd stats`, `bd show 212 --json`, and `git rev-parse HEAD` before filing or editing.

## Recommendation

[evidence] Bead `polylogue-212` already defines the right constraint: every demo must run on the deterministic seeded corpus, have a live-archive operator variant, resolve every displayed number to structural evidence, and decompose into product primitives rather than bespoke scripts. It explicitly scopes 212 around D1/D2/D4/D5/D8 plus post-hoc forensic Q&A, while leaving D3/D6/D7 to adjacent campaigns. `polylogue-212`.

[proposal] Make 212 a **prompt-file portfolio**, not a demo shelf. Each demo is an executable `PROMPT.md` given to a coding agent, and every prompt emits the same **Demo Finding Packet**. Start with five “today” prompts, including the anti-demo. Then add near-term prompts only when the missing primitive is implemented. The portfolio should optimize for repeatable citable artifacts, not slick one-off recordings.

Runner-up rejected: a single high-polish “agent recovery” flagship video. [evidence] The situation brief says the closest demonstration is browser-captured agent recovery, but also says the shelf’s current failure is not lack of capability; it is lack of one externalized proof that a stranger can inspect, reproduce, and cite. A video alone does not create the structural spine for 8–16 future demos, and risks repeating the deferral pattern where the scaffold absorbs the launch artifact. situation-brief(2).md:65–69, 135–137, 151–153. fileciteturn1file5

## Uniform artifact: Demo Finding Packet

[evidence] The bundle already has the key output constraints. The finding-publishing bead `polylogue-3tl.4` requires `docs/findings/<slug>/finding.yaml` with five provenance fields: archive cursor id/position, measure/query version, git commit SHA, sample-frame predicate, and run date; it also requires stable `/findings/<slug>/` URLs, refusal to render missing provenance, and changelogged living pages. `polylogue-3tl.4`.

[proposal] Every 212 prompt should emit this exact packet:

```text
.agent/demos/212/<demo_id>/
  PROMPT.md                 # executable instruction file for a coding agent
  finding.yaml              # five-part provenance stanza + structured claim
  report.md                 # human-readable citable report
  evidence.ndjson           # one row per cited evidence ref
  queries.ndjson            # query text + lowered/resolved spec if available
  annotations.ndjson        # optional agent judgments/assertions
  checks.json               # pass/fail, unsupported claims, coverage notes
  run.log                   # command transcript, no private rows in public mode
```

The report format should be identical across demos: claim, corpus, method, findings, specimens, counterexamples, limits, reproduce. The anti-demo emits the same packet with `verdict: not_supported`.

[evidence] This aligns with the current shared payload direction: surface payloads are frozen Pydantic models with JSON serialization, and `SearchEnvelope` is already the canonical ranked-result envelope shared across surfaces. polylogue/surfaces/payloads.py:107–113, 1186–1208. The read algebra already defines `QueryProjectionSpec = SelectionSpec × ProjectionSpec × RenderSpec`, but the code comments say the projection bridge is still a contract builder, not an executor. polylogue/surfaces/projection_spec.py:141–218. fileciteturn1file1

## Layer 1 — with today’s substrate

[evidence] Today’s substrate can already support serious read demos: the query layer has boolean predicates, structural units, sequence, pipeline stages, terminal actions, and render formats; the current limitation is that projection is still mostly named views rather than fully composable projection algebra. SWARM_BRIEF.md:9–34. The action view already joins tool-use blocks to tool-result blocks and exposes `tool_name`, command/path/input, `is_error`, and `exit_code`; session tables also carry git branch/repo/commit fields, and repo/commit correlation tables exist. polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/index.py:39–82, 324–343, 470–519. fileciteturn1file3

1. `demos/212/d01_receipts_claim_vs_evidence/PROMPT.md`

[evidence] This is bead `polylogue-212.2`: “D1 ‘The receipts’: claim-vs-evidence on a real PR.” It resolves PR → authoring session through `session_commits/session_repos`, renders PR-body claims beside observed action rows, and drills to raw tool-result blocks. `polylogue-212.2`.

[proposal] Prompt claim: “For one merged agent-authored PR, show whether the PR’s claimed verification matches the tool outcomes.” The prompt should select one seeded PR fixture, resolve it to the session, extract claim sentences, extract verification/tool rows, and emit a packet with a two-column table plus drill refs. This should be the first public demo because it directly expresses the wedge: structured tool outcomes versus assistant claims. situation-brief(2).md:57–61.

2. `demos/212/d02_behavioral_archaeology/PROMPT.md`

[evidence] This is bead `polylogue-212.4`: six DSL queries, including SEQ thrash-loop, failure-rate by model, tool breakage by observed-event outcome, semantic probe across providers, abandoned-this-repo-this-quarter, and a query piped into `read`; it must show `explain_query_expression` once. `polylogue-212.4`.

[proposal] Prompt claim: “Polylogue can answer engineering-lead questions that normal chat UIs cannot because it has a queryable archive.” Keep it rapid-fire and citable: six sections, one query each, one output table each, one `explain` block showing the query’s parsed meaning.

3. `demos/212/d03_posthoc_forensic_qa/PROMPT.md`

[evidence] This is bead `polylogue-212.1`: post-hoc forensic Q&A over a completed multi-hour coding-agent session, answering when a bad assumption entered, which file churned before a regression, what evidence was cited for a design choice, and which prior failures resemble the present one; it must include one explicit “we cannot answer X” slide. `polylogue-212.1`.

[proposal] Prompt claim: “A completed session becomes interrogable after the fact.” The output should be a Q&A report where every answer cites session/message/action/commit refs; one question must intentionally fail if evidence is absent.

4. `demos/212/d04_method_trace_swarm_to_beads/PROMPT.md`

[evidence] The situation brief says the process story is the safest, least contested inbound story, because the rare asset is the disciplined agentic-engineering method, not merely “uses coding agents.” situation-brief(2).md:90–99. The attached session shows a large swarm auditing and restructuring the bead set; the later excerpt reports the external-legibility/demo cluster and states that 212 is the demonstrable-evidence layer. Pasted text(34).txt:1991–2006. fileciteturn1file12

[proposal] Prompt claim: “Polylogue plus Beads makes agentic engineering auditable as a process.” The prompt should use the bundle corpus to reconstruct one swarm-to-beads episode: initial directive, subagent launches, findings, applied bead mutations, verification, and final state. This should not be a self-congratulatory velocity demo; it should show mistakes, gates, held changes, and verification.

5. `demos/212/d05_honesty_anti_demo_no_evidence_no_number/PROMPT.md`

[evidence] The situation brief explicitly praises a negative result: “do not force the multi-source demo yet, the upstream data quality is not there,” and says the trap is that every deferral reason is locally correct but the demo remains one step away. situation-brief(2).md:65–69. The 3tl.4 publishing lane is supposed to refuse findings without the provenance stanza. `polylogue-3tl.4`.

[proposal] Prompt claim: “Polylogue refuses to publish unsupported numbers.” The prompt should attempt a tempting finding, such as “multi-source reconstruction proves what the operator was doing minute-by-minute,” and then emit a `verdict: not_supported` packet with missing modalities, missing refs, and the exact query/evidence gap. This is the required honesty/anti-demo. It should be shipped beside the successful demos, not hidden.

## Layer 2 — with a near-term substrate change

[evidence] The near-term substrate change needed here is not the full daemon/composer stack; it is a small set of object types and import surfaces: query/result objects, annotation batches over assertions, and a common packet runner. Assertions are already close: `user.db` has a unified `assertions` table with `scope_ref`, `target_ref`, `kind`, `value_json`, `body_text`, `author_ref`, `author_kind`, `evidence_refs_json`, status, visibility, confidence, staleness, context policy, supersedes, and timestamps. polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/user.py:7–31. The enum already includes `annotation`, `saved_query`, `recall_pack`, `judgment`, `run_state`, `prompt_eval`, `transform_candidate`, and `pathology`; assertion statuses include candidate/accepted/rejected/deferred/superseded. polylogue/core/enums.py:399–447. Upsert already accepts target/scope/kind/value/body/author/evidence/status/visibility/confidence/context policy. polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/user_write.py:901–999.

6. `demos/212/d06_cost_by_outcome/PROMPT.md`

[evidence] This is bead `polylogue-212.3`: “D2 ‘Where did the money actually go’: cost by outcome.” It wants provider-reported exact versus catalog-priced cost basis, then cost by outcome: monthly spend, percent in abandoned/failing sessions, and five most expensive failures, drillable to exact turns. It explicitly needs the outcome-conditioned join. `polylogue-212.3`.

[proposal] Prompt claim: “The important cost report is not total spend; it is spend by outcome.” Near-term substrate requirement: finish the action-outcome join and cost-honesty lane, then the prompt runs as a normal packet.

7. `demos/212/d07_resume_triage_to_next_action/PROMPT.md`

[evidence] This is bead `polylogue-212.6`: “D8 ‘Pick up where I left off’: abandoned-session triage to live continuation.” It chains `find_abandoned_sessions → get_resume_brief → resume routing`, and explicitly says this proves the archive changes what you do next. `polylogue-212.6`.

[proposal] Prompt claim: “The archive changes the next action, not just the postmortem.” Near-term substrate requirement: make the resume ranking honest, exclude known-dead scorer paths until fixed, and in public mode end at a printed continuation command if live harness routing is not available.

8. `demos/212/d08_self_watching_live_capture/PROMPT.md`

[evidence] This is bead `polylogue-212.5`: “D5 ‘The session that watched itself’: live capture proof.” It queries the archive for the current session mid-session, uses ingest-cursor timestamps for capture latency, and ends by generating the session’s own postmortem. `polylogue-212.5`.

[proposal] Prompt claim: “A session can become queryable while it is still being created.” Near-term substrate requirement: a seeded/public variant needs synthetic live-capture fixtures or a deterministic daemon run. The live operator variant can use the actual daemon.

9. `demos/212/d09_external_annotation_loop/PROMPT.md`

[evidence] Assertions are already queryable as structural fields: assertion field metadata includes author, author kind/ref, body, context, evidence, key, kind, scope/scope_ref, status, target/target_ref, value, visibility, and timestamps. polylogue/archive/query/metadata.py:507–525. The API exposes candidate assertion listing and judgment methods. polylogue/api/archive.py:2079–2206.

[proposal] Prompt claim: “An external agent can annotate sessions/messages, import the judgments, and then query the annotations as evidence-adjacent data.” The prompt should export a small evidence pack, ask the coding agent to classify rows using a fixed JSONL schema, import them as candidate assertions, and produce aggregates plus counterexamples. This is the scalable version of annotation recipes.

10. `demos/212/d10_delegation_rhetoric/PROMPT.md`

[evidence] The bundle’s current query unit vocabulary includes `message`, `action`, `block`, `assertion`, `file`, `run`, `observed-event`, and `context-snapshot`; it does not list a first-class `delegation` unit in the shared read-algebra baseline. SWARM_BRIEF.md:11–18.

[proposal] Prompt claim: “Visible orchestrator-to-subagent delegation can be extracted, classified, and cited.” Near-term substrate requirement: either a temporary annotation recipe over messages/actions, or preferably a first-class `delegation` unit later. The prompt should find candidate delegation instructions, annotate directive intensity/output-contract strictness/control devices, import judgments, and render specimens. This generalizes the Fable-hook idea without making Fable a product silo.

11. `demos/212/d11_composer_relation_preview/PROMPT.md`

[evidence] The composer design says terminal stages preview bounded projections; set algebra previews should show left count, operand count, intersection count, and grain errors before commit; every commit writes a recall entry with query text, resolved spec, result fingerprint, and timestamp. C10_composer_ux.md:142–205. fileciteturn1file13

[proposal] Prompt claim: “Polylogue’s DSL is inspectable while it is being composed.” Near-term substrate requirement: `preview` and `complete` endpoints. The public packet can be generated from a scripted composer trace: keystrokes, preview envelopes, final query run, and rendered result. This is more product-demo than analysis-demo, so it should come after D1/D4/anti-demo.

## Layer 3 — full direction

[evidence] The full direction depends on the hot-daemon/thin-client stack. The swarm brief frames the target as a resident memory-hungry daemon, thin UDS client, no substrate work in CLI/TUI, and live `complete(partial)` / `preview(spec)` in single-digit milliseconds. SWARM_BRIEF.md:47–59. B8 proposes a seven-method service surface: `query`, `read`, `preview`, `complete`, `act`, `status`, and `facets`; `read` should execute `ReadRequest = selection + projection + render`, and `preview`/`complete` are the composer’s reason to require the daemon. B8_contract.md:134–168, 188–219. fileciteturn1file11

12. `demos/212/d12_work_reconstruction_repo_trace/PROMPT.md`

[evidence] The current archive has session git fields, action/tool outcome fields, and session↔repo↔commit correlation tables. polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/index.py:39–82, 324–343, 470–519.

[proposal] Prompt claim: “Polylogue can reconstruct the work trace of a coding-agent session across messages, tool calls, files, and commits.” Full substrate requirement: artifact graph and work-trace projection. Do not call it deterministic replay yet. The packet should say “reconstruction” or “reproduction plan,” and it should mark any missing file snapshots/env/state as non-replayable.

13. `demos/212/d13_context_compile_after_compaction/PROMPT.md`

[evidence] The attached Claude Code excerpt shows `/compact` followed by a flat `bd prime --memories-only` injection of 19 persistent memories, including automagic invariants, Beads workflow, demo-regeneration profiling, and live-archive pitfalls. Pasted text(35).txt:28–65. fileciteturn1file4

[proposal] Prompt claim: “A compiled Polylogue context pack can be more relevant and auditable than a flat memory dump.” Full substrate requirement: compaction-boundary units, context-compile runs, selected/omitted memory refs, and outcome tracking. The anti-overclaim guard: the demo should compare what was included/omitted and why; it should not claim improved agent performance unless run as a paired experiment.

14. `demos/212/d14_query_objects_analysis_dag/PROMPT.md`

[evidence] C10 already proposes recall entries with query text, resolved spec, result fingerprint, timestamp, macros, and `@` completion. C10_composer_ux.md:190–205. B8’s service contract would make `query/read/preview/complete/act/status/facets` a single substrate boundary. B8_contract.md:134–168.

[proposal] Prompt claim: “The analysis itself is queryable.” Full substrate requirement: promote recall entries into `query_definition`, `query_run`, `result_relation`, `annotation_batch`, and `analysis_run` objects. The prompt should run a multi-step analysis, store each query/result/annotation import as objects, then generate a report that cites those objects.

## Defended implementation order

[proposal] Implement the portfolio in this order:

First ship **D1 Receipts**, **D4 Behavioral Archaeology**, and **D5 Anti-demo** as a three-packet public mini-portfolio. D1 is the wedge; D4 proves breadth of query; D5 proves honesty. This directly matches the situation brief’s warning that the next artifact matters more than more substrate. situation-brief(2).md:77–81, 135–137.

Second add **D3 Post-hoc Forensic Q&A** and **D4 Method Trace** because they use today’s data and strengthen the “system of record for AI work” story without needing daemon/composer work.

Third, only after the packet runner and assertion import are in place, add **Cost by Outcome**, **Resume Triage**, **Annotation Loop**, and **Delegation Rhetoric**.

Fourth, leave **Work Reconstruction**, **Context Compile**, and **Query Objects Analysis DAG** as full-direction demos. They are valuable, but making them first would recreate the exact deferral pattern the brief warns about. situation-brief(2).md:103–113.

## What this implies for bead 212

[proposal] Update `polylogue-212` from “portfolio of named demos” to “portfolio contract plus children.” The epic should own:

A packet schema child: `212.packet`.

A prompt runner child: `212.runner`.

A public corpus verification child: `212.seed-1843-corpus`.

The existing 212.1–212.6 children.

A new anti-demo child: `212.anti`.

A new annotation-loop child after assertion batch import exists.

A “demo registry manifest” child that lists every prompt file, expected packet path, public/private mode, and required primitives.

[evidence] This stays inside the bead’s existing compositionality rule: shell/python is glue; product primitives own the logic. `polylogue-212`.

## Open questions for the operator

1. Should the first public portfolio be three packets, five packets, or one packet? My recommendation is three: D1 + D4 + anti-demo.

2. Should anti-demo be framed as “no unsupported number is published” or as “multi-source reconstruction is not ready”? The former is more general and less self-defeating; the latter is more concrete.

3. Should `finding.yaml` live only under `docs/findings/<slug>/`, or should `.agent/demos/212/<demo>/finding.yaml` be the source and docs be a rendered projection?

4. Do you want the live-archive variants in the same packet format but private, or should public seeded packets and private operator packets be separate artifact classes?

5. For delegation rhetoric, should the first version be annotation-only over messages/actions, or should it wait for a true `delegation` unit?

import json, textwrap
issues=[]
for l in open('polylogue-beads-export.jsonl'):
    d=json.loads(l)
    if d.get('_type')=='issue': issues.append(d)
terms=['subagent','delegation','artifact','scratch','report','agent','coordination','context','run','assertion','query object','recall','cohort','analysis','work-evidence','compaction','repo','commit']
for term in terms:
    hits=[]
    for b in issues:
        txt='\n'.join(str(b.get(k,'')) for k in ['id','title','description','design','acceptance_criteria','notes','labels'])
        if term.lower() in txt.lower(): hits.append(b)
    print('\nTERM',term,'hits',len(hits))
    for b in hits[:18]:
        print(b.get('id'), 'P'+str(b.get('priority')), b.get('status'), b.get('issue_type'), b.get('title'))

## [assistant 379]
According to the 2026-07-05 bundle snapshot, the right answer is: **Polylogue should add a first-class `delegation` derived unit now, not wait for the full work-replay graph.** The current substrate already sees enough Claude-Code/Codex subagent structure to extract high-value delegation edges, and the existing query/projection/assertion machinery is close enough that this can be made generic rather than a Fable silo. The runner-up is “represent delegation only as assertions over messages/actions.” I reject that because it keeps the central relation invisible to the DSL, projections, set algebra, previews, and analytics; assertions should annotate delegations, not be the delegation graph itself.

I am grounding this in the bundle snapshot; live code and live Beads may have moved after July 5, 2026, so all code/file claims below should be verified locally with `rg`, `bd show`, and current migrations before implementation.

## Recommendation

[evidence] The bundle’s read frame is already relation-shaped: `Query × Projection × Render`, with structural query units including `message`, `action`, `block`, `assertion`, `file`, `run`, `observed-event`, and `context-snapshot`; the pipeline is split on `|`; terminal actions include `read`, `analyze`, `select`, `mark`, `delete`, and `continue`. The same brief says projection is still closed-view-driven and should move toward composable projection/macros. fileciteturn2file3 Code agrees: `QueryUnitName` is declared in `polylogue/archive/query/metadata.py:8-17`, and `QueryProjectionSpec = SelectionSpec × ProjectionSpec × RenderSpec` is in `polylogue/surfaces/projection_spec.py:141-146`.

[proposal] Add `delegation` as the next derived query unit, with a materialized relation in `index.db` or a derived read model backed by existing blocks/runs/topology/artifacts. Then add a `delegation-card` projection preset over that unit, and let external agents annotate delegation rows through the existing assertion/judgment substrate. This is the narrowest substrate change that makes the Fable demo, Codex/Claude comparison, multi-agent work audits, and future work-replay all easier.

[evidence] This is not inventing a new direction. The Beads/system frame already names `s7ae` as the agent coordination substrate: evidence-backed multi-agent work over sessions, topology, repos/worktrees, work items, activity/resource episodes, context injection, messages, handoffs, proof evidence, and no Beads lock-in. The bundle also says `37t.11` is the context scheduler, `37t.12` is the judgment queue, `fnm.13` is set algebra, `t46` is contracts-own-surfaces, and `4p1` is the one read algebra. Bead IDs: `polylogue-s7ae`, `polylogue-s7ae.4`, `polylogue-s7ae.5`, `polylogue-37t.11`, `polylogue-37t.12`, `polylogue-fnm.13`, `polylogue-t46`, `polylogue-4p1`.

[proposal] The defended path is therefore: **derived `delegation` unit first; generic artifact/evidence edges second; annotation batches third; full analysis/work-trace graph later.** This gives a publishable, useful demo without blocking on the entire “replay work from git/tool calls” vision.

## Runner-up rejected

[proposal] Runner-up: keep delegation as an external `annotations.jsonl` / assertions-only workflow, where an agent scans sessions, labels messages/actions, imports judgments, and reports over assertion rows.

[evidence] The assertion substrate is strong enough to support that: `user.db.assertions` already has `target_ref`, `scope_ref`, `key`, `kind`, `value_json`, `body_text`, `author_ref`, `author_kind`, `evidence_refs_json`, `status`, `visibility`, `confidence`, `staleness_json`, and `context_policy_json` (`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/user.py:7-31`). Assertion kinds include `annotation`, `saved_query`, `recall_pack`, `decision`, `lesson`, `handoff`, `judgment`, `run_state`, `prompt_eval`, `transform_candidate`, and `pathology` (`polylogue/core/enums.py:399-428`). The API already exposes listing and judging assertion candidates (`polylogue/api/archive.py:2079-2128`, `2181-2206`), and B8 explicitly names `save_annotation`, `record_correction`, `judge_assertion_candidate`, saved views, workspaces, recall packs, and blackboard as real facade methods not yet unified under the cross-surface contract. fileciteturn2file9

[proposal] I reject assertions-only because it makes the most important noun—delegation—implicit. You would constantly query “actions where tool:Task plus assertions where key:directive_style plus maybe runs where role:subagent,” then reconstruct the graph in scripts. That defeats the point of the DSL/composer direction. Assertions should say “this delegation is stern / failed / under-specified / used by parent,” not define what a delegation is.

## Layer 1 — with today’s substrate

[evidence] Today, Polylogue can already see much of the delegation structure, especially for Claude Code and Codex. Claude Code’s parser treats `agent-*` session files as child sessions, but special-cases `agent-acompact-*` as continuation/compaction rather than real subagent work (`polylogue/sources/parsers/claude/code_parser.py:432-451`). Codex parsing records that `source.subagent.thread_spawn` is positive evidence for subagent lineage, while `forked_from_id` alone proves a parent but not the relationship type; only `source.subagent.thread_spawn` assigns `BranchType.SUBAGENT` (`polylogue/sources/parsers/codex.py:592-599`, `821-837`).

[evidence] The insight layer already extracts “subagent reports.” `SubagentReport` has `subagent_type`, `tool_id`, `task_id`, `child_session_id`, link status/type, prompt preview, final report preview, PR refs, issue refs, test evidence, caveats, and raw refs (`polylogue/insights/transforms.py:214-228`). Extraction pairs `tool_use` with `tool_result` by `tool_id`, recognizes subagent tools, captures prompt/result previews, and records raw refs (`polylogue/insights/transforms.py:1618-1655`). It also enriches reports with child-session links where topology/session links can resolve them (`polylogue/insights/transforms.py:1658-1690`). The detector recognizes a Claude-style `Task` tool or tool inputs carrying `subagent_type` / `agent_type` (`polylogue/insights/transforms.py:2072-2116`).

[evidence] The lower pipeline also already marks subagent spawns: `extract_tool_invocations` sets `is_subagent = tool_name == "Task"` (`polylogue/pipeline/semantic_capture.py:125-138`), and `extract_subagent_spawns` emits agent type, prompt, description, and `run_in_background` from `Task` invocations (`polylogue/pipeline/semantic_capture.py:193-208`).

[evidence] Structured tool evidence is already strong enough for serious analytics: `blocks` store `tool_name`, `tool_id`, `tool_input`, `tool_result_is_error`, `tool_result_exit_code`, generated `tool_command`, generated `tool_path`, and `search_text` (`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/index.py:182-208`). The `actions` view pairs tool use and tool result blocks and exposes `tool_command`, `tool_path`, output text, `is_error`, and `exit_code` (`index.py:324-343`). The code comments explicitly frame tool-result error/exit fields as the anchor for structured outcome reports rather than prose guesses (`index.py:217-224`; `polylogue/insights/transforms.py:1709-1717`).

[evidence] Runtime/run structure also exists. `session_runs` includes `parent_run_ref`, `agent_ref`, `context_snapshot_ref`, provider origin, harness, `role` constrained to `main|subagent`, status, confidence, cwd, git branch, lineage refs, evidence refs, transcript ref, payload, and search text (`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/index.py:913-938`). `session_observed_events` and `session_context_snapshots` add event and context-boundary units tied to runs (`index.py:952-1024`).

[evidence] Repo/commit correlation is partially present. Sessions carry `git_branch`, `git_repository_url`, and `commit_hash` (`index.py:51-55`); `repos`, `session_repos`, and `session_commits` model repo roots, branch names, commit SHAs, detection types (`time_window`, `file_overlap`, `explicit_ref`, `origin_reported`), method, confidence, and evidence JSON (`index.py:477-520`). This supports the earlier raw-log idea of correlating logs with commits/issues/PRs. fileciteturn1file17

[evidence] Artifact observation exists but is too source-tier/local today. `raw_artifacts` records `artifact_id`, `raw_id`, origin, `source_path`, `source_index`, `artifact_kind`, support status, classification reason, parse eligibility, malformed/decode state, `cohort_id`, `link_group_key`, `sidecar_agent_type`, and first/last observed times (`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/source.py:84-102`). This is enough to see sidecar/report-like artifacts, but not enough to query “artifact produced by delegation D and consumed by parent session P.”

[evidence] Current query units do not include `delegation`. The registry has `action`, `block`, `file`, `message`, `assertion`, `run`, `observed-event`, and `context-snapshot`; examples already cover `exists file(...)`, `runs where ...`, and `observed-events where ...`, but there is no delegation source (`polylogue/archive/query/metadata.py:692-728`). The query field metadata does include action fields such as `command`, `exit_code`, `followup_class`, `is_error`, `output`, `path`, `tool`, and `type` (`metadata.py:475-505`), and assertion fields such as `author_kind`, `evidence`, `key`, `kind`, `scope_ref`, `target_ref`, `status`, and `value` (`metadata.py:507-525`).

[proposal] With today’s substrate, a workable demo can be built as an external script/agent prompt:

`query candidate parent sessions → inspect actions/tool_use Task blocks → resolve child session/report refs via existing SubagentReport/session topology → export evidence windows → annotate rows externally → import annotations as assertions → write report`.

[proposal] The demo should avoid claiming “the delegation graph” as a built-in Polylogue feature. The honest present-tense claim is: **Polylogue can mine a candidate delegation inventory from existing subagent/report/runtime evidence, then use assertions to layer external judgments over it.**

[proposal] Example today-ish analysis flow:

```text
1. Find candidate sessions:
   sessions with action:subagent OR action tool:Task OR runs role:subagent.

2. For each candidate:
   read the Task/tool_use block, paired tool_result, SubagentReport, child session link,
   parent follow-up window, artifact paths mentioned in prompt/result.

3. Produce delegations.jsonl externally:
   one row per candidate delegation edge, with evidence_refs to session/message/block/run/artifact refs.

4. Ask an agent to annotate:
   directive_intensity, output_contract_strictness, scope_control, tone, control_devices, result_status.

5. Import as assertions:
   kind=judgment or annotation, key=directive_style_v1.*, target_ref=<block/session ref>,
   scope_ref=analysis:<id>, evidence_refs_json=[...].
```

[evidence] This “external annotation loop” fits the existing assertion model and the `37t` memory loop: `37t` explicitly describes agents declaring claims, the operator judging them, active claims compiling into preambles, and reboot/handoff through evidence packs; `37t.12` exists to make judgment queue bulk review/accept/reject of candidate assertions an owned feature. Bead IDs: `polylogue-37t`, `polylogue-37t.12`.

[proposal] Today’s ceiling: this will be useful but fiddly. The agent/script has to rebuild a graph from actions, reports, sessions, and assertions each time. Projection is manual. The DSL cannot say `delegations where ...`. The result is good enough for one demo, not good enough as a substrate.

## Layer 2 — near-term substrate change

[proposal] Add a derived `delegations` table/read model and make `delegation` a query unit. This should be a derived/index-tier model, not durable source evidence. Raw messages/tool blocks/session files stay source truth; delegation rows are materialized, recomputable claims with extractor version and confidence.

[proposal] Minimal `delegations` row:

```text
delegation_id                 stable deterministic id
parent_session_id             session containing the delegation act
parent_message_id             message containing delegation tool_use or instruction
parent_run_ref                run ref if known
tool_use_block_id             instruction/call block
tool_result_block_id          result block if paired
child_session_id              resolved child session if any
child_run_ref                 resolved child run if any
task_id                       taskId/task_id if present
tool_id                       tool id if present
delegation_kind               subagent | background-agent | sidecar-report | async-task | unknown
harness                       claude-code | codex | gemini-cli | hermes | unknown
subagent_type                 researcher | implementer | general-purpose | ...
subagent_model                if visible
subagent_model_family         if normalized
description                   short description field if present
instruction_preview           bounded preview, not canonical evidence
result_preview                bounded preview, not canonical evidence
status                        spawned | completed | failed | stopped | unresolved | unknown
link_status                   resolved | unresolved | inferred | quarantined
confidence                    raw | inferred plus numeric if useful
evidence_refs_json            block/session/run/artifact refs
artifact_refs_json            generic artifact refs
created_at_ms / updated_at_ms
materializer_version
payload_json                  provider-specific residue
search_text
```

[proposal] Stable identity should prefer `(parent_session_id, tool_use_block_id)` for tool-based delegations. If there is no tool block, use a deterministic hash over parent session + message + child session + instruction ref. Do not use natural-language prompt text alone; identical prompts can be different delegations.

[evidence] This schema mirrors existing patterns. `session_runs` already carries parent/agent/context/evidence fields (`index.py:913-938`). `session_observed_events` already carries subject/object/evidence/payload/search fields (`index.py:952-968`). `SubagentReport` already carries tool/task/child/prompt/report/test/caveat/raw refs (`transforms.py:214-228`). Therefore the new table is a normalization of existing concepts, not a foreign ontology.

[proposal] Extraction rules:

For Claude Code, high-confidence delegation comes from a `Task` tool use or tool input containing `subagent_type` / `agent_type`; pair it with the `tool_result` block via `tool_id`, use `_subagent_child_session_id` extraction when present, and link to `agent-*` child sessions unless the child is `agent-acompact-*`, which must be typed as compaction/continuation, not delegation. Evidence: Claude parser special-cases `agent-acompact-*` as `BranchType.CONTINUATION` and real `agent-*` as `BranchType.SUBAGENT` (`code_parser.py:432-451`); transform extraction recognizes Task/subagent input and child session IDs (`transforms.py:2072-2116`).

For Codex, high-confidence delegation requires `source.subagent.thread_spawn`; `forked_from_id` alone should create a parent/topology relation but not `delegation_kind=subagent`. Evidence: Codex parser says exactly that `source.subagent.thread_spawn` is positive subagent evidence, while `forked_from_id` alone proves parentage but not relationship type (`codex.py:821-837`).

For provider-neutral/local-agent structure, use `session_runs.role = subagent`, `parent_run_ref`, `native_parent_session_id`, and `agent_ref` as candidate evidence. Evidence: `session_runs.role` is constrained to `main|subagent`, and the row carries parent/agent/evidence fields (`index.py:913-938`).

For artifact linking, do not special-case `.agent/scratch`. Use generic `artifact_ref` edges with edge types: `produced`, `consumed`, `mentioned`, `reported_by`, `derived_from`, `evidence_for`. Raw source already has `source_path`, `artifact_kind`, `link_group_key`, and `sidecar_agent_type` (`source.py:84-102`); the missing piece is a derived graph edge from delegation/session/action/run/query/analysis to artifact.

[proposal] Add two derived relations:

```text
delegation_artifact_edges(
  delegation_id,
  artifact_ref,
  edge_type,        -- produced|consumed|mentioned|reported_by|derived_from|evidence_for
  evidence_refs_json,
  confidence,
  extractor_version
)

artifact_observations_public(
  artifact_ref,
  source_path,
  artifact_kind,
  content_hash/blob_ref if available,
  repo_ref,
  commit_ref,
  first_observed_at_ms,
  last_observed_at_ms
)
```

[proposal] Then add the DSL/source:

```text
delegations where parent.repo:polylogue and harness:claude-code
delegations where subagent_type:researcher and status:failed
delegations where instruction.text:"do not edit" | group by subagent_model_family | count
delegations where artifact.kind:markdown and artifact.path:swarm2 | read delegation-card
delegations where parent.model:Fable | except (delegations where child.family:claude)
```

[evidence] This fits the existing query model because unit query execution already centralizes terminal unit-source requests (`QueryUnitRequest`) and resolves unit descriptors into payload models (`polylogue/archive/query/unit_results.py:57-79`, `158-184`). It also fits C10’s composer/set-preview design: set operations are intended to show operand sizes and grain mismatch before commit, and recall/macros are intended to make composed sets reusable. fileciteturn2file0

[proposal] Add `DelegationQueryRowPayload` and register `delegation` in `QueryUnitName`, structural field metadata, terminal source list, and unit-row execution. First fields:

```text
parent, parent_session, parent_run, child, child_session, child_run
harness, parent_model, child_model, child_family
subagent_type, task_id, tool_id, description
instruction, result, status, link_status, confidence
artifact, artifact_kind, artifact_path
repo, branch, commit, time
annotation_key, annotation_value   -- joins assertions later, optional
```

[proposal] The `delegation-card` projection should render:

```text
header: delegation id, harness, parent→child, status, confidence
instruction: full or bounded instruction/tool_use prompt
parent context window: N messages before/after delegation
child output: child report/result/session summary
parent use: messages/actions after result where parent consumed/synthesized it
artifacts: linked report/files/commits
annotations: assertions/judgments over the delegation
provenance: exact evidence refs, extractor version, caveats
```

[evidence] Current projection families include `sessions`, `messages`, `blocks`, `actions`, `raw`, `context`, `chronicle`, `neighbors`, `correlation`, `temporal`, and `assertions`, with body policies `full`, `omit-tool-outputs`, `authored-dialogue`, and `metadata-only` (`projection_spec.py:18-40`). Named views are mapped to family bundles, and the file explicitly says this is a contract builder, not executor (`projection_spec.py:149-218`). This is why `delegation-card` should start as a server-side preset but be designed as a projection program, not a permanent special view.

[proposal] For external annotations, add `target_kind=delegation` to user-state target registries and allow assertions to target `delegation:<id>`. The current user-state target registry supports session, message, work_event, thread, block, attachment, and paste_span, but not delegation, query, artifact, or analysis (`polylogue/core/user_state_targets.py:29-118`). Even though raw `target_ref` is a free text field in `assertions`, surface affordances, recall packs, workspaces, and validation need a registered kind.

[proposal] Near-term implementation sequence:

1. `delegation` derived model/materializer over existing subagent reports, Task/action blocks, session_runs, and session topology.
2. `delegation` query unit + `DelegationQueryRowPayload`.
3. Generic artifact edge model; use raw artifacts as source, not `.agent/scratch` as a special case.
4. `target_kind=delegation` and annotation-batch import into assertions.
5. `delegation-card` projection preset and evidence-pack renderer.
6. Minimal demo prompt that runs the loop and produces `cohort.json`, `annotations.jsonl`, and `report.md`.

## Layer 3 — full direction

[proposal] The full direction is a **work graph**, not only a delegation graph:

```text
session
  -> message
  -> block/action
  -> run
  -> delegation
  -> artifact
  -> repo file / commit / PR / bead / issue
  -> query_run / result_relation / cohort
  -> annotation_batch / assertion
  -> analysis_run / report
```

[evidence] The bundle already argues for this broader framing: Polylogue is characterized as a “system of record for AI work,” with durable source/user tiers, derived index/embedding tiers, disposable ops tier, and program epics around coordination, content variants, lineage truth, attachment/blob integrity, scale-hardening, and external legibility. fileciteturn2file1 The situation brief says the strategic gate is an externalized proof that an agent/operator does a real task better with the substrate, not more internal machinery. fileciteturn2file16

[proposal] In the full design, `delegation` is one edge family inside `work_trace`. Work trace supports reconstructing, and sometimes reproducing, what happened: tool calls, command exits, file paths, repo/commit links, generated artifacts, handoffs, query runs, and reports. Do not promise deterministic replay by default; promise **reconstruction** and **reproducibility bundles**. Replay is a privileged, unsafe, partial operation.

[evidence] The raw-log already contains the seed of this: correlate Polylogue logs with git commits/issues/PRs, use temporal analysis to distinguish editing vs builds/tests, and make work more observable. fileciteturn1file17 Current code stores sessions↔repos↔commits with confidence/evidence (`index.py:477-520`), action rows with commands/paths/exit status (`index.py:324-343`), and run/event/context units (`index.py:913-1024`).

[proposal] Query objects become essential in the full direction. A Fable/delegation analysis should be able to say:

```text
analysis:a_fable_rhetoric
  step 1: query_run:q1 -> result_relation:r1 -> cohort:@candidate_delegations
  step 2: evidence_pack:e1 -> annotation_batch:b1
  step 3: query_run:q2 over assertions -> cohort:@strict_delegations
  step 4: report:artifact:rpt1
```

[evidence] C10 already proposes recall entries in `user.db` with query text, resolved spec, result fingerprint, timestamp, and macros via `@name`; it also says recalled queries should store resolved specs rather than just text. fileciteturn2file0 B8 proposes a single `PolylogueService` contract with `query`, `read`, `preview`, `complete`, `act`, `status`, and possibly `facets`, replacing scattered facade/CLI/HTTP paths. fileciteturn1file15

[proposal] In the full design, `cohort` means a named relation over a grain. A dynamic cohort is a saved query/spec; a snapshot cohort is frozen member ids at an archive epoch. Delegation analytics wants both: `@fable_candidate_delegations` should be dynamic while exploring; `@fable_report_v1_specimens` should be a snapshot for publication.

[proposal] External annotation recipes should compile to actual database objects, not only YAML. A recipe/prompt is portable intent. The durable record is `analysis_run`, with child `query_run`, `result_relation`, `cohort`, `evidence_pack`, `annotation_batch`, `assertion`, and `report` refs. This makes complex agent loops general without forcing every analysis into a rigid YAML workflow language.

[proposal] Full analytics examples:

```text
delegations where harness:claude-code
| group by subagent_type, status
| count

delegations where parent.model:Fable
| project delegation-card
| annotate schema:directive_style_v1

assertions where scope:analysis:fable and key:directive_intensity and value >= 4
| lift delegations
| group by child_model_family
| count

delegations where status:failed
| join parent.actions after result
| project failure-recovery-card

cohort:@strict_fable_delegations
| except (delegations where parent_use:none)
| render specimen-gallery
```

## Fable demo generalized

[evidence] The Fable idea is only the public hook. The bundle’s own strategic frame says the valuable demonstration is externally inspectable proof, and the project’s category is “system of record for AI work,” not a chat viewer. fileciteturn2file16

[proposal] Generalize the demo as **orchestrator delegation analysis**:

```text
Question:
How does an orchestrator instruct, constrain, route, and consume subagent work?

Units:
delegations, child runs/sessions, artifacts, parent-use windows, annotations.

Metrics:
fanout, model-family routing, task type, directive intensity, output-contract strictness,
scope-control devices, completion/failure status, parent-use/ignore rate, retry/escalation.

Specimens:
delegation-card projections with exact evidence refs.

External agent role:
annotate delegation rows under schema directive_style_v1, import assertions,
then re-query aggregates and outliers.
```

[proposal] This makes Fable one cohort, not one product feature:

```text
@fable_delegations
@claude_code_delegations
@codex_subagent_delegations
@strict_output_contracts
@failed_but_used
@non_claude_children
```

[proposal] A demo prompt should ask for three artifacts:

```text
cohort.json          candidate delegations + evidence refs
annotations.jsonl   directive_style_v1 judgments targeting delegation:<id>
report.md           citable report with specimen cards, counts, caveats, reproduce command
```

[proposal] The citable claim should be modest: “In this local archive slice, Fable-visible orchestration uses these delegation/control patterns.” It should not claim hidden Fable internals or generalize beyond visible local evidence.

## Concrete bead recommendations

[evidence] Existing owner beads: `polylogue-s7ae` for coordination substrate, `polylogue-s7ae.4` for archive session-tree/topology/proof/context-flow composition into coordination envelope, `polylogue-s7ae.5` for live two-agent proof, `polylogue-37t.12` for judgment queue, `polylogue-fnm.10` for fields/select, `polylogue-fnm.13` for set algebra, `polylogue-4p1` for read algebra, `polylogue-t46` for contract-owned surfaces, `polylogue-9l5` for construct-valid analytics, `polylogue-83u` for artifact/blob integrity, and `polylogue-4ts` for lineage truth.

[proposal] Add one new P1/P2 child under `s7ae`, not a new top-level epic:

**`s7ae.delegation-unit` — First-class delegation graph unit**

Design: materialize provider-neutral `delegation` rows from Claude Code Task blocks, Codex `source.subagent.thread_spawn`, `session_runs.role=subagent`, SubagentReport extraction, and session topology. Include parent/child refs, instruction/result block refs, link confidence, status, artifact refs, and evidence refs. Do not special-case `.agent/scratch`; artifacts are generic produced/consumed/mentioned/derived_from edges.

Acceptance: `delegations where ...` works as a terminal query unit; fixture tests cover Claude Task, Claude acompact exclusion, Codex subagent spawn, unresolved child, and no false subagent from plain `forked_from_id`; rows carry evidence refs; result is queryable via CLI/API/MCP; devtools verify green.

[proposal] Add a second child, probably under `83u` or `s7ae` depending on ownership:

**`artifact-edge-derived` — Generic artifact links from sessions/actions/runs/delegations**

Acceptance: derived artifact edges link raw artifacts to sessions/actions/runs/delegations with edge type and evidence refs; no path name is special; `.agent/scratch`, report markdown, JSON findings, exported evidence packs, generated PR summaries, and raw sidecars all use the same relation.

[proposal] Add a child under `37t.12` or a sibling:

**`annotation-batch-import` — Agent-written JSONL judgments into assertions**

Acceptance: schema-registered JSONL imports candidate assertions targeting session/message/block/run/delegation/query-result refs; rows require evidence refs; batch metadata records model/prompt/analysis; CLI/MCP can list/accept/reject/import; accepted assertions are queryable via `assertions where ...`.

[proposal] Add a child under `4p1` / projection surface:

**`delegation-card-projection`**

Acceptance: read/projection renders a bounded delegation card with instruction, parent context, child result, parent-use window, artifacts, annotations, and provenance; output works in markdown and JSON; no custom Fable view.

[proposal] Add a child under `fnm`:

**`delegation-query-unit`**

Acceptance: `delegations where ...` supports rows/count/group/select, joins assertion labels by target, respects grain rules, and participates in set algebra.

## Open questions for the operator

[proposal] Should every delegation attempt get a row, even if no child session is resolved? My recommendation: yes, with `link_status=unresolved`; otherwise failed/unlinked delegation behavior disappears.

[proposal] Should `agent-acompact-*` become a separate `compaction` unit rather than excluded entirely? My recommendation: yes later; for delegation extraction, exclude it now to avoid false Fable/Claude subagent counts.

[proposal] Should artifact edges live in `index.db` only, or should some artifact annotations live in `user.db`? My recommendation: raw/derived artifact observations and edges in source/index; human/agent judgments about artifact meaning in assertions/user.db.

[proposal] Should annotation imports default to `candidate` or `active`? My recommendation: agent-written qualitative labels default to `candidate`; deterministic extractor facts can be `active` if schema-owned and tested.

[proposal] How sensitive are delegation prompts? Should `delegation-card` show full prompts by default? My recommendation: JSON evidence pack can include full text under explicit opt-in; public markdown defaults to bounded prompt excerpts plus evidence refs.

[proposal] Should “Fable” be a normalized model/provider token or an analysis-level cohort label? My recommendation: normalize model/provider if present in source; otherwise keep “Fable-visible” as a cohort assertion with evidence, not a source fact.

[evidence] I did not run the daemon, migrations, query unit tests, or materializers. All implementation estimates assume the July 5 snapshot code paths still exist and have not moved.

[evidence] I did not inspect raw Claude/Codex fixture payloads beyond parser/materializer code. The extraction design should be validated against real source files before bead acceptance is finalized.

[evidence] I did not verify the live Beads state after the snapshot. The bundle contains post-swarm bead changes, but the repository may have moved; verify with `bd show polylogue-s7ae polylogue-37t.12 polylogue-fnm.13 polylogue-4p1 polylogue-t46`.

[evidence] I did not run multimodal artifact analysis. If delegation artifacts include screenshots, PDFs, or image reports, this design only covers their refs/metadata, not content extraction.

## [assistant 396]

## Recommendation

[proposal] Build **reproduction-first verification**, not “exact session replay,” as the next substrate slice.

The defended recommendation is: **make Polylogue produce a replayable work-trace bundle whose default operation is to verify the final claimed work from a clean repo state, not blindly re-run every historical tool call.** The object should answer: “Given this session, which repo state did it start from, what files/actions/commands/results did it touch, which commits/artifacts did it produce, and can we independently re-run the relevant verification commands or apply the resulting patch?”

The runner-up I reject is: **raw command-stream replay**, i.e. “take every Bash/tool call from the session and re-execute it in order.” It is tempting because the archive already has tool commands and exit codes, but it is too brittle and unsafe as the main product claim: the bundle currently does not guarantee action-level cwd/env/sandbox/network state, pre/post file hashes, secrets policy, package-cache state, or per-tool side effects. Raw replay should exist later as a best-effort mode for carefully classified commands, not as the headline.

The better framing is a replay ladder:

`L0 visual playback → L1 evidence reconstruction → L2 final-state verification → L3 patch/commit reproduction → L4 classified command replay → L5 deterministic full replay`

Polylogue is already credible at L1 today, can reach L2/L3 with a small substrate addition, and should only claim L4/L5 for sessions captured under stricter instrumentation.

## Layer 1 — With today’s substrate

[evidence] Polylogue already stores the raw source evidence in `source.db`: `raw_sessions` records origin, native id, source path, blob hash/size, acquisition and parse/validation state (`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/source.py:15-33`), and `blob_refs` records durable blob references (`source.py:51-59`). Raw artifacts are also modeled with `artifact_kind`, `support_status`, source path/index, parse eligibility, cohort/link keys, sidecar agent type, and first/last observed timestamps (`source.py:84-102`). This means a reproduction report can point back to original captured session payloads and artifact observations, not only derived rows.

[evidence] The parsed index already has session-level git hints: `sessions` includes `git_branch`, `git_repository_url`, and `commit_hash` (`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/index.py:51-55`). It also has `session_working_dirs`, `repos`, `session_repos`, and `session_commits` tables; `session_commits` stores `commit_sha`, `repo_id`, `detection_type`, `method`, `confidence`, and `evidence_json` (`index.py:470-512`). Codex parsing promotes provider git metadata into typed `git_branch`, `git_repository_url`, and `git_commit_hash` fields (`polylogue/sources/parsers/codex.py:847-888`), and the writer persists working dirs, repo edges, and explicit commit refs as `session_commits` with `detection_type='explicit_ref'`, `method='parser-git-meta'`, and confidence `1.0` (`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/write.py:3045-3053`, `3212-3276`).

[evidence] The action substrate is strong enough for **claim-vs-evidence verification**. Blocks store `tool_name`, `tool_id`, `tool_input`, `semantic_type`, `tool_result_is_error`, `tool_result_exit_code`, generated `tool_command`, generated `tool_path`, and generated `search_text` (`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/index.py:182-208`). The public `actions` view pairs `tool_use` blocks with matching `tool_result` blocks and exposes `tool_command`, `tool_path`, `tool_input`, `output_text`, `is_error`, and `exit_code` (`index.py:324-343`). There is also an index specifically for structured tool-result failures (`idx_blocks_tool_result_outcome`, `index.py:217-224`). The proof-artifacts page explicitly says the failure predicate is normalized structure, `is_error=1` or non-zero `exit_code`, and assistant prose is only follow-up acknowledgment (`docs/proof-artifacts.md:11-14`). fileciteturn1file18

[evidence] The query surface already treats replay-relevant things as units. The swarm brief says the query grammar supports structural `exists <unit>(...)` over `observed-event`, `context-snapshot`, `message`, `action`, `block`, `assertion`, `file`, and `run`, with terminal actions such as `read`, `analyze`, `select`, `mark`, `delete`, and `continue` (`SWARM_BRIEF.md:9-18`). Query metadata gives common fields such as `command`, `exit_code`, `is_error`, `output`, `path`, `tool`, and `duration_ms` (`polylogue/archive/query/metadata.py:474-505`), and terminal query descriptors exist for `assertions`, `files`, `runs`, `observed-events`, and `context-snapshots` (`metadata.py:792-867`). fileciteturn1file8

[evidence] There is already a materialized run/event/context layer: `session_runs` stores run refs, parent run refs, agent refs, context snapshot refs, harness, role `main|subagent`, status, cwd, git branch, lineage/evidence refs, transcript ref, payload JSON, and search text (`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/index.py:913-938`). `session_observed_events` stores event kind, subject/object refs, evidence refs, payload, and search text (`index.py:952-968`). `session_context_snapshots` stores context snapshot refs, boundary, inheritance mode, segment refs, evidence refs, metadata, payload, and search text (`index.py:1000-1015`).

[evidence] There is already a work-event read model: `session_work_events` stores type, summary, confidence, start/end indexes, times/duration, `file_paths_json`, `tools_used_json`, evidence, inference, and search text (`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/index.py:689-709`). This is not a replay log, but it is a useful mid-level reconstruction layer.

[evidence] The codebase already has an embryonic session↔commit detector. `polylogue/insights/session_commit.py` states that it detects likely commits through time windows, file-overlap scoring, and explicit references (`session_commit.py:1-10`). It extracts referenced files from tool calls/text (`session_commit.py:148-186`), derives scan windows (`session_commit.py:218-238`), runs `git log --since/--until --name-only` (`session_commit.py:290-305`), scores commits by explicit refs/file overlap/time-window fallback (`session_commit.py:319-363`), and builds a correlation result with commits, issue refs, PR refs, and file paths (`session_commit.py:387-449`). But the persistence hook is still a placeholder (`persist_session_commits`, `session_commit.py:455-468`), so this is not yet a complete product path.

[evidence] Bead `polylogue-7xv` already names the exact missing capability: “Native git/repo awareness: session-to-commit/branch/repo correlation in Polylogue.” Its design says to start from evidence already in the archive, infer session→repo from cwd/git tool calls, session→commit from SHAs in tool results plus Claude-session trailers in commit messages, materialize as a derived read model with evidence refs, and add DSL predicates/projections. Bead `polylogue-bby.12` already names “Session replay: play a session back the way it happened,” but it is explicitly a **derived visual view** over occurred timestamps, cost, change rails, and commit markers; it is not command re-execution. Bead `polylogue-6mv` draws the boundary: Polylogue owns raw AI-session evidence; Sinex owns redacted machine-timeline events and causal windows; Polylogue should emit derived privacy-preserving agent-trace events rather than pushing raw transcripts into Sinex. Bead `polylogue-x4s` and `polylogue-4c0` cover devloop/assertion and session↔bead work-history joins.

[proposal] So with today’s substrate, the honest demo is not “replay the session.” It is:

`reconstruct session work trace → correlate likely commits/files → compare claimed success against structured tool outcomes → generate a reproduction checklist`

A today-level output could be:

```text
session:<id>
  actions: ordered tool calls, outputs, error flags, exit codes
  files: paths referenced by tool calls / file units
  repo: inferred from cwd/repo metadata
  commits: explicit or candidate commits with confidence
  final claims: assistant/user summary messages
  verdict: verified / contradicted / unverified
  reproduction instructions: checkout commit X, inspect diff Y, run commands Z
```

[proposal] The correct today-level command surface is something like:

```text
polylogue read session:<id> --projection work-trace
polylogue query 'actions where session:<id> | group by tool | count'
polylogue query 'actions where session:<id> AND (is_error:true OR exit_code > 0)'
polylogue query 'files where session:<id>'
polylogue query 'runs where session:<id>'
```

The exact syntax may differ, but the units/fields exist in the snapshot.

[evidence] Current limitation: exact re-execution is not supported as a substrate. The action view exposes command/path/input/output/error/exit, but the schema does not guarantee normalized action-level cwd, environment, shell, timeout, stdin, sandbox/network policy, tool version, before/after file hashes, or pre/post git status (`index.py:324-343`; `session_runs.cwd` exists only at run level in `index.py:931`). This is enough for forensic reconstruction and many final verification checks; it is not enough for safe deterministic command replay.

## Layer 2 — Near-term substrate change

[proposal] The near-term change should be a **Work Trace + Reproduction Attempt** substrate, not a full replay VM.

Create a derived relation:

```text
session_work_trace_events
```

It should normalize existing evidence into an ordered trace:

```text
trace_event_ref
session_id
run_ref nullable
message_id
block_id / tool_use_block_id / tool_result_block_id
position
occurred_at_ms / started_at_ms / ended_at_ms
kind: message | tool_call | tool_result | file_ref | repo_snapshot | commit_ref | assertion | artifact
tool_name
semantic_type
command_text
argv_json nullable
input_json
output_blob_ref / output_text_excerpt
is_error
exit_code
cwd
repo_id
git_head_before
git_head_after
touched_paths_json
evidence_refs_json
replayability_class
redaction_json
payload_json
```

[evidence] This is not a new silo. It composes the existing `actions` view (`index.py:324-343`), `session_runs` (`index.py:913-938`), `session_work_events` (`index.py:689-709`), `session_repos/session_commits` (`index.py:491-512`), `raw_artifacts` (`source.py:84-102`), and `assertions` (`user.py:7-31`).

[proposal] Add one durable or semi-durable object:

```text
reproduction_attempt
```

This records an actual attempt to reproduce or verify work:

```text
attempt_ref
session_id
analysis_id / query_run_ref nullable
base_repo_ref
base_commit
target_commit / target_patch_ref nullable
selected_trace_event_refs
runner_version
mode: final-verify | patch-apply | command-replay | visual-only
sandbox_profile
started_at
finished_at
status: passed | failed | partial | unsafe | unverified
verifier_commands_json
result_events_json
produced_artifact_refs_json
assertion_refs_json
```

Store the attempt result as assertions/judgments over the session, commit, and trace events. The user-tier assertions table already supports `target_ref`, `scope_ref`, `kind`, `value_json`, `body_text`, `author_ref`, `author_kind`, `evidence_refs_json`, `status`, `visibility`, `confidence`, `staleness_json`, and `context_policy_json` (`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/user.py:7-31`); assertion kinds include `annotation`, `correction`, `saved_query`, `recall_pack`, `judgment`, `run_state`, `prompt_eval`, and `pathology` (`polylogue/core/enums.py:399-428`). The missing part is a first-class target kind and import/write affordance for reproduction attempts.

[proposal] Add target kinds beyond the current user-state registry. Today the canonical registry supports `session`, `message`, `work_event`, `thread`, `block`, `attachment`, and `paste_span`, and explicitly says some stable identities are not listed until external work lands (`polylogue/core/user_state_targets.py:1-21`, `29-95`). For replay/reproduction, add:

```text
query_run
result_relation
analysis_run
trace_event
reproduction_attempt
artifact
repo
commit
bead
```

[evidence] This fits the B8 contract rather than fighting it. B8 recommends a single `PolylogueService` with `query`, `read`, `preview`, `complete`, `act`, `status`, plus possibly `facets` (`B8_contract.md:134-168`). `read` should execute `QueryProjectionSpec` rather than named views (`B8_contract.md:188-205`), and `act` is the typed mutation/effect verb (`B8_contract.md:221-241`). fileciteturn1file8

[proposal] Therefore do **not** add a top-level `replay` RPC. Use:

```text
read({ selection: session/ref, projection: work-trace | reproduction-plan })
act(kind="record-reproduction-attempt", ...)
act(kind="run-safe-verifiers", ...)
```

The daemon/CLI/MCP surfaces remain thin and shared. This is important because B7 identifies `cli/archive_query.py` as a second engine and says it should shrink to formatting while substrate execution moves behind `Polylogue` (`B7_thinning.md:29-65`). fileciteturn1file17

[proposal] The near-term replayability classifier is the safety hinge:

```text
pure_read          e.g. ls, cat, rg, git status, git diff
safe_verify        e.g. pytest, mypy, devtools verify, cargo test
mutating_patch     e.g. file edits, sed -i, apply_patch, git checkout
networked          e.g. curl, gh, npm install, provider API calls
secret_sensitive   e.g. env, credentials, cloud deploys
interactive        e.g. editor, TUI, prompts
unknown
```

Only `pure_read` and `safe_verify` should be auto-runnable by default. Mutating commands should be replayed only inside a disposable worktree/sandbox, and network/secret-sensitive commands should be plan-only unless explicitly allowed.

[proposal] The near-term runner should operate this way:

1. Resolve session → trace events.
2. Resolve repo root and candidate base commit.
3. Build a disposable worktree at base commit.
4. Optionally apply the session-produced patch or checkout the target commit.
5. Run verifier commands, not every historical command.
6. Compare verifier results with the original session’s structured tool outcomes.
7. Write a `reproduction_attempt` plus `judgment` assertions.
8. Render a proof card.

[evidence] This preserves the existing daemon direction. A3 says the daemon request handler should become the single execution core, with `--no-daemon`/library/MCP/tests invoking the same core in-process, and that warm daemon is required for speed/composer while break-glass is a transport swap, not a parallel codebase (`A3_daemonless.md:7-31`). It also notes the Python substrate must remain directly constructable for CI/cloud/tests/recovery (`A3_daemonless.md:120-145`). fileciteturn1file17

[proposal] For session replay specifically, near-term UI should split two products that bead `bby.12` currently risks conflating:

`session playback`: timeline/scrubber/cost/file/commit rails, no side effects.

`session reproduction`: creates a sandbox, applies target state, runs verifiers, writes a verdict.

Keep `bby.12` for playback. Add a new bead for reproduction.

Suggested bead:

```text
polylogue-REPRO.1 — Work-trace reproduction harness: verify a session’s repo work from clean checkout

Parent: polylogue-7xv or polylogue-1xc/3tl depending operator priority
Priority: P1 if tied to external proof demo; otherwise P2
Type: feature

Description:
Polylogue can already reconstruct action evidence and correlate sessions to repos/commits,
but cannot safely reproduce a coding session’s work. Build a work-trace/reproduction
harness that turns one session into a replayable proof bundle: repo base, trace events,
touched files, produced commits/patches, verifier commands, and a recorded reproduction verdict.

Design:
Derived work-trace materializer over actions/session_runs/session_work_events/session_repos/
session_commits/raw_artifacts/assertions. Add replayability classification and a reproduction
attempt record. Default mode is final-state verification in a disposable git worktree, not
blind command replay. `read --projection work-trace` renders the trace; `act(kind=run-safe-verifiers)`
records the attempt as assertions/judgments.

Acceptance:
1. Given a fixture coding session with Bash/tool calls, file edits, and a final test command,
   Polylogue renders a work-trace with ordered actions, cwd/repo/commit, touched paths,
   error/exit-code evidence, and source refs.
2. Given a repo fixture, reproduction creates a disposable worktree at the selected base,
   applies the target patch/commit or checks out target commit, runs verifier commands,
   and records pass/fail as a reproduction_attempt plus assertions.
3. Unsafe/network/secret/interactively mutating commands are classified and not auto-run.
4. A report card cites original action refs and reproduction attempt refs.
5. `devtools test <fixture tests>` green; no CLI direct storage reads added.
```

## Layer 3 — Full direction

[proposal] The full design is **replay as a provenance DAG**, not a script log.

The graph should connect:

```text
session → run → message → block/action
action → tool result
action → file observation/artifact
action → repo snapshot
repo snapshot → commit/patch/status
query/run/analysis → trace selection
reproduction attempt → verifier commands/results
assertions/judgments → evidence refs
report → query/reproduction/cohort refs
```

[evidence] The existing architecture is already pointed this way. The swarm brief’s read algebra is `Query × Projection × Render`, with query units for actions/files/runs/observed-events/context-snapshots/assertions and projection families including sessions/messages/blocks/actions/raw/context/chronicle/neighbors/correlation/temporal/assertions (`SWARM_BRIEF.md:9-28`). B8’s `ReadRequest` recommendation explicitly wires selection + projection + render as the read input (`B8_contract.md:188-205`). fileciteturn1file8

[proposal] Full replay requires storing more than Polylogue currently guarantees. The archive must store, or link to a system that stores:

```text
Per action:
- normalized tool invocation
- raw tool input JSON
- shell/script/argv split
- cwd
- environment allowlist + redacted secret markers
- stdin if any
- timeout
- sandbox/network policy
- started_at/ended_at
- stdout/stderr/output refs with truncation markers
- exit code and error flag
- tool/runtime version

Per repo:
- repo root and origin
- branch
- HEAD before/after each mutating cluster
- index/worktree status before/after
- patch/diff after mutating cluster
- changed path list
- file hashes before/after
- file modes, renames, deletions
- submodule/LFS/annex references
- lockfile/devenv/Nix flake state

Per artifact:
- path/URI
- content hash/blob ref
- producer action/session
- consumer action/session
- media/type/support status
- redaction/privacy tier

Per reproduction attempt:
- base commit
- target commit/patch
- runner version
- selected event range
- sandbox profile
- verifier commands
- outputs
- verdict
- evidence refs
```

[evidence] The raw-log already points to the broader machine-observability layer: terminal sessions, web provenance, neovim logs, ActivityWatch-like data, and explicit desire to reconstruct what was happening across the desktop are recurring themes; one raw-log entry specifically says Polylogue could correlate/connect logs with git commits, issues, and PRs (`logs.raw-log.md`, 2026-04-22 13:45:04), and another notes the need to analyze wall-clock time in agent sessions such as edit/build/test cycles (`logs.raw-log.md`, 2026-04-21 23:24:03). fileciteturn1file4

[evidence] Bead `polylogue-6mv` is the important boundary: Polylogue should own raw AI-session evidence while Sinex owns redacted machine-timeline events and causal windows. Bead `polylogue-fs1.9` already points to a future Polylogue→Sinex derived agent-trace emitter. So full L5 replay belongs to the combined Polylogue+Sinex system, not Polylogue alone.

[proposal] Full deterministic replay should be opt-in and capture-mode-dependent. Sessions captured before the work-trace substrate can often be reconstructed and verified, but not deterministically replayed. Sessions captured after the substrate lands can be classed by evidence completeness:

```text
replay_class A: exact verifier reproduction available
replay_class B: patch/commit reproduction available
replay_class C: action-level command replay possible for safe commands
replay_class D: visual/evidence replay only
replay_class E: insufficient evidence
```

[proposal] The strongest external demo would not say “we replayed every command.” It would say:

“Polylogue reconstructed this agent session, checked out the repo at the recorded base, applied the produced diff/commit, reran the exact verifier class, and recorded a pass/fail verdict with links to the original tool outputs and reproduction outputs.”

That is defensible, useful, and far less brittle than pretending every historical command can be replayed.

## Feasibility verdict

[evidence] **Forensic reconstruction is high-feasibility today.** The archive already stores raw payloads, structured tool use/results, exit codes, file paths, sessions/runs/events/context snapshots, repo metadata, and some commit links (`source.py:15-102`; `index.py:182-224`, `324-343`, `470-512`, `689-709`, `913-1015`).

[evidence] **Final-state verification is medium-feasibility today, high with a near-term work-trace substrate.** Today a human/agent can inspect actions and run likely verification commands manually. Near-term, Polylogue can generate the worktree/verifier plan and record the verdict.

[evidence] **Patch/commit reproduction is medium-feasibility near-term.** The open `polylogue-7xv` bead already scopes native git/repo awareness; the current code has typed repo/commit tables and explicit parser-git commit persistence, but the older `session_commit.py` detector still has a placeholder persistence function (`session_commit.py:455-468`).

[evidence] **Blind command re-execution is low-feasibility today.** The action view does not guarantee normalized action-level cwd/env/stdin/sandbox/tool version/pre/post file hashes (`index.py:324-343`), and some commands are unsafe, nondeterministic, networked, or secret-bearing.

[proposal] **Deterministic full replay is a long-term capture-mode claim, not an archive-backfill claim.** It needs Sinex-like machine traces plus stricter repo/file snapshots and sandbox/environment capture.

## Concrete architecture

[proposal] Add these derived/read objects:

```text
work_trace_event
repo_snapshot
artifact_observation_edge
reproduction_plan
reproduction_attempt
reproduction_verdict
```

[proposal] Add these projection presets, not hardcoded silos:

```text
work-trace
reproduction-plan
reproduction-card
claim-vs-reproduction
session-playback
```

[proposal] Add these query examples:

```text
actions where session:<id> AND (is_error:true OR exit_code > 0)
files where session:<id> | group by path | count
runs where session:<id>
observed-events where session:<id> AND kind:tool_finished
assertions where target_ref:reproduction_attempt:<id>
```

[proposal] Add these commands as thin client calls over the shared service:

```text
polylogue read session:<id> --projection work-trace
polylogue reproduce plan session:<id> --json
polylogue reproduce verify session:<id> --mode final-state --worktree /tmp/...
polylogue reproduce card reproduction_attempt:<id>
```

Under B8’s contract, `plan` and `card` are `read` projections; `verify` is an `act` because it creates a reproduction attempt and writes assertions.

## What the archive must store

[evidence] Already stored or partially stored:

```text
raw session payload and blob refs                 source.py:15-59
raw artifact observations                         source.py:84-102
session git branch/repo/commit hints              index.py:51-55
messages and blocks with structured tool fields   index.py:92-125, 182-208
tool result error/exit fields                     index.py:195-196
actions paired tool_use/tool_result view          index.py:324-343
working dirs, repos, session_repos, commits       index.py:470-512
session work events with file/tool evidence       index.py:689-709
runs/observed-events/context snapshots            index.py:913-1015
assertions/judgments over evidence refs           user.py:7-31; enums.py:399-447
```

[proposal] Missing or insufficiently normalized:

```text
action-level cwd/env/sandbox/network/timeout
argv/script normalization separate from raw command text
stdin and input-file refs
stdout/stderr blob refs with truncation markers
pre/post git HEAD and dirty status
pre/post file hashes for touched paths
patch bundles linked to action ranges
artifact producer/consumer edges
dependency lockfile/devenv/Nix state
safe/unsafe replayability classification
reproduction attempt object and verdict assertions
query_run/result_relation/analysis_run targets
```

## Bead implications

[evidence] This should not become a Fable/demo silo. The existing bead set already implies the capability across multiple towers:

`polylogue-bby.12`: visual session replay.

`polylogue-7xv`: native git/repo/session↔commit awareness.

`polylogue-6mv`: Polylogue/Sinex boundary for agent traces.

`polylogue-x4s`: devloop state as assertions/substrate.

`polylogue-4c0`: session↔bead work-history joins.

`polylogue-s7ae.5`: two agents, one repo, overlap/message/context/handoff proof.

`polylogue-fs1.9`: Polylogue→Sinex derived agent-trace emitter.

`polylogue-9l5.7`: statistics/measure registry with construct-validity metadata.

`polylogue-3tl`: external legibility / citable proof artifacts.

[proposal] Add one new explicit bead because none of those owns “verify/reproduce a session’s repo work” end-to-end. Parent choice:

Best parent if proof-driven: `polylogue-3tl` or a child under `polylogue-sru`/`tf2` demo lineage.

Best parent if substrate-driven: `polylogue-7xv`.

I would parent it under `polylogue-7xv` and add a `relates-to` edge to `polylogue-3tl`, `polylogue-bby.12`, `polylogue-4c0`, and `polylogue-6mv`.

## Open questions for the operator

1. [proposal] Do you want the first shipped claim to be “verifies final work” or “replays command history”? I strongly recommend the first.

2. [proposal] Should the reproduction attempt be allowed to run networked commands at all, or should networked steps always be plan-only unless explicitly whitelisted?

3. [proposal] What is the canonical repo environment target: plain git worktree, Nix/devenv shell, container, or “use whatever the session used”? I recommend disposable git worktree + optional Nix/devenv profile when detected.

4. [proposal] Should Polylogue store patch bundles itself, or only link commits/artifacts and let git remain the patch store? I recommend content-addressed patch artifacts for session-produced uncommitted changes, but ordinary git commits for committed work.

5. [proposal] How much belongs in Polylogue vs Sinex? My answer: Polylogue owns session semantics, tool evidence, reproduction plans, and verdicts; Sinex supplies machine/process/filesystem timeline for higher replay classes.

6. [proposal] Should reproduction attempts be durable by default? I recommend yes if user/agent explicitly ran `reproduce verify`; no for ordinary preview/planning.

## What’s missing

[evidence] I did not run the daemon, tests, or live `polylogue` commands. The line refs are from the uploaded tarball and markdown reports, not live checkout.

[evidence] I did not verify whether `polylogue-7xv`, `polylogue-bby.12`, or the later bead-set changes have moved after the bundle snapshot. The pasted Claude Code session indicates later bead churn and even mentions the snapshot hazard; live `bd show` should confirm status/parents before filing new work. fileciteturn1file9

[evidence] I did not inspect every provider parser for whether action-level cwd/env is sometimes present inside raw `tool_input`; I only verified that the normalized schema does not guarantee it.

[evidence] I did not inspect the full implementation of `query_files`/file unit lowering; I relied on the query metadata and table schemas.

[evidence] I did not read or run Sinex sources; the Polylogue↔Sinex boundary is grounded in bead `polylogue-6mv` and the bundle descriptions, not current Sinex code.

[evidence] I did not check whether `session_commit.py`’s placeholder persistence has been replaced in live code. In this snapshot it is still placeholder (`polylogue/insights/session_commit.py:455-468`).

[evidence] I did not test whether old archived sessions have enough raw data to reconstruct cwd/env from provider-specific payloads. That is a necessary sampling task before claiming backfill coverage.
