## [assistant 337]
According to the 2026-07-05 bundle snapshot, I would make **queries-as-first-class-objects** a near-term substrate bead, not just a composer nicety. The defended recommendation is:

**[proposal] Store every committed query execution as an `ops.db` `query_run` with a stable ref and result-relation ref; promote only named/cited/saved results into durable `user.db` objects.** Do not make every query a `user.db` assertion. Assertions should attach to query/query-run/result objects; they should not be the only storage mechanism for those objects.

**Runner-up rejected:** use the existing `AssertionKind.SAVED_QUERY` / `RECALL_PACK` machinery as the whole model. It is tempting because those enum values already exist (`polylogue/core/enums.py:415-416`) and recall-pack HTTP endpoints already exist (`polylogue/daemon/user_state_http.py:445-508`). I reject it as the main model because it collapses three different things — query definition, execution event, and result relation — into a user-overlay table. It also cannot yet attach cleanly to query objects because the public object-ref vocabulary has `saved_view` and `recall_pack`, but no `query`, `query_run`, or `result_relation` kind (`polylogue/core/refs.py:8-38`, `polylogue/core/refs.py:197-213`).

I am assuming the code snapshot in `polylogue-all.tar(69).gz` is the intended bundle state, not necessarily live HEAD. The local tree should verify all path:line references before turning this into Beads or code.

## 0. Frontier in one paragraph

**[evidence]** The read side already thinks algebraically: the swarm brief states the baseline as `Query × Projection × Render`; query has boolean predicates, field predicates, FTS, semantic, structural `exists <unit>(...)`, `seq(...)`, and pipeline stages, while projection/render are separate layers. It also names `fnm.12` macros and `fnm.13` set algebra as roadmap items. `SWARM_BRIEF.md:9-34` fileciteturn1file13L9-L34

**[evidence]** The hot-daemon direction says the client should do no substrate work, should speak UDS to a warm daemon, and the composer should use `complete(partial)` and `preview(spec)` in single-digit ms. `SWARM_BRIEF.md:48-65` fileciteturn1file13L48-L65

**[evidence]** B8 already proposes a `query` verb returning `SearchEnvelope`, a `read` verb, `preview`, `complete`, `act`, and `status`, with `facets` likely separate. `B8_contract.md:134-168` fileciteturn1file9L134-L168

**[proposal]** The missing frontier is: every committed `query`/`read`/`preview→commit` should create a typed object graph:

```text
query_definition?  →  query_run  →  result_relation  →  render_artifact?
                         │              │
                         │              └─ result_members / fingerprint / sample
                         └─ assertions / annotations / analysis_step refs
```

The important jump is not “save query text.” It is **make the question, its execution, and its resulting relation addressable separately.**

## 1. With today’s substrate

### What is already possible

**[evidence]** `user.db` already has a unified assertions table. It stores `scope_ref`, `target_ref`, `kind`, `value_json`, `body_text`, `author_ref`, `author_kind`, `evidence_refs_json`, `status`, `visibility`, `confidence`, `staleness_json`, `context_policy_json`, `supersedes_json`, and timestamps. The table comment explicitly says marks, annotations, corrections, suppressions, tags, metadata, saved views, recall packs, workspaces, and blackboard notes are represented there. `polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/user.py:7-31`

**[evidence]** The assertion kind vocabulary already includes `SAVED_QUERY`, `RECALL_PACK`, `JUDGMENT`, `RUN_STATE`, `PROMPT_EVAL`, `TRANSFORM_CANDIDATE`, and `PATHOLOGY`. Lifecycle states include `active`, `candidate`, `accepted`, `rejected`, `deferred`, `superseded`, and `deleted`. `polylogue/core/enums.py:399-447`

**[evidence]** The write path can upsert assertions with explicit target, scope, author, evidence refs, status, visibility, confidence, staleness, context policy, and supersession. `polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/user_write.py:901-999`

**[evidence]** The API already exposes assertion read/review affordances: `list_assertion_claims`, `list_assertion_claim_payloads`, `list_assertion_candidates`, `list_assertion_candidate_reviews`, and `judge_assertion_candidate`. `polylogue/api/archive.py:2079-2206`

**[evidence]** Assertion rows are queryable as terminal query units: `QueryUnitKind` includes `assertion`, and `AssertionQueryRowPayload` exposes target/scope/kind/key/body/value/author/status/visibility/evidence/staleness/context fields. `polylogue/surfaces/payloads.py:1252-1261`, `polylogue/surfaces/payloads.py:1407-1426`

**[evidence]** The assertion query metadata includes structural fields for `author`, `author_kind`, `body`, `context`, `evidence`, `key`, `kind`, `scope`, `scope_ref`, `status`, `target`, `target_ref`, `text`, `time`, `value`, and `visibility`. `polylogue/archive/query/metadata.py:507-525`

So today, an external demo can already fake the workflow:

1. Run a query through CLI/API/MCP.
2. Save the result-set manually as a recall pack, or as an external JSON artifact.
3. Ask an agent to annotate sessions/messages/actions/assertions.
4. Import the annotations as assertion rows targeting existing refs.
5. Query `assertions where ...` for aggregate analysis.

This is enough for a crude Fable/delegation demo, but not a clean substrate demo.

### What is blocked today

**[evidence]** Public object refs include `session`, `message`, `block`, `attachment`, `paste_span`, `work_event`, `phase`, `thread`, `file`, `branch`, `commit`, `check-run`, `workspace`, `agent`, `user`, `repo`, `insight`, `run`, `context-snapshot`, `observed-event`, `assertion`, `saved_view`, `recall_pack`, `transform`, `tool-call`, `subagent-report`, and GitHub refs. There is no `query`, `query_run`, `query_definition`, `result_relation`, `cohort`, `analysis`, or `annotation_batch`. `polylogue/core/refs.py:8-38`

**[evidence]** `normalize_object_ref_text` parses and validates object refs against that closed kind map, so a string like `query_run:abc` is not merely undocumented; it should fail as an unsupported object-ref kind until the registry expands. `polylogue/core/refs.py:197-213`

**[evidence]** `ops.db` currently has operational tables such as `ingest_cursor`, `ingest_attempts`, `convergence_debt`, `cursor_lag_samples`, `daemon_stage_events`, `daemon_events`, `embedding_catchup_runs`, and OTLP tables, but no `query_runs` / `result_relations` table. `polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/ops.py:10-158`

**[evidence]** User-state target kinds are still reader-oriented: session, message, work_event, thread, block, attachment, paste_span, plus some storage-only kinds. There is no query or result target there either. `polylogue/core/user_state_targets.py:1-22`, `polylogue/core/user_state_targets.py:52-115`

**[evidence]** C10’s composer design already proposed recall entries: every commit writes query text, resolved spec, result fingerprint, and timestamp to `user.db`; naming a recall entry promotes it to a macro; recalled entries store resolved specs, not only text. `C10_composer_ux.md:221-230` fileciteturn1file15L221-L230

**[proposal]** Today’s limitation is therefore precise: Polylogue can store **claims about existing archive objects**, and can store **recall packs**, but it cannot yet make the **query act itself** a typed, ref-addressable archive object. That means no clean `assertion.target_ref = query_run:...`, no query-run lineage, no query-object composition, no “from this prior result” syntax, and no self-audit of query usage beyond generic daemon/OTLP events.

## 2. Near-term substrate change

This is the concrete implementation frontier I would turn into a bead.

### Storage-tier decision

**[proposal]** Use **`ops.db` for automatic query telemetry** and **`user.db` for promoted durable analytical objects**.

`ops.db` should receive every committed query run by default because query executions are operational events. They are high-volume, disposable-ish, and useful for latency/debug/self-observation. This matches the existing role of `ops.db` as disposable daemon telemetry and operational state (`polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/ops.py:1-158`).

`user.db` should receive durable objects only when the operator or an agent intentionally saves/promotes them: saved query definitions, named cohorts, cited result snapshots, analysis runs, reports, and assertions about any of those. This matches `user.db`’s role as irreplaceable overlay state, and it avoids turning ordinary `polylogue find ...` usage into permanent clutter.

The doctrine from the compaction memory agrees with this shape: durable `source.db`/`user.db` use explicit additive migrations, derived tiers rebuild, and `ops.db` remains disposable bootstrap/ALTER territory. `Pasted text(35).txt:73-77` fileciteturn0file0L73-L77

### Minimal schema

**[proposal]** Add these `ops.db` tables:

```sql
CREATE TABLE query_runs (
    query_run_id          TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
    parent_query_run_id   TEXT,
    actor_ref             TEXT,
    actor_kind            TEXT,
    surface               TEXT NOT NULL,       -- cli|mcp|tui|web|api|agent
    verb                  TEXT NOT NULL,       -- query|read|preview_commit|facets
    input_text            TEXT,
    query_request_json    TEXT NOT NULL,
    lowered_spec_json     TEXT,
    projection_spec_json  TEXT,
    render_spec_json      TEXT,
    archive_root_hash     TEXT,
    archive_epoch_json    TEXT,
    started_at_ms         INTEGER NOT NULL,
    finished_at_ms        INTEGER,
    status                TEXT NOT NULL,       -- running|completed|failed|cancelled
    degraded_json         TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}',
    diagnostics_json      TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}',
    result_relation_id    TEXT,
    render_artifact_refs_json TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT '[]',
    trace_id              TEXT,
    span_id               TEXT
) STRICT;
```

```sql
CREATE TABLE result_relations (
    result_relation_id    TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
    query_run_id          TEXT NOT NULL,
    grain                 TEXT NOT NULL,       -- session|message|action|block|assertion|file|run|...
    identity_policy       TEXT NOT NULL,       -- physical|logical|content|lineage-root
    member_storage        TEXT NOT NULL,       -- fingerprint|sample|exact_inline|exact_table|dynamic
    total_count           INTEGER,
    count_precision       TEXT NOT NULL,       -- exact|estimate|capped|unknown
    result_fingerprint    TEXT,
    sample_refs_json      TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT '[]',
    capped_at             INTEGER,
    created_at_ms         INTEGER NOT NULL
) STRICT;
```

```sql
CREATE TABLE result_relation_members (
    result_relation_id    TEXT NOT NULL,
    ordinal               INTEGER NOT NULL,
    object_ref            TEXT NOT NULL,
    score                 REAL,
    payload_json          TEXT,
    PRIMARY KEY(result_relation_id, ordinal)
) STRICT;
```

Use `result_relation_members` only for exact or deliberately snapshotted relations. Most routine query runs should store a fingerprint + sample refs, not the entire member set.

**[proposal]** Add these durable `user.db` tables or assertion-backed equivalents:

```sql
CREATE TABLE query_definitions (
    query_definition_id   TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
    name                  TEXT UNIQUE,
    input_text            TEXT NOT NULL,
    normalized_spec_json  TEXT NOT NULL,
    default_projection_json TEXT,
    default_render_json   TEXT,
    author_ref            TEXT NOT NULL,
    visibility            TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'private',
    created_at_ms         INTEGER NOT NULL,
    updated_at_ms         INTEGER NOT NULL
) STRICT;
```

```sql
CREATE TABLE cohorts (
    cohort_id             TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
    name                  TEXT UNIQUE,
    kind                  TEXT NOT NULL,       -- dynamic|snapshot
    grain                 TEXT NOT NULL,
    identity_policy       TEXT NOT NULL,
    query_definition_id   TEXT,
    source_query_run_id   TEXT,
    result_relation_id    TEXT,
    member_count          INTEGER,
    member_fingerprint    TEXT,
    description           TEXT,
    created_at_ms         INTEGER NOT NULL,
    updated_at_ms         INTEGER NOT NULL
) STRICT;
```

I would still allow `AssertionKind.SAVED_QUERY` and `AssertionKind.RECALL_PACK` as compatibility/projection rows, but the durable primary keys should be typed rows if we want a serious algebra.

### Object-ref expansion

**[proposal]** Add public ref kinds:

```text
query-definition:<id>
query-run:<id>
result-relation:<id>
cohort:<id>
analysis:<id>
analysis-step:<id>
annotation-batch:<id>
report:<id>
```

Minimum first slice: `query-run`, `result-relation`, `query-definition`, `cohort`.

This unlocks assertions attached to queries:

```json
{
  "target_ref": "query-run:qr_20260705_abc",
  "scope_ref": "analysis:fable_delegate_tone_v1",
  "kind": "judgment",
  "key": "methodology.validity",
  "value_json": {"label": "biased_sample", "severity": "medium"},
  "evidence_refs_json": ["result-relation:rr_20260705_def"],
  "author_ref": "agent:gpt-5.5-pro",
  "author_kind": "agent",
  "status": "candidate"
}
```

Strictly, `evidence_refs_json` currently normalizes public refs through `normalize_public_ref_text`, which today accepts object refs or evidence refs. Once `result-relation` is an object-ref kind, it can participate. `polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/user_write.py:941-946`, `polylogue/core/refs.py:190-206`

### Service contract change

**[evidence]** B8 wants all client/substrate communication through typed DTO verbs and specifically says `query` should collapse list/search/count into one response envelope, while `act` should absorb mutations including annotations/corrections/saved views/judgments/ingest. `B8_contract.md:151-168`, `B8_contract.md:231-241` fileciteturn1file9L151-L168 fileciteturn1file9L231-L241

**[proposal]** Extend those DTOs, not the method count.

`query(QueryRequest) -> QueryResponse` should return:

```json
{
  "query_run_ref": "query-run:...",
  "result_relation_ref": "result-relation:...",
  "grain": "session",
  "total": 142,
  "count_precision": "exact",
  "items": [...],
  "diagnostics": {...},
  "route_state": {...}
}
```

For backward compatibility, this can initially be `SearchEnvelope` plus optional `query_run_ref` and `result_relation_ref`.

`preview(QueryRequest)` should not persist every keystroke by default. It can return an ephemeral `preview_id` for cancellation/debugging, but only **commit** creates a `query_run` unless `debug_record_previews=true`.

`read(ReadRequest)` should accept `selection_ref` as an alternative to inline query:

```json
{
  "selection_ref": "result-relation:rr_...",
  "projection": {...},
  "render": {...}
}
```

`act(ActionRequest)` should gain these kinds:

```text
save_query_definition
save_cohort
promote_result_relation
attach_assertion
import_annotation_batch
delete_query_run        -- probably ops/admin only
pin_query_run           -- promote from ops to user-visible
```

### DSL syntax

**[evidence]** Existing design already has `@` macro completion and `@arm_pack | except (@arm_raw)` examples for composed cohorts/macros. `C10_composer_ux.md:223-230` fileciteturn1file15L223-L230

**[proposal]** Keep `@name` for dynamic saved query definitions/macros. Do not overload it for every result.

Recommended DSL:

```text
@macro
```

expands a dynamic saved query definition.

```text
from query-definition:<id>
```

re-evaluates the saved query definition.

```text
from query-run:<id>
```

uses the result relation produced by that specific run if retained; otherwise errors with “run has no retained result relation.”

```text
from result-relation:<id>
```

uses a stored relation directly.

```text
from cohort:<name-or-id>
```

uses a durable named cohort. If the cohort is dynamic, it re-evaluates; if snapshot, it yields stored members.

Examples:

```text
from query-run:qr_fable_candidates_001
  | intersect (@strict_directives)
  | read with assertions
```

```text
from result-relation:rr_20260705_fable_delegations
  | group by assertion.value.directive_intensity
  | count
```

```text
@fable_delegations
  | except (from cohort:claude_family_subagents)
  | read layout:delegation-card
```

**[proposal]** A query referencing another query should lower to a typed AST node:

```text
RefOperand(kind=query_definition|query_run|result_relation|cohort, ref=...)
```

Do not textual-expand everything. Textual macro expansion is fine for `@macro`, but `from query-run:<id>` should remain a provenance-preserving reference node so `explain` can show the parent query/run/result lineage.

### MCP affordances

**[proposal]** MCP should expose ergonomic tools even if internally they all call the B8 `query/read/act` verbs.

Minimum:

```text
polylogue_query
  input: QueryRequest
  output: QueryResponse with query_run_ref/result_relation_ref

polylogue_read
  input: ReadRequest, including selection_ref
  output: ReadEnvelope/rendered artifact ref

polylogue_save_query
  input: name, query_run_ref or input_text/spec
  output: query_definition_ref

polylogue_save_cohort
  input: name, result_relation_ref, kind=snapshot|dynamic
  output: cohort_ref

polylogue_assert
  input: target_ref, scope_ref, kind, key, value/body, evidence_refs
  output: assertion_ref

polylogue_import_annotation_batch
  input: schema_id, scope_ref, rows[]
  output: annotation_batch_ref + assertion refs

polylogue_get_query_run
  input: query_run_ref
  output: full envelope, parent refs, result refs

polylogue_explain_ref
  input: query_definition|query_run|result_relation|cohort ref
  output: provenance/explain tree
```

This makes the agent loop easy:

```text
query → get result_relation_ref
read evidence pack for that relation
annotate rows
import annotation batch
query assertions scoped to the batch
save cohort/report
```

That is the scalable version of the external annotation recipe you described.

## 3. Full direction

The full design is not “query history.” It is **analysis provenance**.

**[proposal]** The object graph should eventually include:

```text
analysis
  ├─ analysis_step
  │    ├─ query_run
  │    │    └─ result_relation
  │    ├─ evidence_pack / render_artifact
  │    ├─ annotation_batch
  │    │    └─ assertions
  │    └─ report
  └─ final cohort(s)
```

Queries become one node type in a larger analysis DAG. That matters because complex analyses are loops, not static YAML:

1. Agent runs broad query.
2. Sees noisy results.
3. Saves a narrowed query.
4. Exports evidence pack.
5. Annotates evidence.
6. Queries annotations.
7. Finds counterexamples.
8. Revises schema.
9. Writes report.

A YAML recipe can describe the intended loop, but the durable truth is the run graph.

**[proposal]** This graph also solves “Polylogue tracks its own use.” The CLI, TUI, web workbench, MCP, and external agents all become actors that produce query runs, reads, actions, annotations, cohorts, reports, and context packs. Polylogue can then analyze:

```text
query-runs where actor_kind:agent and status:failed
```

```text
query-runs where degraded:true | group by degraded.reason | count
```

```text
analysis-runs where report_ref:* and query_run.count_precision:capped
```

```text
assertions where target_ref:query-run:* and key:methodology.caveat
```

**[proposal]** The full DSL should treat prior query results as first-class relations, not as saved text snippets. A query result has grain. That makes `result-relation:...` algebraically valid only when the downstream operation accepts its grain. A message-result relation cannot silently flow into a session-only action. This follows the set-algebra / composer doctrine in C10: grain mismatch should fail closed and surface suggestions rather than broaden silently. `C10_composer_ux.md:206-230` fileciteturn1file15L206-L230

**[proposal]** Continuous queries are then just installed query definitions with triggers:

```text
continuous_query {
  query_definition_ref
  schedule_or_event
  action: save_result_relation | notify | create_candidate_assertions | refresh_cohort
}
```

Do not build continuous queries in the first slice. The first slice should only make committed query runs and saved result relations real.

## Concrete bead I would create

**Title:** First-class query runs and result relations

**Parent:** likely `polylogue-fnm` or `polylogue-t46`; I lean `t46` if the first deliverable is protocol DTOs, `fnm` if the first deliverable is DSL/reference syntax. It also relates to `37t.12` because external annotation batches need query/result targets. Existing relevant bead IDs: `polylogue-fnm.12` user-defined macros, `polylogue-fnm.13` set algebra, `polylogue-4p1` one read algebra, `polylogue-t46` contracts own surfaces, `polylogue-37t.12` judgment queue.

**Description:** Queries currently execute as transient operations or composer recall entries. Agents and operators need addressable query definitions, query runs, and result relations so analysis can be iterative, citable, annotatable, and composable.

**Design:**

1. Add ObjectRef kinds `query-definition`, `query-run`, `result-relation`, `cohort`.
2. Add `ops.db.query_runs`, `ops.db.result_relations`, and optional `ops.db.result_relation_members`.
3. Extend `SearchEnvelope` / query response with `query_run_ref`, `result_relation_ref`, `grain`, `count_precision`.
4. Add `user.db.query_definitions` and `user.db.cohorts`, or an equivalent assertion-backed compatibility layer with typed rows as primary.
5. Add `act` kinds `save_query_definition`, `save_cohort`, `promote_result_relation`, `attach_assertion`, `import_annotation_batch`.
6. Add DSL support for `from query-definition:<id>`, `from query-run:<id>`, `from result-relation:<id>`, and `from cohort:<id-or-name>`.
7. Add MCP tools for query, save-query, save-cohort, attach/import assertions, and explain-ref.
8. Add retention policy: previews not recorded by default; committed queries recorded in ops; promoted objects durable in user.

**Acceptance criteria:**

A CLI/MCP query returns a stable `query_run_ref` and `result_relation_ref`.

`polylogue read --selection result-relation:<id>` renders the same relation with a different projection.

`assertions` can target `query-run:<id>` and `result-relation:<id>`.

`@macro` still expands saved query definitions; `from query-run:<id>` does not textual-expand and preserves provenance in `explain`.

A result relation can be promoted to a snapshot cohort and later used as a set-op operand.

Routine preview keystrokes are not persisted unless a debug flag is set.

A migration test proves `user.db` additive migration preserves existing assertions and recall packs.

A parity test proves CLI and MCP receive the same refs for the same committed query through the shared service contract.

## Why this is the right first move

**[evidence]** The strategic brief says finished demos prove the substrate is honest, but not yet that an agent/operator completes a real task better with it; the missing gate is a committed, reproducible artifact. Query objects directly serve that gate because they let the artifact cite exactly which queries, result sets, annotation batches, and reports produced the analysis. `situation-brief(2).md:67-79`, `situation-brief(2).md:133-137` fileciteturn0file10L67-L79 fileciteturn0file10L133-L137

**[evidence]** The B7 thinning audit says the CLI currently has a second engine and must shrink to formatter/client over shared payloads; it also says query schema/parse contract and projection-as-input are first blockers. `B7_thinning.md:24-46`, `B7_thinning.md:153-168` fileciteturn0file7L24-L46 fileciteturn0file7L153-L168

**[proposal]** Query objects are a low-risk bridge between today’s evidence/archive strength and tomorrow’s analysis workbench. They do not require solving the whole recipe language, work trace replay, or continuous-query engine. They only require making the already-central operation — querying — leave behind a typed, reusable object.

## Open questions for the operator

1. Should **every committed query** be recorded in `ops.db` by default, or only queries with `--record` / agent/MCP callers? I recommend every committed query, with retention policy, because self-observation is the point; do not record every preview keystroke.

2. Should durable saved query definitions live in a new `user.db.query_definitions` table, or should the existing `AssertionKind.SAVED_QUERY` be the primary storage? I recommend a dedicated table plus assertion compatibility/projection, because query definitions are state/programs, while assertions are claims/judgments.

3. Should `@name` resolve both macros and cohorts, or should cohorts use a visibly different namespace? I recommend `@name` for dynamic query macros and `from cohort:<name>` for cohorts at first, because conflating dynamic query definitions and snapshot cohorts will create surprising freshness behavior.

4. How much of a result relation should be stored by default: fingerprint + sample, exact member list, or only exact member list when promoted? I recommend fingerprint + sample in `ops.db`; exact members only for bounded results or promoted snapshot cohorts.

5. Is `query-run:<id>` allowed as a long-lived public ref if the underlying `ops.db` row may expire? I recommend yes, but expired refs should resolve to a typed “expired operational ref” payload, not silently disappear.

6. Should annotation batches be a first-class table in the first query-object slice, or should imports just create assertions with a shared `scope_ref`? I recommend a first-class `annotation_batch` soon after query runs, but not necessarily in the same PR.

## What’s missing

I did not run the daemon, tests, or live CLI; this is static analysis of the uploaded snapshot. Live HEAD may already have moved.

I did not inspect the full `docs/design/query-set-algebra.md`; I relied on the swarm brief and C10 summary for set-op semantics.

I did not verify whether `AssertionKind.SAVED_QUERY` is currently surfaced by CLI/MCP as a real user-facing saved-query feature or only exists in the enum/storage substrate.

I did not verify Beads after the final swarm apply pass against live `bd`; the bead IDs cited here come from the bundled export/snapshot and the transcript, so priority/status may be stale.

I did not inspect generated OpenAPI/MCP tool schemas, so MCP tool names above are proposed affordances, not confirmed current tools.

## [assistant 382]
According to the 2026-07-05 bundle snapshot, my defended recommendation is: **make analysis recipes DB-native runtime objects, with YAML as import/export/source-control serialization, and keep annotation rows as assertions.** [proposal] YAML-only prompt files are the runner-up; I reject them as the canonical substrate because they cannot themselves be queried, targeted by assertions, linked to query runs/results, resumed, judged, or audited as part of the archive. [proposal] The third tempting option, “store recipes themselves as assertions,” is also wrong: assertions are authored claims about targets; recipes/runs are procedure/state. The bundle’s own schema separates `user_settings` from `assertions`, which supports this distinction. [evidence: `polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/user.py:7-49`] fileciteturn3file0

## Layer 1 — with today’s substrate

[evidence] The assertion storage substrate is substantially real. `user.db` has a strict `assertions` table with `assertion_id`, `scope_ref`, `target_ref`, `key`, `kind`, `value_json`, `body_text`, `author_ref`, `author_kind`, `evidence_refs_json`, `status`, `visibility`, `confidence`, `staleness_json`, `context_policy_json`, `supersedes_json`, and timestamps; it also has indexes by target/kind/status/visibility. [evidence: `polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/user.py:7-40`] fileciteturn3file0

[evidence] The runtime vocabulary is already broad enough for external annotations: `AssertionKind` includes `annotation`, `correction`, `saved_query`, `recall_pack`, `note`, `decision`, `caveat`, `lesson`, `blocker`, `handoff`, `judgment`, `run_state`, `prompt_eval`, `transform_candidate`, and `pathology`; lifecycle states include `active`, `candidate`, `accepted`, `rejected`, `deferred`, `superseded`, `deleted`, and `inactive`. [evidence: `polylogue/core/enums.py:399-447`] fileciteturn2file12

[evidence] The low-level writer is capable: `upsert_assertion()` accepts target, kind, scope, key, JSON value, body text, author ref/kind, evidence refs, status, visibility, confidence, staleness, context policy, and supersedes; it normalizes target/scope/author/evidence refs before insert/update. [evidence: `polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/user_write.py:901-999`] fileciteturn3file10

[evidence] Querying annotations back is partially real, not aspirational. The query grammar includes `assertion` as a structural unit, the query metadata exposes assertion fields such as `author`, `author_kind`, `author_ref`, `body`, `context`, `evidence`, `key`, `kind`, `scope_ref`, `status`, `target_ref`, `text`, `value`, and `visibility`, and `ArchiveStore.query_assertions()` executes unit-scoped assertion predicates against `user_tier.assertions`. [evidence: `SWARM_BRIEF.md:11-18`; `polylogue/archive/query/metadata.py:507-525`; `polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/archive.py:5393-5447`] fileciteturn0file9 fileciteturn3file8

[evidence] Candidate review is also real. The storage layer has `list_assertion_candidate_reviews()` and `judge_assertion_candidate()`, where decisions are `accept`, `reject`, `defer`, or `supersede`; accepted/superseded candidates can be promoted into active assertions, and the judgment itself is recorded as an assertion targeting the candidate assertion. [evidence: `polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/user_write.py:1185-1370`] fileciteturn3file3

[evidence] The API facade exposes read/review methods for claims and candidates: `list_assertion_claims`, `list_assertion_claim_payloads`, `list_assertion_candidates`, `list_assertion_candidate_reviews`, and `judge_assertion_candidate`. [evidence: `polylogue/api/archive.py:2079-2206`] fileciteturn3file12

[evidence] The shared payload layer has typed JSON-ish envelopes for assertion claims, judgments, judgment results, candidate-review items, and candidate-review lists; payload validators normalize object refs and public evidence refs. [evidence: `polylogue/surfaces/payloads.py:1465-1518`, `1554-1696`] fileciteturn3file4

[evidence] Existing high-level write APIs are still uneven. `save_annotation()` exists but is a legacy/narrow annotation method over `annotation_id`, `session_id`, `note_text`, target type/id, and optional `message_id`; it does not expose the full assertion shape to agents. `post_blackboard_note()` is richer — it accepts `author_ref`, `author_kind`, `evidence_refs`, `staleness`, and `context_policy` — but it is still semantically a blackboard note surface, not a general annotation-batch writer. [evidence: `polylogue/api/archive.py:4717-4746`, `5284-5345`] fileciteturn3file12

[evidence] The B8 contract audit says the facade exposes many loose methods, including `save_annotation`, `record_correction`, `judge_assertion_candidate`, `save_view`, `save_workspace`, and `post_blackboard_note`, but those write/read surfaces are not yet declared as a complete cross-surface contract; B8 explicitly calls out that annotate/correction/saved-view/workspace/blackboard/assertion-judgment are missing from the protocol family. [evidence: `B8_contract.md:84-124`] fileciteturn3file12

[proposal] Practical verdict for today: **storage is about 75% ready, query-back is about 55% ready, agent ergonomics are about 25% ready, and recipe substrate is about 5–10% ready.** An external agent can already produce assertion-shaped JSON and, with privileged/in-process access or a narrow existing API, store candidate annotations. It can query back through `assertions where ...` for basic fields. But it cannot yet have a smooth, stable loop of “export evidence pack → annotate JSONL under schema → import batch → query annotations → review candidates → render report” through one daemon-fast CLI/MCP/API contract.

### What is missing today for external agent annotation

[proposal] Missing 1: **general assertion import/write surface.** The agent needs `assertions import` / `act(kind=assertions.import)` / MCP equivalent that accepts JSONL rows with `target_ref`, `scope_ref`, `kind`, `key`, `value`, `body_text`, `evidence_refs`, `confidence`, `author_ref`, `author_kind`, and `status=candidate`. The low-level helper exists, but the stable external surface does not. This is exactly the kind of gap B8 says should move behind a single `act` verb rather than remaining loose facade/storage plumbing. [evidence: `B8_contract.md:151-155`, `117-124`] fileciteturn3file7

[proposal] Missing 2: **annotation schema registry.** Today `key`/`value_json` can hold arbitrary label data, but nothing declares that `directive_style_v1.directive_intensity` is an integer 0–5, requires at least one evidence ref, targets messages or delegations, has an abstain value, or was produced by a particular prompt/model. Without a schema registry, annotations remain queryable blobs rather than safe analytical variables.

[proposal] Missing 3: **annotation batches.** The unit of import should not be “many unrelated assertions.” It should be `annotation_batch:<id>` with schema id, source query/result, actor/model/prompt, import time, counts, validation failures, and review state. Each row is still an assertion; the batch is the provenance container.

[proposal] Missing 4: **analysis/run/query/result refs.** Current `ObjectRefKind` includes sessions/messages/blocks/files/commits/runs/context-snapshots/observed-events/assertions/saved_views/recall_packs/transforms/tool-calls/subagent-reports/GitHub refs, but not `analysis`, `analysis-run`, `annotation-schema`, `annotation-batch`, `query-run`, `result-relation`, or `cohort`. [evidence: `polylogue/core/refs.py:8-38`] Those refs are needed so assertions can target not only sessions/messages but also the analysis process itself.

[proposal] Missing 5: **typed JSON-value querying.** Current assertion fields include a broad `value` text/JSON substring field. That is enough for “find rows whose value mentions strict,” but not enough for “directive_intensity >= 4” or “control_devices contains read-only.” For annotation recipes, Polylogue needs schema-aware virtual fields or JSON-path predicates over assertion values.

[proposal] Missing 6: **evidence-pack export.** The annotation agent needs bounded evidence packs with stable refs, not ad hoc transcript excerpts. Existing read algebra can point in this direction, but B8 says read still executes through named views rather than the projection algebra executor. [evidence: `B8_contract.md:66-75`, `113-115`] fileciteturn3file12

[proposal] Missing 7: **operator-grade candidate review.** The storage/API candidate review exists, but the bead set still treats the actual ergonomic queue as open work: `polylogue-37t.12` is “Judgment queue: operator bulk review/accept/reject of candidate assertions”; `polylogue-p5g` is “polylogue judge: interactive candidate triage in the terminal”; `polylogue-dmp` is “polylogue note: zero-friction memory capture from the terminal.” Those are the missing affordances that make candidate assertions not rot.

## Layer 2 — near-term substrate change

[proposal] The near-term design should be: **assertion rows remain the annotation primitive; add first-class `annotation_schema`, `annotation_batch`, `analysis_recipe`, and `analysis_run` objects in `user.db`; expose them through the B8 `act/query/read/preview/complete/status/facets` shape; YAML is only a portable serialization.**

[proposal] Minimal tables or equivalent user-tier objects:

```text
annotation_schemas(
  schema_id,
  version,
  target_grain,
  value_schema_json,
  required_evidence_policy_json,
  allowed_keys_json,
  validity_note,
  created_at_ms,
  updated_at_ms
)

analysis_recipes(
  recipe_id,
  name,
  version,
  definition_json,
  source_artifact_ref,
  created_by_ref,
  created_at_ms,
  updated_at_ms
)

analysis_runs(
  analysis_run_id,
  recipe_id,
  status,
  actor_ref,
  archive_epoch,
  started_at_ms,
  finished_at_ms,
  input_refs_json,
  query_run_refs_json,
  annotation_batch_refs_json,
  artifact_refs_json,
  degraded_json
)

annotation_batches(
  batch_id,
  analysis_run_ref,
  schema_id,
  source_result_ref,
  target_grain,
  author_ref,
  author_kind,
  prompt_ref,
  model_ref,
  row_count,
  accepted_count,
  rejected_count,
  validation_json,
  created_at_ms
)
```

[proposal] Assertion rows imported by an agent should look like this:

```json
{
  "scope_ref": "annotation-batch:fable-rhetoric-v1-batch-001",
  "target_ref": "message:claude-code-session:abc123:m45",
  "kind": "judgment",
  "key": "directive_style_v1.directive_intensity",
  "value": {"score": 4, "scale": "0..5"},
  "body_text": "Strict bounded delegation with explicit non-overreach instruction.",
  "author_ref": "agent:gpt-5.5-pro",
  "author_kind": "agent",
  "evidence_refs": ["claude-code-session:abc123::m45::0"],
  "status": "candidate",
  "confidence": 0.82,
  "context_policy": {"inject": false}
}
```

[proposal] The near-term CLI/MCP affordances should be these, all daemon-backed:

```text
polylogue recipe import recipe.yaml
polylogue recipe run <recipe-id> --json
polylogue evidence-pack export --query '<query>' --projection <preset> --out evidence.jsonl
polylogue assertions import annotations.jsonl --schema directive_style_v1 --scope analysis-run:<id>
polylogue assertions query 'assertions where scope_ref:analysis-run:<id> AND key:directive_style_v1.directive_intensity'
polylogue judge --list --scope analysis-run:<id>
polylogue report render --analysis-run <id> --format markdown
```

[proposal] This uses the B8 service-contract direction rather than inventing a sidecar runner. B8’s recommended protocol already has `query`, `read`, `preview`, `complete`, `act`, `status`, and optional `facets`; `act` is explicitly the place to gather mutations such as save-annotation, correction, saved-view, assertion-judgment, and ingest. [evidence: `B8_contract.md:134-155`] fileciteturn3file7

[proposal] Recipe YAML should exist, but only as source/export. A recipe file should be importable, hash-pinned, and rendered back out from the DB. Example:

```yaml
api_version: polylogue.analysis/v1
recipe_id: fable-delegation-rhetoric
version: 1
question: >
  How does the orchestrator phrase delegation instructions to subagents?
inputs:
  corpus:
    query: 'sessions where model:Fable OR text:"subagent"'
    grain: session
evidence_pack:
  projection: delegation-card
  limit_per_target: 3
annotations:
  schema: directive_style_v1
  target_grain: message
  require_evidence_refs: true
  initial_status: candidate
  prompt_ref: file:prompts/directive-style-v1.md
post_import_queries:
  - name: strict_by_model_family
    query: 'assertions where key:directive_style_v1.directive_intensity AND value.score>=4 | group by target.session.model_family'
review:
  require_operator_judgment: true
report:
  renderer: finding-report
  outputs:
    - markdown
    - json
```

[proposal] DB-object canonicalization is better because the live object can be resumed, cited, queried, targeted by assertions, and inspected by later agents. YAML-only is attractive because it is simple, portable, and agent-readable, but it loses the whole benefit of Polylogue tracking its own analytical work. Use YAML as a declaration artifact; use the database as the execution record.

[proposal] Current bead coverage already implies this but does not name it cleanly. Relevant open/closed beads: `polylogue-37t` covers the declared-claims → judgment → preamble → reboot loop; `polylogue-37t.1` covers assertion consumer/lifecycle tightening; `polylogue-37t.2` covers agent-authored inline annotation markers; `polylogue-37t.12` covers judgment queue; `polylogue-dmp` covers zero-friction note capture; `polylogue-p5g` covers terminal candidate triage; `polylogue-fnm.12` covers user-defined query macros; `polylogue-fnm.13` covers set algebra; `polylogue-pj8` covers agent query cookbook / skill recipes; `polylogue-27p` being closed suggests MCP write access has landed in some form. The missing bead is the one that binds these into **analysis recipe + annotation batch substrate**, not another Fable-specific demo bead. [evidence: bead ids from `polylogue-beads-export.jsonl` in bundle]

## Layer 3 — full direction

[proposal] The full direction is: **analysis is a first-class graph over query runs, result relations, evidence packs, annotation batches, cohorts, reports, and artifacts.** Assertions remain the claim layer, not the workflow layer.

[proposal] Full object graph:

```text
analysis_recipe
  -> analysis_run
    -> query_run*
      -> result_relation*
        -> evidence_pack_artifact*
    -> annotation_batch*
      -> assertion*
    -> cohort*
    -> report_artifact*
```

[proposal] A **query run** is a specific execution with actor, surface, query text, lowered spec, archive epoch, degraded state, result grain, count/exactness, timing, and output refs. This generalizes C10’s recall-entry idea, where every committed composer run writes query text, resolved spec, result fingerprint, and timestamp to `user.db`. [evidence: `C10_composer_ux.md:202-219`] fileciteturn1file10

[proposal] A **result relation** is the durable/semi-durable set returned by a query, with grain and identity policy. This is the thing a recipe passes to an annotation agent. It can be exact, capped, sampled, or snapshot. It is the cleaner successor to “parse stdout and keep going.”

[proposal] A **cohort** is a named result relation. Dynamic cohort = saved query/spec; snapshot cohort = frozen refs from one archive epoch. Cohorts are needed because annotation recipes need stable input populations: “these 47 delegation messages were labeled in report v1.” They also become operands for set algebra, which is already on the query roadmap as `fnm.13` and in the composer design as live set-op preview. [evidence: `C10_composer_ux.md:183-200`; bead `polylogue-fnm.13`] fileciteturn1file10

[proposal] A **recipe** should be able to loop. The YAML example above is only the declarative first pass. The actual `analysis_run` should record that an agent queried, inspected partial results, refined the query, exported a second evidence pack, imported another annotation batch, and then rendered a report. That is why DB-object beats YAML-only: complex analyses are interactive DAGs, not static phase lists.

[proposal] A **delegation unit** belongs in this full direction, but not in the annotation substrate itself. Delegation should be a typed evidence/read unit — parent run/message/action → subordinate run/report/output → parent use — and external annotations can label delegations or their instruction messages. Do not encode delegation as a special recipe. Make it a queryable unit, then recipes can use it.

[proposal] A **measure/validity registry** should connect annotation schemas to analytics. Bead `polylogue-9l5.7` already names the right doctrine: analytics need uncertainty primitives and construct-validity metadata; every measure should declare construct, formula, evidence tier, sample-frame requirements, and confounds. Annotation schemas should reuse that discipline: a label is not just a JSON key; it is an operationalization with caveats.

## The defended recommendation

[proposal] Build **DB-native analysis recipes + annotation batches** now. Use assertions as the row-level annotation primitive. Keep YAML as import/export and as a nice demo artifact. Do not build a separate “recipe runner” silo; put it behind the same daemon-fast CLI/MCP/API contract.

Why this wins:

[evidence] The durable user tier already has an assertion model designed for authored/interpretive overlays, with status, evidence refs, staleness, context policy, and visibility. [evidence: `polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/user.py:7-40`; `polylogue/core/enums.py:399-447`] fileciteturn3file0

[evidence] The query DSL already treats assertions as a query unit, and the read algebra frame already wants `Query × Projection × Render`, not siloed commands. [evidence: `SWARM_BRIEF.md:9-34`] fileciteturn0file9

[evidence] The service-contract work says all surfaces should converge on typed request/response DTOs and a small set of verbs. Recipe/annotation import belongs there, not as a shell-only script. [evidence: `B8_contract.md:134-155`] fileciteturn3file7

[proposal] Runner-up rejected: **YAML-only recipe files executed by external coding agents.** This is useful for demos, but insufficient as substrate. It cannot answer “which query produced this batch?”, “which model labeled these rows?”, “which assertions came from report v1?”, “what did the agent see?”, “which batches were superseded?”, or “rerun this recipe against archive epoch N and diff outputs.” Those questions require DB objects and refs.

[proposal] Also rejected as a secondary runner-up: **everything as assertions.** An annotation row is an assertion; a recipe is not. A recipe is procedure/config. A run is execution state. A batch is provenance. If all of those become assertion kinds, the epistemic layer gets overloaded and `assertions where ...` becomes a dumping ground.

## Open questions for the operator

[proposal] Should accepted external-agent annotations become `status=active` assertions automatically for trusted schemas, or should all external-agent rows enter as `candidate` and require `polylogue judge`? My lean: default `candidate`; allow schema-level `trusted_actor_refs` later.

[proposal] Should annotation schemas live in `user.db` only, or can built-in schemas ship as code/config and seed into `user.db`? My lean: built-ins as versioned bundled schemas, user overrides/copies in `user.db`.

[proposal] What is the first target grain for the demo: `session`, `message`, `block`, or a new `delegation` unit? My lean: begin with `message` plus evidence windows; add `delegation` once artifact/run linking is ready.

[proposal] Should recipe runs write every query-run automatically, or only promoted/significant query-runs? My lean: all query runs in `ops.db`; promoted/cited/query-result-producing runs in `user.db`.

[proposal] Is `analysis_run` a durable user object by default, or does it start in ops and get promoted? My lean: if launched through `recipe run`, durable by default; casual CLI search stays ops by default.

[proposal] Should YAML recipes be hand-written, generated from composer sessions, or both? My lean: both; the composer can “save as recipe,” and hand-authored prompt files can import into the same representation.

## What’s missing / assumptions to verify locally

[evidence] The snapshot is dated 2026-07-05; live code and beads may have moved. Verify locally before implementing: `git status`, `rg "class AssertionKind" polylogue/core/enums.py`, `rg "def judge_assertion_candidate" polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/user_write.py`, `bd show polylogue-37t.12`, and current MCP/CLI command inventory.

[evidence] I did not run the daemon, MCP server, CLI, or tests. So “assertions are queryable” is grounded in code/DSL descriptors and storage methods, not a live command execution against the archive. [evidence: `polylogue/archive/query/metadata.py:792-805`; `polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/archive.py:5393-5447`] fileciteturn3file8

[evidence] I did not fully audit the MCP write tool list in live code. `polylogue-27p` is closed and B8 names write methods, but the exact external-agent affordance available today needs local verification. [evidence: `B8_contract.md:84-124`; bead `polylogue-27p`] fileciteturn3file12

[evidence] I did not inspect every user-tier migration or parity test. The DDL and helper code show the assertion substrate exists, but migration completeness across all old overlays should be verified by the existing user-audit tests before relying on it for external annotations. [evidence: `polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/user.py:7-49`; `polylogue/storage/sqlite/archive_tiers/user_write.py:1591-1660`] fileciteturn3file0

[proposal] The unverified claim most relevant to this design is: “a recipe-run object belongs in `user.db`, not `ops.db`.” I defended it for cited/reproducible analyses, but retention policy is an operator decision.

[proposal] The source I did not read deeply here is the current live `mcp/server` command/tool registration. That matters because the fastest path for external annotation agents may be MCP rather than CLI, even if the CLI is daemon-fast.

[proposal] The modality not run is a live annotation roundtrip: export a small evidence pack, have an agent label 5 messages, import as candidate assertions, query them back, accept one, and render it. That should be the acceptance demo for the new bead.
## [user 307]
think of many more demo ideas, grounded ones

## [assistant 322]
The right bar for these demos is: **a stranger can inspect the artifact and see a task get easier, truer, or more recoverable because Polylogue exists.** The situation brief is explicit that the current demo shelf mostly proves the substrate is honest, while the missing thing is an agent or operator completing a real task better; it names browser-captured agent recovery and claim-versus-evidence as the closest high-leverage demos. fileciteturn22file4

Below are many grounded demo ideas. I’m deliberately biasing toward things that use real existing traces: Claude Code compaction, Beads, claim/evidence data, browser capture, raw logs, agent swarms, commits, sessions, tool calls, cost data, lineage, and context packs.

## Highest-value demos to ship first

1. **Cut-session recovery pack**

A coding agent is handed a session id and a terse goal: “continue this work.” Baseline: agent gets only the user’s manual summary. Polylogue version: agent gets a recovery pack with prior session summary, relevant messages, tool calls, files touched, commits, open beads, branch state, and unresolved risks. Output: the next agent successfully performs a bounded follow-up without the user re-explaining. This directly matches the situation brief’s closest-to-done demo: browser-captured agent recovery. fileciteturn22file4

2. **Claim-versus-evidence report**

Run a corpus analysis over coding-agent sessions: find places where the assistant claimed success, but tool calls, exit codes, CI logs, failed tests, or verifier output contradicted it. Output: a report with counts by model/provider/tool, a specimen gallery, and exact evidence refs. This is probably the most externally legible “finding travels on its own” demo: “coding agents silently proceed past failed calls N% of the time.” fileciteturn21file11

3. **Claude compaction memory audit**

Use the attached Claude Code excerpt as the hook. After compaction, Claude receives a flat dump of 19 persistent Beads memories, including global doctrine, shell traps, schema rules, daemon gotchas, and cost semantics. Polylogue demo: compile a task-specific context pack from the same memory/assertion material, explain why each memory was included or omitted, and compare token load plus downstream usefulness. fileciteturn22file2

4. **“Fable as Foreman” subagent-rhetoric report**

The tweet hook becomes a general analysis: extract subagent delegations, classify instruction style, output-contract strictness, scope policing, retry behavior, and model-family routing. Output: funny specimen gallery plus serious aggregate tables. This uses the same external-annotation loop discussed earlier: an agent labels delegation events, imports judgments/assertions, then queries them.

5. **Beads swarm autopsy**

Take the huge Beads audit swarm as data. Reconstruct: prompts issued, domains assigned, subagent outputs, contradictions between auditors, critic gate decisions, applied mutations, held items, and final ledger. Output: “How a 40-agent backlog audit actually worked.” This is a process-story demo, and the situation brief says the process story is the safest and most ready inbound story. fileciteturn22file19

6. **Before/after Beads quality audit**

Input: pre-audit Beads snapshot. Polylogue extracts null acceptance criteria, orphaned beads, missing dependency edges, stale GitHub refs, and under-specified frontier work. Output: before/after dashboard: acceptance criteria filled, new beads created, deps added, cycles avoided, held decisions. This turns the Beads restructuring into a concrete “agentic project management substrate” demo.

7. **Stale docs versus code reality check**

Given a stale architecture doc and live code/schema, Polylogue finds contradictions and produces a PR-ready patch plan. The uploaded swarm/chat excerpt contains exactly this pattern: architecture-spine schema-versioning contradicted additive durable migrations and execution-plan was stale. Output: stale-doc report with code/doc/bead refs and recommended patches. fileciteturn22file15

8. **Critical-path selector**

Input: the whole Beads graph. Ask: “What should I work on next?” Polylogue produces a ranked frontier: ready, blocked, stale, high-leverage, proof-campaign relevant, and anti-recommendations. Output: a short decision memo, not a giant list. This is grounded in the audit’s conclusion that the real wave-1 collapsed to a small frontier like `cfk`, `3tl.11`, `3tl.4`, `1xc.*`, `pj8`, and a few 4smp entries. fileciteturn21file15

9. **Notes-sidecar trap detector**

Demo a specific Beads failure mode: many beads looked under-specified because important content lived in the notes sidecar rather than design/acceptance fields. Polylogue finds these, lifts/formalizes them, and prevents agents from inventing duplicate specs. Output: “hidden spec recovery” report plus patch commands.

10. **GitHub external-ref reconciliation**

Beads are authoritative; GitHub issues are external refs, not mirrors. Demo: Polylogue compares Beads and GitHub issue state, identifies done issues still open on GitHub, stale refs, issue scopes folded into larger beads, and non-mirror relationships. Output: operator checklist, no automatic GH mutation. This is grounded in the Beads workflow memory in the compaction excerpt. fileciteturn22file2

## Demos centered on the live query/composer vision

11. **Live set-algebra explainer**

A TUI or recorded terminal demo: compose `A intersect B`, see `|A|`, `|B|`, and `|A∩B|` update before commit, then export the result. The C10 design explicitly frames live set sizes as the payoff of set-algebra preview because users otherwise guess wrong and discover empty results too late. fileciteturn22file0

12. **Projection preview: selection is not enough**

Show the same query rendered as `summary`, `dialogue`, `tool-failures-only`, `commit-card`, and `evidence-pack`. The demo claim: Polylogue is not just finding sessions; it is composing evidence. C10’s commit model already says terminal stages preview their projection, and export reruns the same render spec so preview and artifact match. fileciteturn22file0

13. **“Find touches:ids.py” composer walkthrough**

Use C10’s concrete example. User types `find touches:ids.py |`, stage rail shows the upstream cardinality, completion suggests `group by`, `sort`, `limit`, `intersect`, `union`, `except`, `read`, and preview shows the current relation before the next stage is chosen. Output: a short screen recording showing query literacy emerging from the UI. fileciteturn22file11

14. **Query recall becomes macro**

Run a query, commit it, then reverse-search it with `Ctrl-R`, preview it, name it, and use it as `@macro` in another set expression. This grounds your “query objects” idea in the existing C10 design, which says committed runs write recall entries with query text, resolved spec, result fingerprint, and timestamp, and named recall entries become macros. fileciteturn22file1

15. **Value completion over the real archive**

Type `origin:cod...`, `model:cla...`, `tool:rg...`, `tag:...`, and show values plus counts from the live archive. C10 calls this the honest gap: current completions cover structure, but field-value completion needs live archive-backed values. fileciteturn21file6

16. **Safe destructive action**

A deliberately theatrical demo: query a set, type `| delete` or `| mark`, and Polylogue refuses to do anything until it shows affected-row count and asks for confirmation. This demonstrates the algebra/action model and safety posture at once. C10 explicitly says preview never executes destructive terminals and commit gates them on preview-backed confirmation. fileciteturn22file0

17. **Explain-at-point-of-use**

User types an ugly query. Polylogue shows parse tree, grain, retrieval lane, pipeline stages, projection, exactness/capped count, and why the current preview is stale or sampled. Output: query debugging as a teaching surface. This is a better demo than generic “autocomplete,” because it shows the archive being inspectable.

18. **Daemon-fast CLI versus cold CLI**

Record the same query run cold and then through the daemon-backed thin client. But do not make it a benchmark-only demo. Make the claim: because the warm daemon makes preview/completion possible, the CLI becomes an interactive instrument. A3 says the composer/live-preview UX only exists honestly with the warm daemon, while daemonless remains break-glass/substrate-direct. fileciteturn22file5

## Demos centered on annotations/assertions

19. **External annotation loop**

Prompt an agent: “Label these 200 delegation prompts for directive intensity, output-contract strictness, and scope control. Evidence refs required.” Import JSONL as assertion/judgment candidates. Then query the annotations. Output: report generated from external labels, not manual spreadsheet fiddling.

20. **Assertion provenance demo**

Take one judgment, such as “this assistant ignored a failing test,” and expand it: target message, evidence refs, tool result, confidence, author/model, schema, batch, status. This demonstrates why assertions are better than CLAUDE.md or flat memories. The raw log explicitly notes that assertion entries could be timestamped, carry expiry, have navigable origin refs, versioning, and hierarchical expansion refs. fileciteturn22file8

21. **Human-vs-agent annotation disagreement**

Two models label the same cohort of messages for “claim unsupported,” “scope drift,” or “overconfident closeout.” Polylogue shows agreement, disagreements, and specimen rows. Output: construct-validity artifact, not just labels.

22. **Pathology atlas**

Create an annotation schema for agent failure modes: ignored error, false completion, excessive scope, repeated dead-end, under-specified plan, stale doc reliance, unsafe shell quoting, wrong archive root. Run it over a sample and produce an atlas with examples and counts.

23. **Correction lifecycle**

An agent imports candidate assertions. Human accepts/rejects a few. Polylogue then changes what gets injected into future context packs. Output: one loop from observation → candidate memory → accepted assertion → context behavior.

24. **Finding package**

Select a cohort, import annotations, generate a report, and include every dependency: query run refs, snapshot cohort, annotation batch, evidence pack, render artifact. This is the “analysis itself as object” demo.

## Demos centered on compaction, memory, and context

25. **Flat memory dump versus compiled context**

Use the Claude excerpt exactly. Baseline: 19 global memories dumped after compaction. Polylogue: selects 6 relevant memories for the next task, omits 13 with reasons, includes expansion refs, stale/conflict flags, and task-specific hazards. Output: side-by-side context pack. fileciteturn22file2

26. **Post-compaction failure analysis**

Find sessions where compaction happened, then inspect the next 20 messages/actions. Did the agent ask orientation questions? Re-run commands already known? Miss a memory? Query wrong archive? Output: “what compaction loses” report.

27. **Agent reboot with refs, not pasted context**

A demo inspired by your raw-log idea: instead of huge compaction prose, the agent starts a new session with a compact recap plus refs to expand tool outputs, files, reports, prior messages, and query results. The raw log already sketches this: agents could reset/reboot sessions with prose intact, tool outputs stripped or replaced by refs, and richer context management around session starts. fileciteturn22file6

28. **Context pack diff**

Show what changed between the context given to Agent A and Agent B: new assertions, omitted stale docs, added bead, removed irrelevant memory, branch/daemon warning added. Output: context is no longer invisible magic; it is inspectable state.

29. **Memory utility analytics**

Across sessions, ask: which injected memories were actually used, which were ignored, which warnings prevented mistakes, which are stale noise? Output: delete/supersede recommendations for memories.

30. **CLAUDE.md replacement pressure test**

Use the recent CLAUDE.md compaction session: the file was reduced to ~4K tokens from a ~50K transclusion chain, with AGENTS.md symlinked to it. Demo: Polylogue compiles the truly relevant slices dynamically instead of relying on one static master file. fileciteturn22file3

## Demos centered on work reconstruction and repo evidence

31. **Session-to-commit reconstruction**

Given a commit hash, Polylogue finds the session(s) that produced it, the tool calls that edited files, tests run, verifier output, PR text, and follow-up fixes. Output: “why this commit exists” card.

32. **Commit-to-session archaeology**

Reverse of the above: start from a session, reconstruct which commits/PRs/branches came out of it. The Claude excerpt’s branch/PR cleanup is perfect source material: entangled commit, cherry-pick, force-with-lease, CI verification, final merged commits. fileciteturn22file3

33. **Replay plan, not replay promise**

For a coding-agent session, Polylogue emits a “reproduction plan”: checkout commit X, inspect files Y, rerun commands Z, compare outputs. It does not claim deterministic replay unless evidence supports it. Output: honest work-trace bundle.

34. **Tool-call timeline**

Render a session as: user intent → assistant plan → shell commands → file writes → tests → errors → corrections → commit. This is a much more useful “transcript” for coding work than chat messages.

35. **CI failure root-cause lens**

Select sessions mentioning a failing CI check. Polylogue groups by error class, command, file, responsible commit, and whether the agent fixed or ignored it. Output: top failure modes in agent-built PRs.

36. **“This code path is haunted” report**

Given a file path, Polylogue finds every session, message, tool call, commit, failed test, assertion, and bead involving it. Output: maintenance archaeology for one file.

37. **Branch-local daemon stale-code trap**

Use the compaction memory about the branch-local devloop daemon serving stale code after branch switches. Demo: Polylogue identifies sessions where daemon status/branch state made results suspect, then emits a warning/context pack for the next agent. fileciteturn22file2

38. **Live archive root pitfall detector**

Another concrete memory-derived demo: catch commands that would query `/tmp/polylogue-archive` instead of the live archive. Output: “silent empty archive” prevention. It is small, but highly legible because it prevents a real repeated operator error.

## Demos centered on cost, usage, and provider behavior

39. **Codex cached-token correction**

Before: cost report double-counts Codex cached tokens and inflates costs. After: Polylogue reports disjoint lanes and shows API-equivalent versus subscription-credit views. Output: cost-honesty report with before/after numbers.

40. **Provider/task routing economics**

For multi-agent work, show which model families were assigned which tasks, cost per task type, retries, failures, and output usefulness. This pairs well with the Fable/subagent demo.

41. **Semantic search earned its cost**

Compare lexical, semantic, and hybrid retrieval on a real query set. Show cases where semantic found genuinely useful sessions and cases where it did not. Output: “keep/kill/tune embeddings” decision memo.

42. **Preview budget honesty**

Use the composer or CLI to show exact, estimated, capped, and stale counts. Output: a small demo that Polylogue refuses to silently fabricate certainty. C10’s preview design explicitly labels capped/sampled previews and avoids silent truncation. fileciteturn22file0

43. **Slow demo regeneration autopsy**

Take the claim-vs-evidence regeneration slowdown memory: broad reruns hid an OR/COALESCE predicate and monolithic pairing query; stage timing isolated the bottleneck and led to indexed disjoint failure legs plus chunked pairing. Demo: Polylogue turns a “slow demo” into a structured performance investigation. fileciteturn22file2

44. **Daemon startup and warming honesty**

Record a cold daemon start. Show `ACCEPTING`, `WARMING`, `READY`, stale-available, and composer preview disabled until warm. This demonstrates user trust: no frozen CLI, no silent fallback. A4’s lifecycle design explicitly distinguishes accepting connections from ready/warm reads. fileciteturn22file17

## Demos centered on browser capture and external agents

45. **Browser-captured cloud research delegation**

The raw log suggests browser-capture posting could let a local agent delegate research to cloud web UIs, observe ongoing reasoning, support projects/attachments, and reduce dogfooding friction. Demo version: don’t start with full posting. Start with “local agent sees a cloud research thread as evidence, reconstructs it, and imports the answer with refs.” fileciteturn22file6

46. **WebUI continuation recovery**

Given a browser-captured ChatGPT/Claude/Gemini web thread, Polylogue reconstructs context and emits a prompt for a new web thread to continue it, with source refs and omitted-material index.

47. **Cloud/local boundary report**

Show what a cloud agent can safely certify versus what only the local daemon/operator can certify. This is grounded in the locality doctrine from the Beads audit: cloud agents can patch source/docs/fixtures, but cannot certify deployed local truth. Output: closeout checklist.

48. **Attachment truth demo**

If browser capture says attachments exist, Polylogue shows whether bytes exist, hashes are real/synthetic, whether re-acquisition is possible, and which claims should be avoided. Output: honesty card for an attachment-heavy session.

49. **Multi-instance browser-capture safety**

Use the raw-log concern about multiple browser-capture instances and DOM-degraded coalescing. Demo: simulate duplicate/degraded captures and show Polylogue coalesces or warns rather than double-counting. fileciteturn22file9

## Demos centered on local-first / personal substrate, probably internal first

50. **What was I doing at 23:10?**

Polylogue + adjacent captured sources reconstruct the active AI sessions, terminal commands, browser tabs, raw-log notes, and work item around a timestamp. Output: one “activity reconstruction” page. This touches Sinex/Lynchpin territory, so make it an internal demo unless data is sanitized.

51. **Raw-log to Beads extraction**

Use the raw log as messy intent. Agent extracts candidate work items, deduplicates them against existing Beads, proposes new beads only for genuinely missing items, and cites raw-log timestamps. Output: “thought stream → backlog” conversion. The raw log contains many Polylogue-relevant ideas, including browser-capture posting, agent reboot/compaction, assertions, context injection, alternates, and demo hooks. fileciteturn22file6 fileciteturn22file8 fileciteturn22file9

52. **Tab/provenance capture**

A small demo from the raw-log theme: instead of opening infinite tabs, capture links with provenance, intent, source page, and optional note. Polylogue later queries “why did I save this?” Output: browsing-state recovery.

53. **Terminal/asciinema session summarizer**

Given terminal recordings and AI sessions, Polylogue produces a command diary: what commands were run, what failed, what changed, what should be remembered. Output: self-observability artifact.

54. **Voice/raw note evidence pack**

Internal demo: raw notes or voice transcripts are not “memory”; they are evidence. An agent extracts assertions with confidence, expiry, and evidence refs. This demonstrates the assertion model without making sensitive content public.

55. **Personal test set for models**

Use your own archive as a benchmark: which model is better at reconstructing a messy dev session, finding the decisive tool failure, or extracting useful Beads? Output: model-eval report over your real corpus.

## Demos centered on content variants and render algebra

56. **Translation as content variant, not evidence mutation**

Pick a bilingual/multilingual session. Add translated variants at message/block level. Render original, translation, and side-by-side, clearly indicating variant substitution. The raw log explicitly suggests alternates attached to messages/blocks, with translation as the motivating case but broader uses possible. fileciteturn22file9

57. **Tool-output folding**

Take a huge coding session. Render it three ways: full transcript, authored dialogue only, and evidence pack with tool outputs folded but expandable by ref. Output: same evidence, different projections.

58. **Long-session budget challenge**

Force a report over a session too large for the context window. Polylogue must produce a bounded, honest context pack with omissions and expansion refs, not a fake complete summary. The situation brief says an existing context-pack demo already proves honest truncation; this turns it into a task-completion demo by giving it to an agent. fileciteturn21file11

59. **Specimen-gallery renderer**

Take any annotation batch, such as Fable delegation labels or claim-versus-evidence failures, and render a clean public “gallery” with short examples, counts, caveats, and source refs. This is a generic render layout, not a Fable-specific feature.

60. **Evidence cockpit**

For a report claim, click into a web/workbench page showing query run, cohort, annotations, source messages, tool calls, raw artifacts, and render artifact. This is the “why should I believe this?” demo.

## What these demos imply Polylogue should build

The demos mostly converge on the same missing primitives. Not Fable-specific, not scratchpad-specific.

Polylogue needs **query runs** as first-class objects: every query returns an id, lowered spec, result grain, exactness, degraded state, timing, and result fingerprint. C10 already proposes recall entries with query text, resolved spec, result fingerprint, and timestamp; that should grow into query-run/result-relation objects. fileciteturn22file1

It needs **cohorts**: named dynamic or snapshot sets of sessions/messages/actions/delegations/assertions/artifacts. These make demos reproducible: “the 47 examples in report v1” is a snapshot cohort, not a vague search.

It needs **annotation batches** over assertions: external agents label messages/sessions/delegations/query results, import JSONL, and Polylogue makes those judgments queryable with schema, author, confidence, evidence refs, and status. The raw-log assertion idea already points to timestamped, expiring, ref-backed, versioned memory/assertion entries. fileciteturn22file8

It needs **artifact/work-trace linking**: sessions, actions, files, commits, PRs, reports, evidence packs, and generated artifacts linked by produced/consumed/derived_from edges. This is what makes replay plans, commit archaeology, and agent-swarm autopsies work.

It needs **analysis runs**: not just YAML recipes, not just database rows. A recipe/prompt describes intended procedure; the analysis run records what actually happened: query runs, cohorts, annotation batches, evidence packs, reports, and decisions.

It needs **context compile runs**: every context pack has selected memories, omitted memories, reasons, refs, freshness, and downstream outcome. This directly beats flat `bd prime` memory dumps after compaction.

## My ranking

The first public demo should be either **claim-versus-evidence** or **cut-session recovery**. The first is the best public finding. The second is the best agent-value proof. The third, slightly more playful but still serious, is **Fable/subagent-rhetoric**.

The best internal dogfood demo is **compaction memory replacement**, because the Claude excerpt gives you a perfect before/after: flat persistent memories versus a compiled, cited, task-scoped context pack. The best substrate-shaping demo is **external annotation loop**, because once that works, almost every other analysis becomes scalable instead of fiddly.
